Decision to Hold the Second General Meeting Today

(Nanjing) The Presidium of the General Assembly held a brief meeting at around 8 a.m. on the 15th. After the first general meeting adjourned at 11 a.m., they met again to discuss the proposals after the review by the Review Committee. All the chairmen participated, and the meeting adjourned at around 12 p.m. It was decided to hold the second general meeting on the morning of the 16th to discuss the proposals after review by the Review Committee, and Zhang Ji was appointed as chairman. In addition, the Party Affairs, Political, Economic, Educational, and Military Group Review Committees all held meetings at 3 p.m. on the 15th and adjourned at around 6 p.m. The results of the review will all be made into reports and submitted to the General Assembly for discussion. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

Guangdong and Guangxi Representatives Arrive in Nanjing One After Another

(Nanjing) A group of more than 60 representatives from Guangdong and Guangxi provinces and cities, the Special Party Headquarters of the two Guangdong armies, and overseas, arrived in Shanghai on the morning of the 15th. Except for the representatives from Guangxi and the army, who were scheduled to take the night train to Nanjing on the 15th, the remaining 41 people took a train from Shanghai at around 1 p.m. and arrived in Nanjing at 7:50 p.m. Ma Chaojun, Liang Hancao, Liu Jiwen, Huang Jilu, and representatives from the Central Party Headquarters all went to the station to welcome them. After the representatives got off the train, they went to the reception center to rest. The representatives who arrived in Nanjing this time were Lu Yougang, Huo Guanghe, Cheng Yueen, Zhou Tang, Xu Yiheng, Lin Songfu, Hu Wencan from Guangzhou City; Peng Zhuoren, Lu Kuangwen, Li Heling, Fu Heqiong, Zheng Lizhen, Wu Zifang, Chen Tongchang, Fang Ruilin, Yu Zuming, Liang Yanming from Guangdong Province; Mei Fangting, Li Qiongsheng, He Shuru, Zhang Weimin, Wu Huafang, Huang Zhichao, Wang Wensheng, Xu Weixiong, Li Wugong, Wu Chi寰, Lan Yaoguang, Li Kexuan, Li Shusheng, He Pingwu, Han Xinchuan, Yao Yuhui, Jiang Biao, Yu Rong, Chen Yuting, Cai Jianbai, Huang Haishan, Zhang Dingming, Li Rulin, Zhao Delan from overseas Party headquarters. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

He Jian Reports on the Military Situation of Suppressing Bandits in Western Hunan

(Nanjing) He Jian presented a report to the Fifth National Congress on the general situation of the suppression in Western Hunan, with the content divided into three parts: military affairs, politics, and Party affairs. The text is more than 200,000 words long. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Li Zongren Did Not Fly to Nanjing Yesterday

(Hong Kong) Li Zongren did not fly to Guangdong on the 15th due to bad weather and changed the flight to Guangdong and then to Nanjing on the 16th. One said that the central plane would fly directly to Nanning to pick up Li and fly directly to Nanjing. Lin Yizhong recovered from his illness and returned to the Civil Affairs Department on the 15th to work, but his spirits had not yet recovered. He decided to stop going to Nanjing, and Chen Jitang planned to send Yu Hanmou as a representative to fly to Nanjing instead. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Military and Political Minister He Yingqin Discusses; The Central Government's Policy Towards Japan Remains Unchanged; Anyone with a Calm Mind and Abundant Common Sense Will Not Be Fooled by Rumormongers

(Nanjing) Because of the various rumors that have occurred in Shanghai recently, which have had a considerable impact on people's hearts and security, the reporter specially visited Military and Political Minister He Yingqin. Minister He personally received the reporter and said in a very relaxed manner: "Shanghai is a place where various parties are mixed, and rumors are easy to arise. Moreover, due to the instigation of speculators, things are often fabricated out of thin air, and rumors are used as their tools, regardless of the interests of the country and society. The Central Government's diplomacy towards Japan is based on a spirit of goodwill in order to improve all relations between the two countries. This policy has never changed. The rumors in Shanghai are completely untrue. Anyone with a calm mind and abundant common sense will not be fooled by the rumormongers." (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

Japanese Troops Arrive in Yushu One After Another

(Tianjin) The Japanese troops who arrived at Shanhaiguan on the 15th all got off the train and lived in civilian houses in the South Gate. They lived in groups of three or four in each room, and after three or four days, they would merge into one room to free up empty rooms for the military to use. Early on the 15th, five more trains of soldiers arrived in Yushu, but the soldiers had not yet gotten off the train. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

(Beiping) According to reliable sources, Japanese troops are currently gathering in Shanhaiguan. A Japanese armored vehicle and a train of cavalry arrived in Shanhaiguan yesterday. The Japanese troops newly transferred from Jinzhou to Shanhaiguan number approximately 2,500. (Reuters dispatch from the 15th)

Japanese Warships Openly Berth in Qingdao

(Qingdao) The commander of the Japanese 13th Destroyer Squadron, Nishigang Mototai, led his three subordinate warships, Wu Takeuchi, Wakatake, and Saemba, from Lushun to Qingdao at 8 a.m. on the 15th and berthed in the front sea. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

President Wang's Injury is Healing Day by Day

(Nanjing) President Wang's injury is healing day by day. On the 15th, he followed his doctor's advice and did not meet with many guests. People from Qinghai, Sichuan, and Gansu all sent telegrams of condolence. In addition, the Central Hospital released a medical report on the 15th, stating that President Wang's temperature was 36.9 degrees Celsius at 4 p.m., his pulse was 84, and his respiration was 17. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

(Nanjing) American Ambassador to China Johnson went to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the afternoon of the 15th to meet with Vice Minister Tang to inquire about President Wang's injury. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Okamura Returns to Japan for a Brief Discussion

Moji Lieutenant General Okamura of the Army Ministry returned to Moji on the 15th and told reporters that he had communicated with the resident officials in Shanghai and reached a completely consistent result. After the Shanghai meeting, he went to South China to inspect various places and crossed to Taiwan from Xiamen. In Guangxi, he met with Li Zongren, Bai Chongxi, and others to exchange opinions. (Japan United News dispatch from the 15th)

Okada Visits Saionji

Shizuoka Prime Minister Okada visited Prince Saionji at Zuogyosō in Okitsu on his way back from the great exercise. They talked for more than an hour, reporting on the various problems that had occurred since the visit in early May, and revealing his beliefs and determination regarding the pressing problems at present. The main points are as follows: Although the budget for the next year was compiled according to the policy of Finance Minister Takahashi to gradually reduce public debt, in view of the current international situation, the budget that fully recognizes national defense first must be included. On the one hand, the budget related to rural areas cannot be ignored, so it was decided to allocate funds appropriately to compile it. Japan has decided to happily participate in the Disarmament Conference and appointed full powers. However, Japan will ultimately deal with the conference in accordance with its established policy, and the future does not seem optimistic. The government plans to hold the election smoothly after the next session of Parliament ends without incident, but depending on the attitude of the Seiyukai, dissolution is not ruled out. (Telecommunication dispatch from the 15th)

Three Japanese Warships Arrive in the Qinhuangdao Area

(Beiping) Three Japanese warships arrived at the most frequently folded part of the Qinhuangdao area. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Amemiya Visits Tang Youren

(Nanjing) Amemiya, the military attaché of the Japanese Embassy, visited Vice Minister Tang at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the morning of the 15th to discuss matters. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Page 4

Qin Dechun Receives the Press; Says That No Boxing Incident Occurred in North China; Will Strictly Suppress Unscrupulous Merchants Disrupting the Market

(Beiping) Qin Dechun received the press this afternoon and released a written statement and answers to questions. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

(Beiping) Qin Dechun received the press at 4 p.m. on the 15th and said that Beiping is a world-renowned city and that in this difficult situation, it is only possible to cooperate with the people on the principle of good neighborliness and internal stability to seek the development of the city. He hoped that the press would understand the difficulties and speak carefully so as not to make the people feel uneasy. He then answered reporters' questions: (1) The overall direction of Sino-Japanese diplomacy is probably being negotiated between the central departments of both sides. As for local issues, no new incidents have occurred in North China recently. Matsui's visit to Beiping is for sightseeing and inspection. (2) Song Zheyuan is very concerned about the implementation of currency regulations. The government has now ordered the establishment of a Tianjin Preparatory Management Branch, and in addition to the personnel already sent by the government, it seems that more honest and powerful local gentry and merchants should participate together to show credibility. Although Beiping is handled by the Tianjin Branch, cash is stored locally to reassure the people, and the market can be stabilized. If unscrupulous merchants and rioters take the opportunity to profiteer and arbitrarily raise prices, they will be severely suppressed. (3) The municipal government's personnel all adopt the principle of talent. At present, the various bureaus and offices are still working as usual, and there are no changes. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

(Beiping) Qin Dechun is holding a banquet at his residence tomorrow noon to bid farewell to Sugito, the councilor of the Japanese Embassy, who has been transferred back to his country, and has invited the main personnel of the embassy to accompany him. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Song Zheyuan Telegraphs Nanjing to Report; Security in Beiping and Tianjin is Not in Danger

(Nanjing) Song Zheyuan, the commander of the Beiping and Tianjin garrisons, telegraphed Nanjing on the 15th to report that the security in Beiping and Tianjin is being closely guarded by the military and police, and there is absolutely no danger. The local area is safe and stable. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

(Tianjin) Liu Yushu said that the Tianjin defense has been carefully prepared, rumors are gradually dying down, and preparations are underway to recruit temporary police. (Special dispatch from the 10th)

(Nanjing) Xiong Bin told people on the 15th that when he left Beiping, the situation in Beiping and Tianjin was peaceful, and the rumors outside were not credible. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Yu Hanmou Returns to Guangzhou

(Hong Kong) Yu Hanmou returned to the province from Dayu by car on the morning of the 15th and will arrive at 5 a.m. on the 16th. A certain representative Deng from Yunnan-Guizhou, accompanied by Dan Maoxin, arrived in Guangzhou on the 14th to meet with Chen Jitang. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

New Magistrate of Xianghe Takes Office; Order in the City Maintained by Security Team

(Beiping) The new magistrate of Xianghe, Liang Jishu, arrived in the county at noon on the 14th and took office on the morning of the 15th. Order in the city is completely maintained by the security team. Tiancun, the liaison officer sent by the Luan-Yu Special Office, and Qu Shihe, the deputy commander of the 5th Security Brigade, returned to Tangshan on the evening of the 14th to report. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

(Beiping) Since Liang Jishu, the new magistrate of Xianghe, arrived in the county and started anew, the 7th Company of Zhang Qingyu's 1st Brigade of the Security Team has entered the city to garrison. Order in the county is gradually recovering. However, due to the great constraints from all sides after the incident, the original situation cannot be restored for a while. Regarding post-war matters, the Hebei Provincial Government has formulated a plan and ordered Magistrate Liang to discuss and maintain measures with fair local gentry. The Bao Wei Tuan [local militia], which has always been under the command of Wu Yiting, is still secretly controlled by Wu and others. Although the county government has been handed over by the rebel people, the actual implementation of local government affairs is still greatly constrained. Tiancun and the Japanese military police who went to Xianghe to assist in the takeover of the county government have recently left Xianghe and returned to Beiping. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

(Tianjin) The Xianghe incident has been completely resolved. Wu Zhenyi and An Houzhai, the leaders of the rioters, sneaked into Tianjin with a certain foreign ronin on the night of the 14th and hid in a certain foreign concession. The order in Xianghe County has been completely restored. The new magistrate, Liang Jishu, has taken over, and all the section chiefs and others appointed by the pseudo-magistrate have fled. Chen Qingyun, a counselor sent by the Provincial Government, went to Baoding on the 14th to investigate and assist Magistrate Liang in handling post-war matters. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

(Tianjin) Baoding telephone: Li Yintang, the magistrate of Qingyun County, telegraphed the province that on the 10th, two foreign ronin and the treacherous people Chen Xiufu arrived in the county from Tianjin. Under the guise of investigation, they planned to travel all over the countryside to mobilize. The magistrate took early precautions and ordered the police to monitor Chen and detained the two ronin. On the 13th, the Provincial Government ordered Ge Yuquan's battalion of the 32nd Army stationed nearby to send two companies of troops to suppress them and escort the two ronin to Tianjin and send them to the Japanese Consulate General. The local area has now been pacified. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Hebei Province Implements Winter Defense; Bandits Lurking in the Suburbs of Baoding; Renpu Not Peaceful in the Huai-Mi Area

(Tianjin) Baoding telephone: Bandits lurking in the suburbs of Baoding. Shang Zhen convened Li Xingcun, the director of the Security Office, and Li Peiji, the director of the Civil Affairs Department, on the 15th to discuss ways to suppress them and issued an order to the whole province, starting from the 15th, to implement winter defense for four months until March 15th of the coming year. The city gates of Baoding are closed every night at 9 p.m. and opened at 6 a.m. the next morning. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

(Tianjin) More than 300 bandits raided Da Shuiyu and Hefengkou in Huairou and Miyun on the 13th, with very complete firearms. The 2nd Company of the Huairou Garrison Security Team fought against them, and the bandits fled to Chachang Village, 15 li west of Huairou, and kidnapped more than 40 men and women and fled to Wangjiayu in Changping. The Security Team and the militia have been sent to the Sanduhe and Shankou areas near Huairou to block them. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

(Beiping) Huairou telephone: More than 300 bandits from Hefengkou raided Wangjiayu Village after fleeing from Chawu Village in Changping yesterday and then fled back to Honglu Mountain in Huairou this afternoon. The magistrate is afraid that the bandits will flee south and ordered the east and west gates to be closed tightly this morning, and the south gate to be half-open, guarded by the police, and strictly inspect the pedestrians. The residents near the county town are very panicked. People from Gaoliying said that Chawu Village in Changping suffered heavy losses after being looted by bandits on the 14th, and the villagers fled to Gaoliying. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

(Beiping) More than 200 bandits suddenly appeared in the Da Shuiyu and Hefengkou area on the border of Miyun and Huairou. Two companies of the Security Team were dispatched by the Ji-Mi District the night before to encircle and suppress them. The bandits fled into Changping County yesterday morning, and the Security Team of Feng Shoupeng's department in the county has been ordered to dispatch to suppress them. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Measures for Exchanging Legal Tender and Regulations for Silver Usage in Silver Products

The Ministry of Finance announced yesterday and notified all provinces and cities.

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance announced on the 15th the "Measures for Exchanging Legal Tender" and the "Regulations for Silver Usage in Silver Products," which have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for record and notified to all provinces and cities. The original text is as follows:

Article 1 of the Measures for Exchanging Legal Tender: All silver firms, shops, other public organizations, or individuals in various regions who possess silver coins, silver bars, raw silver, silver ingots, silver blocks, and other silver items shall, starting from November 4th of the 24th year of the Republic of China, exchange them for legal tender at nearby exchange institutions within three months. However, the following items are not subject to this restriction: (1) Silver items used as raw materials for industrial arts or other essential purposes, with government permission according to the regulations for silver usage in silver products; (2) Ancient coins, rare coins, or silver antiques related to culture; (3) Silver utensils and decorations manufactured and stored before the announcement of these measures.

Article 2: The institutions for exchanging legal tender are as follows: (1) The Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, along with their branches or agencies; (2) Banks, money houses, pawnshops, postal offices, railway bureaus, shipping companies, telegraph offices, and other public institutions or public organizations entrusted by the three banks; (3) National and local tax collection agencies in various locations; (4) County governments.

Article 3: All silver items other than common silver coins and silver bars shall be exchanged for legal tender based on their fineness and estimated value.

Article 4: In areas where legal tender is not circulated, those who possess silver coins, silver bars, raw silver, silver ingots, silver blocks, or other silver items shall deliver them to the institutions listed in items (2), (3), and (4) of Article 2 and request them to exchange them for legal tender on their behalf.

Article 5: The silver coins, silver bars, raw silver, silver ingots, silver blocks, or other silver items collected by the institutions listed in items (2), (3), and (4) of Article 2 shall be immediately delivered to the nearby Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications for exchange into legal tender. Those who conceal them or use them for other purposes shall be prosecuted for embezzlement.

Article 6: During the exchange period, anyone who takes advantage of the holders of silver coins, silver bars, raw silver, silver ingots, silver blocks, or other silver items and extorts them shall be prosecuted for fraud.

Article 7: The exchange rate between common silver coins and legal tender shall not have any price difference. Violators shall have their legal tender and silver coins confiscated separately or together, depending on the circumstances. Those who attempt to evade or leak by collecting and exchanging silver coins or silver items at high prices shall be dealt with in accordance with Articles 2 and 5 of the Provisional Regulations for Punishing Acts Endangering the National Currency.

Article 8: These measures shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Article 1 of the Regulations for Silver Usage in Silver Products: The use of silver in silver products shall be managed in accordance with these regulations.

Article 2: From the date of promulgation of these regulations, the manufacture of silver utensils and silver ornaments shall use chemical silver as raw material. If pure silver must be mixed in, the amount of pure silver contained shall not exceed 30 percent.

Article 3: Silver utensils and silver ornaments manufactured before the promulgation of these regulations may be sold as before until they are sold out. Silver materials that have not been manufactured into finished products shall not be privately sold.

Article 4: Within one month from the date of promulgation of these regulations, manufacturers of silver products shall report the names and quantities of the silver utensils and silver ornaments they have manufactured, as well as the amount of pure silver they contain and the quantity of silver materials they currently possess, to the local trade association or chamber of commerce, which shall forward the report to the local or nearby Central Bank or other agency for verification and then forward it to the Ministry of Finance. In areas where there is no Central Bank, the report shall be forwarded to the Bank of China or the Bank of Communications or their agencies for verification and then forwarded to the Ministry of Finance.

Article 5: Silver product manufacturers who need silver materials shall purchase them from the Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, or designated agencies, but they shall provide a guarantee from the local trade association or chamber of commerce stating that the silver will not be used for other purposes, and they shall bear joint and several liability.

Article 6: The maximum amount of silver materials that silver product manufacturers can purchase shall be 30 percent of the average quantity of silver utensils and silver ornaments sold by the manufacturer in the three years before the promulgation of these regulations. If the manufacturer has not been in operation for three years, the amount shall be 30 percent of the quantity sold in the previous year.

Article 7: Silver product manufacturers shall report the total amount of pure silver contained in the silver utensils and silver ornaments sold every six months to the local trade association or chamber of commerce, which shall forward the report to the Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, or the agency that issued the silver materials for verification and then forward it to the Ministry of Finance.

Article 8: When silver product manufacturers cease operations, they shall exchange the silver utensils, silver ornaments, and silver materials in their possession for legal tender based on the pure silver content at the Central Bank of China or the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications.

Article 9: Silver product manufacturers who violate the provisions of these regulations shall be ordered to suspend operations. Those who evade or attempt to evade shall be convicted in accordance with Articles 2 and 5 of the Provisional Regulations for Punishing Acts Endangering the National Currency.

Article 10: The matters listed in Articles 2 to 8 of these regulations shall be inspected by personnel dispatched by the bank that issued the silver materials at any time. If any of the circumstances listed in Article 9 are found, they shall be reported to the local administrative or judicial authorities for handling.

Article 11: The use of silver for artistic, pharmaceutical, and other industrial purposes shall be subject to the provisions of these regulations. However, those who have obtained special permission from the Ministry of Finance shall not be subject to the 30 percent limit in Articles 2 and 6.

Article 12: These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 15th)

Shanxi Province Seals Existing Silver and Starts Organizing a Legal Tender Exchange Office

(Taiyuan) This morning, the officials of the Suiyuan Provincial Government summoned more than 20 chairmen and representatives of chambers of commerce from various counties in the province to the government office to discuss the verification of the actual amount of existing silver and issued banknotes in various banks, as well as the organization of a legal tender exchange office, and to negotiate matters such as chambers of commerce in various counties pleading with the provincial bank for loans. It was decided to seal them up starting tomorrow. Afterwards, the representatives will inspect them once a month. The members of the legal tender exchange office have been appointed and are starting to organize. The provincial government has agreed to find a way to provide loans to the chambers of commerce in various counties, and the amount is still under negotiation. Current Commentary

Minister of Military Affairs He Yingqin Dispels Rumors

— Yi

Since the incident of the murder of Japanese Navy Marine Corps soldier Nakayama Hideo, rumors have been rife in Shanghai and its surrounding areas. Residents of the 128th War Zone and the Hongkou area have been moving their furniture and luggage to the South Bund Concession one after another. Rental cars have been fully booked. In the past two days, some people were still moving late at night. This floating phenomenon not only causes economic losses to the citizens themselves, but also causes the revival of northern Shanghai to come to a standstill. Even in terms of foreign relations, it is feared that some repercussions will inevitably occur.

It goes without saying that this unconscious state of avoidance is the result of the citizens' belief in unfounded rumors. However, there are two root causes. One is that the nightmare of the Songhu war has not yet been eliminated from the minds of the citizens. The current incident of the murder of a Japanese sailor easily makes the citizens revert to their past state of fear. The second is that recently, just after the promulgation of the new currency policy, important figures from all sides united in sincerity and gathered in the capital to hold the Fifth Plenary Session of the Kuomintang. These two events are major events for the party and the country. Those who are fond of creating disturbances and speculators inevitably take the opportunity to make all kinds of unfounded speculations, which are spread around. And the general public, who have little knowledge, turn fantasy into reality.

Minister of Military Affairs He Yingqin issued a statement yesterday dispelling rumors, saying that the central government's diplomacy with Japan is based on a spirit of friendship in order to seek improvement between the two countries. This policy has never changed. The rumors in Shanghai are completely untrue, etc. At the same time, in addition to ordering the Public Security Bureau to prohibit residents from moving without reason, the Shanghai Municipal Government also issued a statement. It is hoped that citizens will use common sense to judge rumors and observe the situation calmly. At a time when people's hearts are wavering, the sincere expression of the responsible authorities is truly essential. The gloomy atmosphere that has pervaded Shanghai for the past few days should be swept away from now on.

U.S. President Roosevelt's Proclamation Inaugurates Philippine Autonomy, First President Takes Office, Parliament Opens, 19-Gun Salute, Hundreds of Thousands of Spectators

(Washington) President Roosevelt's proclamation on the establishment of the Philippine Autonomous Government has been issued today and will be formally promulgated at the ceremony to be held in Manila tomorrow. The President has also telegraphed the new Philippine President Quezon, asking him to convey his congratulations to the Philippine people. The proclamation was signed by the President himself, with Secretary of State Hull and Army Chief of Staff Craig present at the time. (National Telegram on the 14th)

(Washington) After the President issued the proclamation, he stated, "After the publication of this document, the existing government of the Philippines will cease its functions, and the Philippine Autonomous Government will accept all the powers and responsibilities stipulated in its constitution." The President also sent a telegram to Philippine Governor Murphy, expressing his gratitude for Murphy's loyal service and wishing him success in his new position as the first U.S. High Commissioner to the Philippines, which he will assume tomorrow. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

(Manila) Manila was overjoyed today. About 150,000 to 200,000 people gathered in front of the Legislative Yuan to watch the ceremony. The weather was fine, and airplanes soared in the sky above the Legislative Yuan. The ceremony for the establishment of the new government was as follows: First, the Archbishop blessed the new republic. Then, Philippine Governor Murphy introduced Secretary of War Dern, President Roosevelt's representative, to the public. Dern officially read the U.S. President's congratulatory message to the new President Quezon and the Filipino people. Then, he delivered a speech, comparing the Philippines' request for freedom from the United States with the United States' previous request for freedom from Great Britain. Afterwards, Philippine Governor Murphy officially read the U.S. President's proclamation. The President and Vice President then took office under the supervision of the Chief Justice of the Philippine Supreme Court. A 19-gun salute was fired, and the bells rang nine times. Dern announced that the Republic of the Philippine Islands had been established. Afterwards, President Quezon delivered his inaugural address. After a short break, President Quezon reviewed the troops. Shortly after, President Quezon entered Malacañang Palace. The parliament, with this as the president, was scheduled to open this afternoon, at which time officials will be sworn in. A grand banquet will be held at night to celebrate. (Reuters dispatch on the 15th)

(Manila) The United States promised independence to the Philippine Islands when it first ruled them in 1898. Today, the establishment of the autonomous government is a further step towards this goal. The autonomous government is scheduled for ten years, until July 4, 1946, and then it will be fully independent. This order has been formally promulgated by President Roosevelt and was read out at the ceremony for the establishment of the autonomous government in front of the Philippine Legislative Yuan this morning at 9:00 a.m. Representatives from all sides participated in the grand ceremony, and the Philippine people also gathered in the park at the intersection of Bellgas Road. Initially, President Quezon and Vice President Osmeña were sworn in, indicating the transfer of power. After the swearing-in, a 19-gun salute was fired to celebrate the President's inauguration. Although the Philippines is still under U.S. suzerainty, the salute for the U.S. President's inauguration is also 19 guns, so its honor is in fact no different. Afterwards, Secretary of War Dern, President Roosevelt's personal representative, congratulated the Philippine people and stated that the United States still has a keen interest in the prosperity of the Philippines. Quezon's inaugural speech expressed his loyalty and dedication. At that time, there were about 250,000 people in front of the building, and the Philippine cabinet and Supreme Court justices, etc., were seated in order on the stage, with former Governor Murphy as chairman. After Quezon's speech, high-ranking officials on the stage held the opening ceremony of the parliament at 4:00 p.m. However, the formal meeting will be held at 10:00 a.m. on November 22. There will also be a celebratory dance party in the evening, and there will be important ceremonies every day until the U.S. guests return home on November 20. (National Telegram on the 15th)

(Manila) After President Quezon entered the Presidential Palace, he signed two executive orders and one proclamation. A grand banquet was held at night to entertain guests. Today, all places were very peaceful and there were no disturbances. Because people were coming and going like weaving in Manila, traffic was completely stopped, but everything gradually returned to normal by the evening. (Reuters dispatch on the 15th)

Quezon, the First President of the Philippines

— Bu Ren

On September 10th of this year, the Philippines held its first election for the autonomous government based on the Independence Act. As a result, the leaders of the United Party, Quezon and Osmeña, were elected as President and Vice President respectively. The competitors, old revolutionary General Aguinaldo and Archbishop Aglipay, were defeated. Mr. Quezon took office as the first President with a six-year term yesterday.

Among the heads of state of various countries, Quezon's origins can be said to be the humblest. He is 57 years old this year and was born in the countryside far from Manila. His father was a poor farmer. He received a few years of education in Manila as a child, and later joined the army. During the Philippine Revolution in 1898, Quezon, who was 20 years old, was a junior officer in the revolutionary army commanded by General Aguinaldo.

In 1900, his classmate Osmeña founded the "Daily News" daily newspaper in Cebu, advocating independence. Quezon was a strong supporter. In 1906, Osmeña organized the "Radical Independence Party," and Quezon joined as a youth leader in the party. The following year, the "Radical Independence Party" merged with the "United Nationalist Party" and reorganized into the "Philippine Nationalist Party." Osmeña was crowned as the party leader, and Quezon was only a second-class leader.

Quezon's opportunity to show his talents began in 1912. From that time on, he was sent to the United States as a special commissioner by the Philippine Parliament to socialize with people in the American political arena and enthusiastically made the following propaganda:

"The people of the Philippines will never be happy to be ruled by the United States or any other country. Since being ruled by Spain, the politics of this country has at least been interfered with by others. As such, the people of the Philippines will never be satisfied. Why? Because they have not yet obtained the rights they deserve. Therefore, unless they manage their own affairs completely by themselves, the Filipinos will never get true satisfaction and gratitude."

Quezon's eloquent rhetoric and sincere appearance finally won the favor of President Wilson and the Progressive Party and Democratic Party under his rule. As a result, the Philippine Autonomy Ordinance, known as the "Jones Act," was passed in the U.S. Senate in 1916. From then on, the Philippine independence movement obtained a legal basis, and Quezon's personal political status in the country also soared. In 1917, the Philippine Parliament was changed to a bicameral system. Quezon was elected as the Speaker of the Senate and continued to serve until this year. Osmeña was the Speaker of the House of Representatives. From then on, the Nationalist Party was secretly divided into two factions, one led by Quezon, which later became the "National Democratic Party," and the other led by Osmeña, which later became the "Independent Democratic Party." The two factions fought openly and secretly, each refusing to give in.

In 1933, Osmeña led an independence request group to the United States and won the concrete independence plan called the "Cutting Act." After returning to the Philippines, he hoped to overwhelm Quezon, but was opposed by the Quezon faction. The Quezon faction was deeply dissatisfied because the bill was attached with a clause reserving military bases, and launched an opposition movement, chanting slogans such as "Immediate Independence" and "Complete Independence." The "Cutting Act" was then rejected by the Philippine Parliament.

Quezon, who opposed the Cutting Act, formed another independence request group to realize his claim, and personally led it to the United States to lobby Roosevelt and other political figures to amend it. As a result of his efforts, he finally achieved his wish, and Roosevelt approved the Tydings Amendment. On May 1 of this year, this amendment was passed by the Philippine Parliament. At this point, the Philippine independence movement came to an end.

In fact, the "Tydings Amendment" is not much different from the original "Cutting Act." However, by making such a new trick, Quezon won the support of party members and the public. Quezon's election as President was probably a foregone conclusion. Unfortunately, Osmeña originally did not even have a share in the vice-presidency. Because the highly respected old revolutionary General Aguinaldo came out to run for President, Quezon felt quite afraid, so he had to win over Osmeña to compete. As a result, the two parties repaired their old relationship and formed the United Party, and the leaders of the two parties won the election victory.

The day after the election results were announced, Quezon declared to the public:

"The election results show that the people believe in the platform and personnel of the United Party. In this moment of victory, I am only thinking about the important work that lies before me. I ask God to help me cope with the serious responsibilities that have been placed on my shoulders. I am deeply grateful to the people who respect me so much."

Here, we see a mixture of complacency and humility in Quezon. However, Quezon should not be complacent, nor should he be humble. Whether the Philippines can truly become independent and whether Quezon can become a true leader, the answers to these questions have only just begun yesterday.

Portrait of Mr. Quezon

The new flag of the Philippines Three small stars represent the three main islands The sun symbolizes independence The blue stripe symbolizes virtue and loyalty The red stripe symbolizes courage

British General Election, Government Party's Victory Confirmed, But Labor Party Receives More Votes Than Last Time, MacDonald and Samuel Both Lose

(London) Although the election results have not yet been fully announced, the opposition party has admitted today that the government party has won. As of 3:00 p.m. today, the election results are as follows: the government party has won 340 seats, the opposition party has won 130 seats, and the independent party has won one seat. Former Prime Minister and current Privy Councilor MacDonald has actually lost the election. The government's victory is certain. The bond market and the commodity exchange market are slightly firmer. (National Telegram on the 15th)

(London) Liberal opposition leader Samuel was defeated by Conservative candidate Russell in Darwin, Lancashire, by a majority of 1,157. This is the first surprising event in the general election. (Reuters dispatch on the 15th)

(London) In this general election, although the Labor Party received more votes than in the 1931 general election, the government did not encounter a "rout" everywhere. Political observers speculate based on this morning's report that the government will definitely win a solid victory. Although the Labor Party won in many industrial areas, the government party was still able to maintain its position in many large towns. All twelve seats in Birmingham were still won by Conservative candidates. Liverpool still has eight Conservative seats and three Labor seats. Scottish Secretary of State Collin and Health Minister Wood, who initially feared failure, have been re-elected. Railway workers' leader Thomas won by a large majority in Derby. As of 3:00 a.m. this morning, the government party had won a total of 184 seats, and the opposition party had won a total of 85 seats. Foreign Secretary Hoare, Finance Minister Neville Chamberlain, and his brother Austen Chamberlain have all been re-elected. Morrison, chairman of the London County Council, who previously served as the Minister of Transport in the Labor government and is a powerful figure in the Labor Party, failed in the last election, but this time he defeated Conservative female candidate Mrs. Graves. Another important Labor leader, Clynes, who previously served as the Lord Privy Seal and Home Secretary in the Labor government and was also the chairman of the Labor Party in Parliament, also failed in the last election, but has been re-elected this time and can return to the House of Commons. (Reuters dispatch on the 15th)

Recent Developments in the Election

(London) The results of the general election are now known for about 400 seats. The government party has a majority of 169 seats over the opposition party. The reports from London and major cities on the first day made the Labor Party's hopes of winning dwindle. Today's results not only decided the Labor Party's failure, but also made the majority of the government party larger than expected. The most noteworthy event in the election is that Privy Councilor MacDonald, his son (Colonial Secretary), and Liberal Party leader Samuel all suffered defeat.

Only 390 candidates have been elected so far, all of whom belong to the Conservative Party.

As of 1:40 p.m. today, the situation of each party is as follows: the government party has won a total of 279 seats, and the opposition party has won a total of 110 seats. At that time, the government party had won 7 seats and lost 55 seats, and the opposition party had won 59 seats and lost 11 seats. Independent Liberal Party leader Lloyd George, Home Secretary Simon, and Cabinet Minister Eden have all been elected.

Privy Councilor MacDonald returned to London from the Seaham constituency without waiting for the election results to be announced and told a Reuters reporter that he had failed. This election was extremely competitive and very dirty. He was very tired and did not want to discuss his personal future plans.

The Conservative Party headquarters was very pleased with the results. Labor leader Morrison said that he was very disappointed with the Labor Party's overall report and that he had hoped that they would have done better. (Reuters dispatch on the 15th)

MacDonald's Sorrowful State

(London) National Labor Party leader and Privy Councilor MacDonald, who previously campaigned in the Seaham constituency, was greatly ridiculed by local miners. After the election ended last night, he returned here and told people, "I knew I would be defeated in the Seaham constituency, but I fought a fierce national battle and did my best." (Havas dispatch on the 15th)

Egyptian Anti-British Movement; Britain Will Not Interfere; Premier Nessim Announces Cooperation with Britain

(London) Responsible sources announced today that Britain intends to avoid political or military interference in the anti-British demonstrations in Egypt. (National Telegram, 14th)

Cairo celebrated the anniversary of the Nessim Cabinet's inauguration today. The government issued a lengthy proclamation defending its policies, stating that the Egyptian economic panic, lasting five years, has had a profound impact on the national economy, and the current cabinet is working to provide relief. Regarding the relationship between Britain and Egypt, due to the current special circumstances, Egypt must cooperate with Britain on a basis of complete freedom. (Havas Dispatch, 14th)

Cairo Premier Nessim recently issued a statement explaining the negotiations between Britain and Egypt on the Egyptian constitution issue. It is said that King Fuad advocated restoring the 1923 Constitution. The British government suggested that a new constitution should be drafted to better meet the needs of the Egyptian people. The negotiations had not yet reached a compromise when the Italo-Ethiopian dispute arose. Premier Nessim then began negotiations with the British government, requesting British protection for Egypt to maintain its independence. Britain then concentrated a portion of its Mediterranean fleet in Alexandria, while also providing assurances to Egypt that it had no intention of changing the status quo of Egypt and did not wish to use Alexandria as a permanent naval base. As soon as the situation in the Mediterranean returned to normal, it would withdraw all warships. Later, on October 18th, the Egyptian government sent a note to Britain, advocating for sincere cooperation, with Britain recognizing Egyptian sovereignty, resolving the issue of extraterritoriality, and allowing Egypt to join the League of Nations. By November 7th, Britain had issued a reply, the tone of which was still considered agreeable. The Egyptian government then expressed hope to Britain, saying that the current international situation was sufficient to raise issues concerning Egypt's survival, and that Britain would consult with the Egyptian people when decisions were made in the future. The British government did not respond, only Foreign Secretary Hoare delivered a speech at the London City Hall, insisting on the previous statement, namely opposing the 1923 Constitution and advocating for the drafting of a new constitution. In short, the government still adheres to the spirit of the constitution before restoring the constitution, which is approved by the Nationalist Party and is what the government is fortunate for. (Havas Dispatch, 15th)

Oil King Ceases Funding Baptists; Future Donations Not Limited to Denominations

(New York) Rockefeller, the son of the "Oil King," announced today the withdrawal of his financial support for the Baptist Church. In the future, donations will not be limited to denominations, as he believes that Christianity is actually one body and should not be divided into different categories. The self-establishment of different associations only serves to divide the work of Christianity and hinder the Christian spirit from benefiting humanity. (National Telegram, 14th)

Britain First Notifies the League of Nations; Embargoes Italian Goods Starting the 18th; Germany Also Announces Ban on Export of Military Supplies; Ten Italian Planes Bomb Ethiopian Military Defenses; Ethiopian Government Communiqué Condemns Italian Military Massacre

(Geneva) The British Foreign Office recently submitted a note to League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol, stating, "The British government has decided to ban the import of Italian goods starting November 18th. For countries bordering Italian territory that have not banned the import of British goods, namely Germany, Austria, Hungary, Switzerland, Liechtenstein, and Albania, goods imported into Britain must be presented with a certificate of origin to be allowed entry. However, large bars of gold and silver, newspapers, magazines, books, musical scores, maps, etc., are not included in the ban. All goods shipped from Italian ports before midnight on November 17th will be subject to the above measures." (Havas Dispatch, 15th)

(Berlin) The German government announced a ban on the export of war materials, except for those with licenses, and violators will be severely punished. This ban is the same as the one previously issued, but the German government does not want to discriminate against any country. (Reuters Dispatch, 15th)

Addis Ababa This government issued a communiqué today stating that the Italian army claims to be carrying out a mission of civilization in Abyssinia, but in reality, they are murderers of civilians, especially women and children. Italy claims to have liberated 16,000 slaves in Ethiopia, but its falsehood can be formally proven by the fact that there are not that many slaves in the entire province of Tigray. It should be noted that this communiqué was issued in response to the Italian note to the League of Nations. (Reuters Dispatch, 14th)

(London) It was learned today that ten Italian planes bombed Ethiopian defense works and large Ethiopian troop concentrations near Magal-Nambuco. (National Telegram, 15th)

A unit of Italian soldiers on the northern front of Asmara, while advancing towards Asbi to link up with the Italian First Corps, was ambushed by 500 Ethiopian soldiers en route. After a fierce battle, the Ethiopian soldiers were defeated. This group of Italian soldiers was traveling along a narrow mountain path when they were unexpectedly attacked by Ethiopian soldiers ambushed on the hillside. The Italian soldiers gradually spread out the battle line under a hail of bullets, surrounding and attacking the Ethiopian soldiers. The battle lasted all day, and eventually, due to the superior tactics of the Italian soldiers, the Ethiopian soldiers were defeated and retreated to a ridge 10,000 feet high to the west, abandoning 50 corpses and some wounded, and losing a considerable amount of military supplies. The Italian side lost four officers and 20 soldiers, and 50 soldiers were wounded. This group of Italian soldiers is still blocked by a ridge 10,000 feet high and cannot connect with the First Corps. The food they need is supplied by airplanes. This morning, the Italian army began an offensive on the southern side of Pimagà Ernand. Italian planes bombed the Ethiopian army camp outside the city of Antalo, and it was found that the camp had 500 tents. (Reuters Dispatch, 15th)

(Rome) According to reliable sources, the government plans to temporarily suspend the publication of the Bank of Italy's report during the critical period of the war against Ethiopia. This quarter's report is already four days overdue. (National Telegram, 14th)

Italian Army Occupies 12,000 Square Miles of Ethiopian Territory; However, Financial Reports Will Be Suspended in the Country

Magal-East Commander-in-Chief of the Italian Army, General Tabono, today annexed the province of Tigray to the Italian territory in the name of the King of Italy. Thousands of Italian soldiers and Ethiopians attended the ceremony. During the ceremony, the Ethiopian leader who surrendered to Italy, Gufsa, and Mussolini's son-in-law, Count Ciano, stood beside him. Thus, Italy has occupied 12,000 square miles of Ethiopian territory. (Reuters Dispatch, 14th)

(Rome) The government has decided not to announce any documents or statistics that could be used by Italy's enemies. It is reported that these documents include reports from the Italian treasury and the Bank of Italy. An order will be issued soon to lift the government's constitutional obligation to announce certain official documents. (Reuters Dispatch, 14th)

American Banking Circles Suggest Government No Longer Control

New Orleans A rift has clearly developed between national bankers and New Dealers. The American Bankers Association adjourned its meeting today in an atmosphere of opposition to the government. The delegates listened quietly to a speech by Eccles, Chairman of the Federal Reserve Board. Eccles stated that if you want the government to withdraw from the banking business, then you must lend directly to the people on security, and no longer re-lend through financial organizations. The bankers brought trouble upon themselves, so the government intervened to help you. Eccles responded to the bankers' boycott of government bonds, saying that those who clamor for a boycott are like drowning people refusing to accept a life preserver, and recognizing this as interfering with their right to drown themselves. (National Telegram, 14th)

New Orleans The American Bankers Association is holding its annual meeting here. On its final day, it passed several resolutions, one of which was that the business community deeply believes that the recovery is now progressing rapidly, and the public's trust in banks has been completely restored. The Resolutions Committee submitted the following suggestions, which were unanimously approved by the assembly: (1) The government should withdraw from the banking business; (2) Government spending should be reduced and taxes should be reduced; (3) Restrictions should be placed on the issuance of bank business licenses; (4) Competition between post office savings and deposit banks should be eliminated; (5) The government should continue to assist state railways. (Reuters Dispatch, 14th)

Detailed Rules for German Anti-Semitism

(Berlin) There were no detailed regulations for anti-Semitic laws, but official detailed rules have recently been passed. The rules are as follows: (1) From today onwards, people of mixed blood whose ancestors were Jewish for no more than two generations may be regarded as German citizens; (2) Only German citizens may enjoy the right to vote or hold official positions; (3) Jews may not be German citizens; (4) Jewish officials must resign by the end of December, but those who participated in the Great War may be granted pensions; (5) All those who have three or more generations of Jewish ancestors, or who are married to Jews, are all Jews; (6) Jews may not marry people of mixed blood; (7) Two people of mixed blood may not marry; (8) German citizens and Jews must obtain a marriage license before marriage and present a certificate of their physical fitness. (Reuters Dispatch, 15th)

Nobel Prize Winners in Chemistry and Physics

Stockholm, Sweden The Nobel Prize in Chemistry was awarded to Professor Joliot and his wife in Paris. The wife is the daughter of Madame Curie, who assisted in the discovery of radium. The Nobel Prize in Physics was awarded to Professor Chadwick of Cambridge University for his discovery of the neutron. (Reuters Dispatch, 14th)

Stockholm, Sweden It has been decided that this year's Nobel Prize in Literature will be postponed until next year. The writer who should receive the Nobel Prize in Literature will also be selected in 1936. Since 1901, the Nobel Prize in Literature has only not been awarded in one year, 1914, but there have been four previous instances where it was postponed to the second year due to special reasons. French writers Romain Rolland and Bergson, Swiss writer Spitteler, and Italian writer Beleda were all awarded the prize one year later. This year is the same. The Swedish Academy of Sciences held a meeting tonight and has decided to award this year's Nobel Prize in Physics to Professor Chadwick of Cambridge University in the United Kingdom. The two winners of this year's Chemistry Prize and last year's unissued Physics Prize will also be decided by the Swedish Academy of Sciences. (Havas Dispatch, 14th)

Soviet Economic Construction; All Departments Show Progress in Production; Railway Transportation and Heavy Industry Are Particularly Commendable; Council of People's Commissars Changes Foreign Trade Organization

(Moscow) In the third quarter of this year, Soviet industrial production increased by 20.8% compared to the same period last year. The output of means of production increased by 23.9%, and the output of consumer goods increased by 15.8%. The average increase in the production of workers in heavy industry was 168%, and the increase rate in September was 19.5%. In the first eight months of this year, the number of workers in heavy industry increased by 8.1% compared to the same period last year. During the same period, the monthly wages of workers in large enterprises increased by 265% compared to last year. In September, the daily transportation volume of railways exceeded one-third compared to September last year, and the total for nine months exceeded 189%.

In agriculture, the economic foundation has been greatly consolidated, collective farms are increasing, and technological transformation is becoming more complete. In the first nine months of this year, the Soviet People's Commissariat of Agriculture and state farms added 7,300 new civilian tractors. On October 1st, there were 350,000 civilian tractors in farms throughout the Soviet Union. If all agricultural work is converted into "cultivation work," the area cultivated by civilian tractors this year was 79 million hectares, compared to only 48.5 million hectares last year.

The total retail trade volume of the Soviet Union increased by 39.2% in the third quarter compared to the same period last year. The amount of food supplied by farms increased by 24.5% in the past eight months, with the largest increases in meat, eggs, and sweet potatoes. The total foreign trade volume of the Soviet Union in nine months was 432.2 million rubles, with a surplus of 83.6 million rubles.

The achievements of economic construction this year indicate that the third year of the Second Five-Year Plan will be successfully completed. Among them, the improvement of railway transportation and the profitability of the egg industry (especially the steel industry) are the most commendable. (TASS Dispatch, 15th)

(Moscow) The Soviet Council of People's Commissars decided that the "Torgsin" foreign trade company will be abolished from February 1st next year, and its branches in various places will be transferred to the People's Commissariat of Domestic Trade. At the same time, foreign travel agencies are ordered to stop operating foreign exchange in the country from January 1st next year. The National Bank is authorized to convert foreign exchange into 10 rubles of national currency in 1936 according to the current exchange rate (1 franc is equal to 33.33 kopecks, and other foreign exchange rates are calculated accordingly). (TASS Dispatch, 15th)

(Moscow) The Russian People's Committee ordered today that the ruble be maintained at a stable rate relative to the American gold dollar, with a ratio of one US dollar for every five rubles, to be implemented from January 1st next year. (National Telegram, 14th)

Fujian-Suiyuan Garrison Headquarters Advisor Wu Ci Suddenly Assassinated

(Xiamen) Wu Ci, advisor to the Suiyuan Garrison Headquarters, left his private residence in Zhangzhou by rickshaw at 1:00 PM on the 15th. When he arrived at Dongmen Street, he was ambushed by more than ten assailants who opened fire, hitting him five times and killing him on the spot. The assailants all escaped. Wu was formerly the leader of greenwoodsmen in the Zhangzhou area. (Special Dispatch, 15th)

National Government Issues Order to Commend He Lizhong and Others

(Nanjing) On the 15th, the National Government ordered that He Lizhong, commander of the 110th Division of the Army, Chief of Staff Fan Qingzhao, and regimental commander Yang Dexin, personally led troops to supervise the suppression of bandits near Laoshan in northern Ganquan. Due to the disparity in numbers, they were wounded and died. The commander and others were loyal, courageous, and devoted themselves to the country. They should be publicly commended and handed over to the Military Affairs Committee for generous pensions to honor their loyalty and encourage those who come after. This order. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 15th)

Sun Chuanfang's Assassin, Shi Jianqiao, Was Escorted to Court Yesterday

(Tianjin) Sun Chuanfang received condolences from Wang Yitang, Cao Rulin, Wang Chengbin, Jin Yunpeng, and others on the afternoon of the 15th. Shi Jianqiao, the assassin of Sun, has been escorted to the court by the Public Security Bureau. Sun Chuanfang's family intends to hire a lawyer to submit a petition to the court requesting severe punishment. (Special Dispatch, 15th)

(Tianjin) Shi Jianqiao's family will present a petition to the court, requesting that Shi be leniently punished according to the regulations on commutation of sentences for those who confess to murder. He Yingqin telegraphed Cheng Ke on the 15th to offer condolences to Sun's family. Sun's relatives and friends will hold a meeting on the afternoon of the 16th to discuss funeral arrangements and follow-up matters. Their external statement will be made by a lawyer, approximately three points: 1. Recount the circumstances of Sun's killing of Shi Congbin; 2. State the attitude of the Sun family, that they will never take revenge on Shi; 3. This case will be decided solely by law. After Shi Jianqiao entered the detention center, she requested preferential treatment from the prosecutor, which has been granted. (Special Dispatch, 15th)

(Tianjin) Sun Chuanfang's family will issue a statement stating that Sun killed Shi Congbin for the sake of the country and the people. (Special Dispatch, 15th)

Hsiang-Han Main Dike Construction Plan Approved

(Hankou) The construction plan for the Hsiang-Han main dike in Hubei has been approved by the central government. The construction funds are 6 million yuan, 2 million yuan will be allocated from the Hubei dike funds, 2 million yuan will be allocated by the conference, and the remainder will be allocated by the central government from the work relief funds. Construction is scheduled to start this month and be completed next May. The repair of people's dikes requires 10 million yuan, which will be undertaken by the people providing labor. The central government has agreed to provide subsidies. The Water Disaster Association telegraphed the central government on the 15th to allocate funds to start repairs while the rivers are dry. (Special Dispatch, 15th)

After the 9th, the market stabilized and prices gradually fell, but compared to five days ago, prices still rose by an average of 10%. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 14th)

International Commercial Telegram

Special Commercial Telegram from Reuters on November 15th

Gold and Silver The London gold price rose half a penny today to 241 shillings and five pence.

The London silver market remained unchanged today. The spot price was 20. The market was stable, with small transactions from American purchases.

Exchange Rates The London foreign exchange market was quiet this morning. The Anglo-American exchange rate opened at $4.921875, up 3125 from yesterday's closing price of American and British currencies. It fell 125 after the first hour and returned to $4.921875 at 2:00 PM.

The Anglo-French rate opened up six pounds, at 74 francs 71. It fell two pounds after the first hour and returned to 74 francs 72 at 2:00 PM.

Cotton and Wheat New York cotton opened unchanged. Although prices fell three points later, the market remained stable due to the extension of the loan term for cotton at one dime and two cents per pound. Subsequent short-selling was absorbed.

Liverpool cotton market rose three points at 1:00 PM today, to 6.49.

Liverpool wheat market, December futures price at 1:00 PM today was five shillings and eleven pence 875, up three seventy-five.

Chicago wheat market, opened down three seventy-five, then fell again The food opened up two five, and then continued to rise one two five due to purchases. There was profit-taking, and the price fell slightly?

Rubber The London rubber market was stable this morning. The transaction price for January-March futures at noon was six pence 5625, up zero six two five from yesterday's close. New York rubber opened up twelve pounds due to the firm London rubber market. Demand was good. The market price fell seven pounds during power-up due to long liquidation.

Securities The New York stock market was still firm at the opening this morning, but there was slight profit-taking during later trading activity. Entertainment stocks were very active after the opening. The average price of the Dow Jones 30 industrial stocks opened at 145.88, up twenty-nine pounds.

Sino-French Air Service to Begin Test Flights Within Days

(Nanjing) It has been decided that the Sino-French air service will begin test flights within days. The Ministry of Communications has ordered the China National Aviation Corporation to select Chinese pilots to handle the matter. The test flight aircraft is the Douglas Door Yu No. The test flight will first depart from Shanghai and fly directly to Guangzhou, and then from Guangzhou directly to Hanoi, the capital of Annam Province. The test flight period is scheduled for three months. After the test flight, it will be officially opened to air traffic in three months. The issues of freight and other fees have been ordered to be drafted by the competent department, and the two parties, China and France, will exchange references with each other. Once it is properly determined, it will be announced and implemented, ordering the China National Aviation Corporation to comply. (Special Dispatch, 15th)

Cause of Continuous Rainy Weather in the Yangtze River Basin

(Nanjing) According to the Central Meteorological Observatory, the cause of the continuous rainy weather in the Yangtze River Basin is that the northwest high pressure bypassed the ocean without heading south directly, and at the same time, the southern low pressure is strong. The current high pressure has a tendency to turn south, and the weather in the capital is expected to improve on the 16th, and the temperature will also decrease. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 15th)

Capital New Games to Hold Meeting to Welcome Representatives of the General Association

(Nanjing) The Capital New Games held a meeting of directors at noon on the 15th to welcome the representatives of the General Association, Yan Baohang and others. Wang Shufang presided over the meeting. In addition to reporting on recent work, Ge also gave a guiding speech. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 15th)

(Kaifeng) The Yellow River Conservancy Commission has compiled a table of the dangerous conditions of the people-built embankments along the Yellow River and ordered the Henan, Hebei, and Shandong River Bureaus to fill out the report. The second section of the river in southern Hebei experienced a significant landslide, and the head of the first brick dam suffered severe erosion. On the 14th, the top of the main current directly impacted the dam, causing the top and bottom openings to abruptly collapse into the water. The Yellow River Conservancy Commission allocated 100,000 bricks and 100 bundles each of sizes 14 and 16 lead wire, ordering a full effort to reinforce the protection. (Fifteenth Day Special Dispatch)

Hunan Province Requests Additional Funds for Dike Repair

(Changsha) The construction project for the Xiangjiang River dike and sluice gates in Linxiang, Hunan, is estimated to require 160,000 yuan. The repair project for the dikes and embankments of Dongting Lake requires more than 12,900,000 yuan. The Provincial Government has reported to the Central Government, requesting the customary allocation of 50% of the funds, totaling more than 6,500,000 yuan. According to current reports, the Economic Commission has only allocated 300,000 yuan, a difference of more than twenty times. The Provincial Government believes that Hunan's public and private economies are in dire straits, and this meager amount is utterly insufficient. On the 13th, they telegraphed the Central Government again, earnestly requesting full allocation according to precedent to facilitate repairs. (Fifteenth Day Central News Agency Dispatch)

Southeastern Bank of Fujian Province Temporarily Suspends Business

(Fuzhou) The Southeastern Bank announced on the 14th that it would suspend business for three days. Authorities have been dispatched to investigate the bank's issued notes, totaling approximately 1,400,000 yuan. Insufficient funds are in the vault, with approximately 600,000 yuan in pledged real estate and approximately 300,000 yuan in credit loans. Currently, all key responsible individuals have gone into hiding. The residences of the managers and others have been searched. The Xin and Tai Farmers' Banks have also experienced runs due to the fluctuations. The two banks announced unlimited withdrawals starting on the 15th, which has calmed the situation. Residents of Northern Xuzhou Desperately Need Relief

(Xuzhou) In the northern Xuzhou area, successive heavy winds and rain have caused unusually cold weather. All dikes are being diligently protected by laborers, and fortunately, no accidents have occurred. However, the disaster victims lack clothing and food and desperately need relief. It is earnestly hoped that all parties will provide assistance. (Fifteenth Day Special Dispatch)

The Water Level in the Hai Prefecture Area Is Receding Very Slowly

(Xuzhou) Hai Prefecture reports that the water level in the Hai Prefecture area is receding very slowly. To this day, most of the disaster area remains deeply flooded, making it difficult to plant wheat, leaving little hope for the coming spring. Winter relief has not yet been organized, and spring famine has already become a problem. The Commissioner's Office has telegraphed a report to the province, urging prompt formulation of effective measures. (Fifteenth Day Special Dispatch)

The Floodwaters in Suqian Are Gradually Receding

(Xuzhou) Suqian reports that the floodwaters in Suqian are gradually receding. All sectors of society are concentrating their efforts on strengthening and protecting the Yinma Dike in Xiangli Township, which is vital to the safety of the entire city, to ensure the security of the urban area. (Fifteenth Day Special Dispatch)

Jiangsu Provincial Government Strictly Orders Expedited Completion of the Huai River Diversion into the Sea Project

(Huaiyin) In light of the Yellow River flood disaster this summer, the Jiangsu Provincial Government, noting that the eastern Guannan, Shuyang, Suyu, and Sucheng counties are still submerged, and to prevent the difficult situation of simultaneous flooding from the Huai, Yi, Si, and Shu rivers next spring, urgently telegraphed the Huai River Diversion into the Sea Project Office on the 14th, ordering the second phase of the project to be completed ahead of schedule by April of next year. It also ordered the nine counties of Huaiyin, Huai’an, Lian’shui, Siyang, Yancheng, Funing, Baoying, and Dongtai to dispatch the full quota of conscripted laborers to the project site by the 20th, and to dispatch an additional 50% of the originally stipulated conscripted labor quota by the end of this month. Delays will be severely punished. (Fifteenth Day Special Dispatch)

Robbery Occurs Outside Zhenjiang City

(Zhenjiang) At around 5 p.m. on the 15th, four plainclothes armed bandits suddenly broke into the home of Shi Shouxin, resident of No. 13 Zhishui Lane outside Zhenjiang City, and robbed him of gold and silver jewelry worth several hundred yuan. The entire city is now under special martial law, and the military and police are conducting a strict search. (Fifteenth Day Central News Agency Dispatch)

Jiangsu Provincial Government Holds Discussion Meeting Yesterday

(Zhenjiang) The Jiangsu Provincial Government Committee, due to insufficient attendance, held a discussion meeting on the 15th and decided: 1. To approve the expenditure of 5,500 yuan from the reserve fund to cover the shortfall in the cost of emergency dike repair in Tongshan District. 2. To appoint Zhou Fei as the director of the Provincial Forestry Experiment Station. 3. To add 17,000 yuan to cover the shortfall in the cost of constructing model agricultural warehouses in Wu County and seven other counties under the jurisdiction of the Finance Department. (Fifteenth Day Central News Agency Dispatch)
