Western Travel Notes

— Ji Yuan

A Visit to Beibei (Part 1)

On the morning of October 6th, the reporter and Mr. Songhua braved the rain to visit Beibei. We had heard of the new construction projects in Beibei while in Shanghai, and upon arriving in Chongqing, friends also told us that Beibei was a must-see. Therefore, immediately after arriving in Chongqing, we went to visit Beibei. On that day, we got up at 4 a.m., quickly got washed and packed, and took the rickshaw that had been reserved the night before to the Qianximen Wharf. As dawn broke, we boarded the Minsheng steamer just after 5 a.m. The autumn rain was drizzling all the way, which was quite inconvenient. Chongqing is very rainy, which is a real pain. The passengers on the ship were crowded, and the voices were noisy. The fare to Beibei was a uniform one dollar, regardless of class, which fits the principle of popularization. However, there were few seats and many passengers, so those who arrived later often had to stand. We were fortunate to be invited by Mr. Zheng Bicheng, the manager of Minsheng Company, to sit in the manager's office, avoiding the crowds. I was secretly very grateful. At 6:30 a.m., the ship sailed up the Jialing River. Peering out the window, we saw picturesque scenery on both banks. The journey from Chongqing to the Wenquan Park in Beibei is only about 140 li, and it passes through two gorges of the Jialing River (Guanyin Gorge and Wenquan Gorge). In addition, there is Niubi Gorge. The scenery of these three gorges, although not as majestic and perilous as the Three Gorges of the Yangtze River, is more beautiful. Now, I will briefly describe the situation in Beibei based on what I saw and heard.

1. Wenquan (Hot Springs) Park. At noon, the ship arrived at Wenquan Park. After disembarking, we climbed up the steps. At that time, the park was busy preparing for a group wedding. The members of the Youth Volunteer Corps were also engaged in preparing the auditorium and the venue, which are part of an ancient temple. The Buddha statue still exists today. Since Lu Zuofu became the head of the Gorge Defense Bureau in 1927, he has been determined to develop it, and it has now become a public tourist area. The park has a lot of flowers and trees, and the scenery is quiet and elegant. Walking through it, one feels as if they are in a cool world. The park is equipped with hotels, restaurants, bathhouses, swimming pools, tennis courts, basketball courts, libraries, music rooms, etc. I heard that many mass gatherings in Chongqing and Beibei are held here. Under the guidance of Manager Zheng and Manager Ma of Minsheng Company, we visited various caves. The next morning, we braved the rain to visit Jinyun Temple, but due to lack of time, we had to turn back halfway, which was regrettable. In the afternoon, we watched the group wedding ceremony in the park's auditorium. This group wedding was initiated voluntarily by the people and was very economical, which corrected the old custom of elaborate rituals and wasteful spending.

2. Youth Volunteer Corps. In Wenquan Park, we saw the lives and work of the Youth Volunteer Corps. The training of the Youth Volunteer Corps is an expression of Lu Zuofu's advocacy of "human training." Mr. Lu believes that the fundamental problem in China is "human training." Therefore, he pays special attention to the training of young people in all kinds of construction. The central meaning of his training of young people is to "make the generally trained young people full of social demands, social ideals, and social activities, requiring them to understand very clearly the current trends of the world and the difficulties of China, and to understand very clearly the ideal Three Gorges and demand to realize it." This is an important point in his rural construction theory and a characteristic of Beibei's construction of China.

The daily life of the Youth Volunteer Corps is very arduous and disciplined. They wear straw sandals and yellow cloth uniforms (woven by the Three Gorges Cloth Factory). They are strong, have shaved heads. The members are all young students with middle school or higher education. I heard that there are many applicants each time they recruit, and due to the limited number of places, the admission is very strict. Special attention is paid to physical examinations. Those who are slightly physically weak are not admitted. The training period is one year, divided into three stages. The first stage is (A) military subjects, (B) scout training, (C) service training, including document management, bookkeeping, statistics, etc. The second stage is (A) police service training, (B) social investigation training, (C) social education training. The third stage is traveling to border areas, investigating the lives of aborigines, and collecting natural specimens. Daily life in the team begins at 5 a.m. After washing, they gather in the sports field to exercise according to the arranged exercise program for one hour. After breakfast, they start work. They are responsible for sweeping the floor, dumping manure, wiping the floor, wiping tables and chairs, glass windows, as well as planting, irrigating, removing insects, and washing clothes, in order to cultivate the spirit of hard work, endurance, courage, and enterprise in group life. The reporters visited the dormitory of the Youth Volunteer Corps and saw that the quilts were neatly folded and printed with the four characters "Sleeping on brushwood and tasting gall," a spirit of perseverance and determination overflowing from their daily lives. I heard that the establishment of the Youth Volunteer Corps began in the autumn of 1928. In the spring of 1933, a special student team was added, graduating in six months. The training program is roughly the same as that of the Youth Volunteer Corps. A total of 95 people have graduated and have been assigned to serve in various business organizations in the Gorge area. Two teams of the Youth Volunteer Corps have graduated, and there are currently about 60 members of the Youth Volunteer Corps in school.

3. Visit to the Gorge Defense Bureau. After visiting Wenquan Park, we hired a small boat at about 4 p.m. on the 7th to go to Beibei. From Wenquan to Beibei is only 10 li away, and the boat travels downstream in about 20 minutes to the borrowed Gorge Defense Bureau. The Gorge Defense Bureau is the abbreviation of the Jiangba Bi-Tai Special Group Gorge Defense Bureau. It was established around 1918-1919, initially named the Gorge Defense Camp. Its mission was to suppress bandits in the Three Gorges of the Jialing River. In 1923, it was renamed the current name (recently, it was heard that it will be renamed the Jiangba Bi-He Experiment Zone). In the spring of 1927, Lu Zuofu and Xiong Mingfu became the director and deputy director, respectively. In addition to suppressing bandits, they began to build cultural and economic projects. The organization of the Gorge Defense Bureau is a director and deputy director, each with one person. Underneath are the Training Department and three sections: General Affairs, Politics, and Audit. The Training Department commands the Youth Volunteer Corps, Special Task Force One, Special Task Force Two, Special Task Force Three, and the Pistol Team. In addition, there are group affairs instructors, hiring local prestigious figures to serve as group affairs instructors. Currently, the First Special Task Force is stationed in Beibei City, with about 60 team members. Their work includes: (1) Police aspects (A) investigating households, (B) registering births, deaths, marriages, and migrations, (C) handling people's disputes, (D) organizing fire brigades; (2) public education aspects (A) training people to observe order (training citizens to observe order at public gatherings, training passengers to observe order at riverside wharves), (B) training people to pay attention to hygiene (inspecting the cleanliness of the market, rewarding the extermination of flies and rats, publicizing hygiene matters, etc.), (C) training people for public activities (teaching people to sing at public gatherings, teaching people to clap at public gatherings); (3) local operations (A) organizing riverside wharves, (B) assisting in the construction of public roads, (C) delineating various markets, (D) constructing public toilets. The Second Special Task Force is stationed along the Beichuan Railway, with about 130 people, with three sub-stations stationed along the railway. Their regular work, in addition to the above points, is to escort trains, passengers, and cargo, and maintain order at the station. In terms of education, they pay attention to inspecting household cleanliness and establishing literacy night schools (there is currently one), public picture newspaper reading rooms (there is one), and news briefings (there are currently four). The Third Special Task Force is stationed in Xiaxikou, with about 130 people. The police work focuses on protecting the security of the mining area. Local management businesses include public sports grounds, public libraries, public clock towers, and the operation of the Canal Park, etc. The main task of the Pistol Team is to maintain local security, with about a hundred people. Their work can be divided into four aspects: (1) Security, (2) Military Training, (3) Social Work, (4) Morning Management. In terms of security (A) dispatching teams to patrol various fields in the Gorge area at any time, (B) secretly observing bandits in various fields in the Gorge area and the Heyu (Hechuan-Chongqing) area at any time. In terms of military training, they practice national martial arts for one hour every morning. Academic subjects are taught for two sessions each in the morning and afternoon. Field exercises and shooting exercises are conducted once a week each. In terms of social work, every year in winter (lecturing to the national people on November 8th and 10th for two days)

Education Broadcasting Special Issue

The Benefits of the National Calendar

— Chen ZunKui, Researcher at the Astronomical Institute of the Academia Sinica

(A lecture given to the national public on November 8th and 10th)

The topic we are going to discuss is "The Benefits of the National Calendar." Before we delve into this topic, we must first understand what a "calendar" is and what the "National Calendar" is. Only then can we understand its benefits. Furthermore, the goodness or badness of a thing is inherently subjective. Someone might say it's good, while another might say it's bad. Therefore, to determine whether something is good or bad, we must compare it with something else. To discuss the benefits of the National Calendar, we need to compare it with another calendar system. The calendar system we will use for comparison is the old calendar that we have abolished. Thus, before we delve into this topic, we must first know how the old calendar was made. Therefore, I can divide this topic into three sections: first, what is a calendar? Second, how are the National Calendar and the old calendar made? Third, what are the benefits of the National Calendar?

First, let's ask what the significance of a calendar is. What exactly is a calendar? In simple terms, a calendar can be described as an almanac or calendar book. More precisely, a calendar is a calendrical system. The calendar itself has no inherent meaning; it arises from the needs of society and evolves with human progress. As you all know, the sun has two most obvious movements relative to our position. The first is its movement from east to west, and the second is its movement from north to south. The causes of these two movements have been explained before: the first is due to the Earth's rotation, and the second is due to the Earth's revolution, which is the Earth's orbit around the sun. The first effect is that sunrise marks the day, and sunset marks the night. This is probably the earliest knowledge known to mankind. In the ancient hunter-gatherer era, when people were hungry, they would look for food, and when they were thirsty, they would look for water. When the sun came out, they would hunt, and when it went down, they would rest. Humans' concept of time only consisted of day and night, knowing only the "day." But the second effect, the north-south movement, created the changing of the four seasons. It dictated the laws of hibernation and awakening, growth, maturity, germination, and withering of plants and animals. This knowledge may have taken humans thousands or even tens of thousands of years to discover. The sun's north-south cycle, which we now call a year, has an inescapable causal relationship with the climate. Gaining this true knowledge can be said to be the first great contribution of astronomy to mankind. Since human life is governed by these two cycles—day and year—for the sake of safety and improvement, humans cannot help but follow the movements of the heavens to define units of time and make them the standard for their lives. Especially for nations that have evolved to the agricultural era, the knowledge and utilization of the year have become an indispensable matter for survival. This is why the two cycles of day and year have become natural units of time in the calendar.

However, the number of days in each year is more than three hundred and sixty. Counting from the beginning to the end of the year, in the eyes of the ancients, was probably very troublesome and difficult to remember clearly. Furthermore, human life became more and more complex, and this method of recording gradually became inconvenient. Therefore, an intermediate cycle was inserted. There were two ways to create this intermediate cycle. The first was to take a set of regular intervals and count them down cyclically. For example, the Chinese Jiazi system of recording days, which uses sixty days as a cycle, rotating continuously, and the foreign weekly system, which uses seven days as a cycle, rotating continuously, are both examples of this method and are both very ancient. The second was to use a visible celestial phenomenon to divide the year, and the waxing and waning of the moon was the most suitable condition. This is why the origins of calendars in various countries around the world mostly contain lunar elements.

Therefore, the calendar arises from the needs of human life and evolution. It is the rule for specifying the allocation of years, months, and dates. It must conform to celestial phenomena and strive for the convenience of society. In the past, calendrical systems focused on the precision of calculations. Now, the cycles of the sun, moon, and earth are already well understood. Therefore, today's calendrical systems are not concerned with the density of calculations, but rather with the harmony of the annual, monthly, and daily allocations.

We already know that the elements of a calendar are the year, the month, and the day. The standard for these three elements is that the year is based on the time it takes for the Earth to revolve around the Sun once, the month is based on the time it takes for the Moon to revolve around the Earth once, and the day is based on the time it takes for the Earth to rotate on its axis once. We know that the number of days it takes for the Earth to orbit the Sun is not a whole number; it is three hundred and sixty-five and a quarter of a day, minus a little bit. However, the practical year must contain a whole number of days, which is already enough to cause us trouble when creating a calendar. Now, we must also insert a monthly division, and the length of the month is based on the time it takes for the Moon to orbit the Earth, which is also twenty-nine and a fraction of a day, not a whole number of days. Since a month does not contain a whole number of days, and a year is not a whole number of months, reconciling them becomes a complex problem. It can be said that the purpose of ancient Chinese astronomy was to solve this problem.

The calendar used in China can be roughly divided into four periods. The first is the calendar used before the first year of the Taichu era of Emperor Wu of the Han Dynasty (before 104 BC). The details are no longer known. The second is the calendar from the Taichu era of the Han Dynasty to the early Qing Dynasty (around 1600 AD). There are written records of the calendar reforms in historical records. Although there were more than seventy calendar reformers, the principles remained unchanged, and they were all calendars created by China itself. The third is the calendar of the Qing Dynasty, which used Western methods and combined them with the old calendar system, which is the period of Sino-Western integration. The fourth is the Roman Gregorian calendar established by Gregory XIII, which was adopted after the establishment of the Republic of China and is now called the National Calendar. (Note 1) In my personal opinion, the current calendar was not created by China itself. It is not appropriate to call a calendar created by others the National Calendar. However, the Central Party Headquarters has designated it as the National Calendar, so I will still refer to it as the National Calendar.

As mentioned above, the principles of the calendar used from the Taichu era of the Han Dynasty to the early Qing Dynasty remained unchanged. Their principle was that each year contained twelve lunar months, and the lunar month was determined by the new moon and full moon. Each month had twenty-nine or thirty days, so twelve months were several days shorter than a solar year of three hundred and sixty-five days. After several years, when the difference amounted to a month, a lunar month was added to that year, called a leap month. That year then had thirteen months. Roughly speaking, there were seven leap months in nineteen years. Their efforts were to obtain accurate lunar and solar cycles and the most appropriate way to insert leap months.

In addition to the lunar month divisions, our old calendar also had twenty-four solar terms. It should be said that there were twelve "zhongqi" (principal solar terms) and twelve "jieqi" (secondary solar terms), but in ordinary speech, they are often mixed up and called solar terms. When discussing the changes of the four seasons last time, I mentioned that the twenty-four solar terms are determined according to the sun's annual position. Their allocation is based on Lichun (Beginning of Spring) as the first month's "jie," Yushui (Rain Water) as the first month's "zhong," Jingzhe (Awakening of Insects) as the second month's "jie," Chunfen (Vernal Equinox) as the second month's "zhong," and so on, dividing them into the third month's "jie," the third month's "zhong," and so on, in the order of Qingming (Clear and Bright), Guyu (Grain Rain), etc. Finally, Xiaohan (Minor Cold) is the twelfth month's "jie," and Dahan (Major Cold) is the twelfth month's "zhong." This is a very scientific method. Frankly speaking, it is more rational than the months of the solar calendar. However, the solar terms are only calculated by calendrical experts or measured by the length of the sun's shadow. They are not as obvious as the waxing and waning of the moon, so they probably came about much later than the lunar month system. This method of accommodating and reconciling the lunar month and the solar year is the so-called "lunar calendar" that China used for thousands of years before the revolution. It should really be called the "lunisolar calendar." This lunisolar calendar has many inconveniences.

First, the number of days in each year is not fixed and can differ by up to a month.

Second, the length of each month is not fixed.

Third, the same month and day of each year do not correspond to the same solar term, and the difference can also be up to a month.

Moreover, these uncertainties do not have simple rules that can be calculated. Therefore, to know the dates and solar terms of the old calendar, one must check the almanac issued each year. Because the positions of the sun and moon relative to the solar terms are not fixed, farmers not only have to check which month is large and which month is small, but also which day is the Vernal Equinox, which day is Clear and Bright, and so on. As for annual and monthly statistics, if accuracy is desired, it is, at the very least, extremely troublesome under this system. Therefore, after the success of the Xinhai Revolution, the Nanjing Provisional Government promulgated the adoption of the solar calendar. On the one hand, this was to eliminate the trouble of the lunar calendar, and on the other hand, it was to align with the world, because most countries in the world now use the solar calendar, and the globalization of various systems is of great significance with increasing global interaction.

The composition of the old calendar has already been mentioned above. How is the current National Calendar composed? Simply put, it abandons the lunar method, meaning it does not base a month on the time it takes for the moon to orbit the earth once. It only seeks the regularity of years and days, rigidly dividing the year into twelve months. Therefore, the names of its months are merely practically assumed terms that have no real scientific meaning. They are only used to coordinate the method of recording time. The unit of a year is considered too long, and the unit of a day is considered too short, so the unit of a month is used to reconcile them. To elaborate further, it is:

(1) A year is divided into three hundred and sixty-five days, and a leap year is three hundred and sixty-six days.

(2) A year is divided into twelve months.

(3) January, March, May, July, August, October, and December each have thirty-one days.

(4) April, June, September, and November each have thirty days.

(5) February has twenty-eight days in a common year and twenty-nine days in a leap year.

(6) A leap year occurs every four years, omitting one leap year every hundred years, and still leaping every four hundred years. (To be continued)

Helping to Dredge Dangerous Waters and Eliminate River Obstructions in the Hechuan-Yongchuan Area. Every summer, when the Jialing River rises, they help residents along the river move their houses. Every spring and autumn, they help the people build roads. In their spare time, all the soldiers in the team plant various flowers and fruit trees. It is said that last year, the Beibei Farm earned over a thousand yuan from watermelon production. The planting method uses scientific methods, and the watermelons are sweet and large, and they are popular. The reporter stayed at the Gorge Defense Bureau for three nights and talked a lot with the gentlemen of the bureau. The reporter's life gradually blended in with theirs. They use communal chopsticks when dining and eat standing up. At first, the reporter was very unaccustomed to it, but then he found it quite meaningful. The director of the Political Affairs Division of the Bureau, Mr. Wang, studied political economy in France. He lives a simple life, just like the soldiers. The Deputy Battalion Commander, Mr. Wu, is a graduate of Whampoa Military Academy and has served as a company commander and battalion commander. He is very loyal. The Company Commander, Mr. Song, used to belong to Liu Wenhui's troops. He served as a battalion commander, and he was brave and good at fighting. Once, he was seriously injured in an internal conflict. After he recovered, he became enlightened, left Liu's troops, and joined the Gorge Defense Bureau. The reporter talked with him, asking about his military experience. Mr. Song spoke frankly, saying, "The life of the army in the past was a life of all evil." He also described the various evils of the Sichuan warlords, and his indignation overflowed from his words. The reporter then asked him about his thoughts on the national crisis. Mr. Song replied indignantly, "As long as there is an opportunity to sacrifice for the country, I will not hesitate to go." His enthusiastic spirit was evident. The annual income of the Gorge Defense Bureau is about 80,000 yuan. The salaries of the staff are very low. The heads of each division receive a monthly salary of about thirty or forty yuan. The monthly salary of the staff is from ten to twenty yuan. Students who graduate from the Youth Volunteer Team and enter the bureau receive a monthly salary of eight yuan. After deducting more than three yuan for food expenses and about half a yuan for laundry and haircuts, the cost of uniforms is also deducted from the salary, so there is very little left.

The enterprises affiliated to the Gorge Defense Bureau include: (1) The Gorge Area Local Hospital, located in Beibei, is converted from an old temple. The scale is quite small. There is one director, one obstetrician-gynecologist, and several nurses. The fees for patients are very low, and free medical care is provided for the poor and sick. The annual income from registration fees, medical expenses, and delivery fees is about 700 yuan. The deficit is subsidized by the Gorge Defense Bureau. (2) The Jialing River Daily, edited and published by the Political Affairs Division of the Gorge Bureau. Initially, it was a tri-weekly publication. In October of the 17th year of the Republic, it was changed to an intermittent publication. In January of the 20th year, it was changed to a daily publication. Each day, a small sheet is printed. The content focuses on national defense, industry, transportation, and cultural news. The supplement focuses on modern new inventions, new discoveries, new records, and new activities, which is quite representative of the consistent spirit of Beibei's construction. The editor, Mr. Pan Bihai, has a lot of research and experience in rural construction. (3) The Gorge Area Reformatory is still in preparation. The reporter visited the streets, hospitals, libraries, public parks, and people's clubs (teahouses) in Beibei Town and saw that the streets were clean, and the residents also paid attention to hygiene and observed order. Most of the roads were built by the townspeople under the leadership of the Gorge Defense Bureau, so the cost was low and the construction was good. According to someone, "Beibei has now reached the point where doors are not locked at night, and only the road is not picked up. But ten years ago, it was an area where banditry occurred from time to time."

Hydraulic Engineering Laboratory in Tianjin Completed and Opened—The Only Hydraulic Experiment Institution in the Country

Tianjin Correspondence. The new construction of the First Hydraulic Engineering Laboratory in China, the only Yongli experiment institution in the country, has been under construction for many years and was completed on the 12th of this month. Coincidentally, the Chinese Hydraulic Engineering Society and the Hebei Provincial Engineering Association held a joint annual meeting in Tianjin, so the institute took the opportunity to hold an opening ceremony and conduct a water release test at the same time. More than 100 guests attended that day. Li Yizhi presided over the meeting and reported on the significance of the construction. Then, the director of the institute, Li Fudu, reported on the construction process. Finally, Director Li Shutian gave a speech. The ceremony ended at 12:00. Li Yizhi released water for the test, and the results were excellent.

According to the report by the director of the institute, Li Fudu, the First Hydraulic Engineering Laboratory in China was jointly established by the Yellow River, Huai River, North China, and Yangtze River four hydraulic committees, the Hebei Provincial Industrial College, the National Beiyang Institute of Technology, the Construction Committee, the Model Irrigation Administration, and the Shaanxi Water Conservancy Bureau eight institutions. When the North China Water Conservancy Committee was completed in the 17th year of the Republic, the Chairman, Li Yizhi, and the Standing Committee Member, Li Shutian, had personally visited major hydraulic engineering laboratories in Europe and the United States. They deeply believed that solving various hydraulic engineering problems required a hydraulic engineering laboratory. Therefore, the North China Water Conservancy Committee proposed a plan to establish a hydraulic engineering laboratory at its general meeting and suggested it to the Construction Committee. However, the plan was shelved due to the failure to allocate funds. In the 22nd year of the Republic, the director of the institute represented the three provinces of Hebei, Shandong, and Henan to participate in the Yellow River test in Germany. At that time, the plan for the hydraulic engineering laboratory was reviewed by Professors Engel and Fangsius, who considered it appropriate. After returning to China, the director reported to the North China Water Conservancy Committee, which then held a meeting with the Yellow River, Huai River, and other seven institutions to organize the board of directors. Construction began in the spring of last year, and the total cost was over 157,900 yuan, which was donated by various participating institutions and national hydraulic institutions and subsidized by the Construction Committee. The regular expenses were set at 1,000 yuan per month. The Yellow River Water Conservancy Committee and the North China Water Conservancy Committee each bear 350 yuan, the Hebei Provincial Industrial College allocates 200 yuan, and the National Beiyang Institute of Technology allocates 100 yuan. The tests are divided into preparatory and formal types: A. Preparatory Tests (1) Yellow River River Preparatory Test, (2) Yellow Earth Sedimentation Test. B. Formal Tests (1) Muddy Water Flow Test, (2) Reservoir Sedimentation Test, (3) Yellow Earth River Fundamental Policy Test, (4) Yellow Earth River Local Engineering Test, (5) Guanting Dam Energy Dissipation Test. After the opening ceremony on the 12th, the tests began. The institute is 70 meters long from east to west and 30 meters wide from north to south. There are two water storage tanks at the rear, about 30 meters high. Below is a reservoir. During the test, tap water is injected into the reservoir, and water is pumped to the aerial water tank by a water pump. Then, the water is passed into various test models through water pipes. The water level and flow rate are measured with instruments. In front of the reservoir is the Guanting Dam energy dissipation test model, which is used to study how the Guanting Dam in the upper reaches of the Yongding River can prevent sediment erosion. Further ahead is the Yellow Earth River model, which stretches for more than 20 meters and meanders. There is a river channel in the middle, only a foot wide, and the banks are made of yellow earth. In the initial Guanting Dam release test, it was seen that the flood passed through the water barrier dam, and the water勢 was turbulent. Gradually, the flow became stable. The test lasted for an hour, and the results were very good. This was commissioned by the Yongding River Engineering Office and tested ahead of schedule. The next test was the Yellow Earth River model and the sedimentation situation. After the water flow was injected into the model, it was gradually seen that the river bank near the water was scoured by the water flow, and most of it was submerged. The flood was turbulent, and there were many vortexes. This test clearly showed the situation along the Yellow River. The test lasted about half an hour. The management of the institute is handled by a board of directors consisting of one director from each of the eight institutions. Li Yizhi was appointed as the chairman of the board of directors, totaling nine directors and chairman. All are honorary positions with a term of three years, and one-third are re-elected each year. After this opening, the preparatory tests will be carried out immediately. (13th)

Situation in Guangzhou After Currency Management—A Glimpse of the Market—Prices About 20% Higher Than Before—Silver Shops and Banks Have Resumed Business

Guangzhou Correspondence. Since the Finance Department announced the currency management measures, although citizens felt slightly inconvenient about the abolition of the silver coin system, there was not much disturbance in the market. However, due to the hasty reform of the system, silver coins lost their value as currency. There was a temporary shortage of auxiliary currency. The one-dime banknotes issued by provincial and municipal banks on weekdays were insufficient for circulation. The Provincial Bank has now issued the five-dime silver coin auxiliary currency that was prepared a few days ago. At the same time, the Guangzhou Municipal Bank has also issued a two-dime auxiliary currency, scheduled to be issued on the 9th. This auxiliary currency is 4 and a half inches long and 2 and one-half inches wide. The front is printed with a half-length portrait of Sun Yat-sen, and the top is the city emblem. The back is printed with the Pearl River Railway Bridge. After the issuance of the above two silver coin auxiliary currencies, the petty transactions in the market will not be as difficult as on the first day, because there is enough auxiliary currency to replace the two-dime silver coins. In recent days, citizens and businesses have been taking silver coins to provincial and municipal banks to exchange for legal tender in an endless stream. As of the evening of the 8th, provincial and municipal banks had recovered 2 million yuan of silver from the market. Those who registered with the Chamber of Commerce to exchange silver for legal tender also amounted to 1 million yuan. In the future, when silver from various counties and cities is successively concentrated in the provincial capital, the number should also be considerable. At present, the government is actively preparing for the Issuance Preparation Management Committee, which should be established in a few days. Recently, in order to facilitate citizens to exchange silver for legal tender, in addition to extending the business hours of the Provincial Bank to 6:00 PM, it has also entrusted Henglong, Dexing, Taicheng, and other silver shops on Thirteenth Street to exchange on its behalf at the prescribed value. Since the government announced that provincial and municipal silver coin auxiliary currency is legal tender, prices have inevitably increased slightly. According to Article 3 of the currency management measures, silver coins are exchanged for legal tender silver coin auxiliary currency at a rate of 1.20 yuan, so the value of legal tender is only 80% of the value of silver. Therefore, ordinary merchants and citizens have calculated according to this discount. Goods that were usually worth one yuan have recently been increased to 1.20 yuan. At the same time, due to the loss of value of the two-dime silver coin and the lack of auxiliary currency, copper coins have risen in price. Usually, one dime of silver coins can be exchanged for 32 copper coins, but now one dime of legal tender can only be exchanged for 26 copper coins. According to general speculation, once the supply and demand of legal tender correspond and the government cancels the additional purchase of silver coins, prices should return to normal.

After the currency management order was issued, silver shops were concerned about disputes arising from mortgage contracts and closed down for one day. Private banks and post office savings bureaus also closed for one day due to the relationship between legal tender and silver coin transactions, fearing disputes. They also sent staff to the Finance Department to request further announcements of measures to be followed. The Finance Department then issued a notice stating, "According to Article 5 of the six currency management measures announced by this department for implementation, all contracts concluded in silver coin units before November 6 shall be converted to the originally agreed amount and settled in legal tender on the due date." The so-called contracts concluded in silver coin units refer to silver deposit books, silver deposit receipts, and promissory notes of banks and silver shops. Those with opening accounts, which are of a deposit nature, are not included. This has been clearly explained. However, the general public still has doubts about the words "amount" and "contract." Now, we will add an interpretation. For example, if Mr. A deposits 1,000 yuan in a bank or silver shop, or a bank or silver shop lends 1,000 yuan to a business, and the deposits and loans are all in silver coins, then on the due date, they shall be settled with 1,000 yuan of legal tender plus interest (i.e., one yuan of the original silver coin is exchanged for one yuan of legal tender). All other sales, purchase, and loan contracts of businesses and private individuals shall be handled in this way and shall not be obstinate. This is a special announcement. General silver shops, banks, and postal savings bureaus, having received this clear explanation, resumed business on the 8th and posted the above notice. In the future, withdrawals will be paid in legal tender. (November 9th)

Shantou Civil Servants Stealing Silver for Export—Customs Seized People and Evidence

Shantou Correspondence. Since the authorities promulgated the currency reform measures, the East District Pacification Commissioner's Office and the Shantou Municipal Government also received the promulgated measures for punishing the smuggling of silver for export. Those who destroy silver coins will be sentenced to imprisonment for a term of not less than one year but not more than seven years and fined not more than 1,000 yuan. Those who intend to profit by privately transporting silver coins, silver bars, and silver ingots for export will be sentenced to death, life imprisonment, or imprisonment for a term of not less than seven years and fined not less than five times the value of the smuggled goods. This notice was posted throughout the city by the Shantou Municipal Government on the 7th, and the counties of Chaozhou and Meizhou were also instructed to forward and post it to inform all the people. Since the currency reform, silver coins have no longer been used in market transactions, so the prices of silver dollars and silver ingots have plummeted, shrinking by 120 yuan per 1,000 yuan. The Bank of China specially telegraphed its Shanghai headquarters to quickly transport 4 million yuan of legal tender to Shantou for exchange to facilitate circulation. The Provincial Bank also announced that all tax revenues would be based on provincial banknotes as the standard legal tender. The Customs Tax Office has changed to collecting central banknotes. Since silver in the market has depreciated due to its inability to circulate, foreign merchants are absorbing silver to profit in Hong Kong. It is said that 100 yuan can earn more than 30 yuan in profit. Where there is profit, there are many people who smuggle silver for export. On the afternoon of the 8th, the new Customs ship sailed from Shantou to Hong Kong. The customs inspectors searched the ship very thoroughly. Suddenly, they saw a suspicious person boarding the ship. The customs officers immediately searched him. At first, this person was full of official authority. As a result, 80 silver dollars were found on his body. The customs officers initially did not know who he was and planned to take him and the silver to the Customs Office for handling. Unexpectedly, the person raised his head and patted his chest, saying to the customs officers, "Don't you recognize me?" He then showed his badge to the customs officers. He was a civil servant of the Chaozhou-Meizhou Anti-Smoking Bureau. He thought he could rely on his official position to avoid being searched. However, the customs officers said that since he was a civil servant, how could he violate the law? So, they ordered the customs soldiers to take him back to the Customs Office and then send him to the Customs Superintendent's Office for interrogation. The citizens are paying close attention to whether the law will be enforced. It is also heard that this person holds several positions and is also one of the influential figures in Shantou. He coveted this small profit and violated the national law. The government should severely punish him. (9th)

Former Palace Museum Theft Case - Second Instance Concluded - Court Determines Xiao and Liu Committed Criminal Acts

Zhenjiang News: The former Palace Museum theft case was previously interrogated by the Jiangning District Court. Xiao Xiangpei and Liu Guang'e were held responsible for safekeeping. Although the main culprits Yi Peiji and Li Zongtong were at large and unapprehendable for direct confrontation, it was confirmed that Xiao and Liu had committed the crimes of embezzlement and damage. Xiao was sentenced to one year and four months of imprisonment, and Liu to eight months. Xiao and Liu appealed, dissatisfied with the verdict. The High Court designated the Zhenjiang Fifth Branch as the court of second instance and held three hearings. Due to incomplete investigation of witnesses, a fourth hearing was held at 10:00 AM on the 14th, presided over by Wang Jian, the chief judge of the criminal court, with Wu and Jin as assisting judges, and Prosecutor Yun Zhenbang. First, the appellants Xiao and Liu were interrogated about the circumstances of the theft. Xiao and Liu stated that they assumed their posts in the 21st year [of the Republic], and the artifacts were transported to Shanghai in the 22nd year. They were completely unaware of the circumstances at the time. However, each time the seals were opened, police and security teams were present to monitor, and someone was recording. How could there have been any possibility of swapping? The storage rooms were all sealed. When opening the storage, personnel from the Secretariat would jointly handle the process with the police. The keys and opening of the storage were managed by dedicated personnel. During the southward transportation, specialists conducted random checks. When Presidents Yi and Ma handed over their duties, they did not count the inventory of antiquities. They were unaware at the time whether the various jewels, treasures, and paintings were genuine or fake. Therefore, the appellants bear no responsibility whatsoever. Subsequently, the prosecutor read out the reasons for the prosecution, stating briefly that in the 22nd year of the Republic, during the southward transportation of antiquities, the defendants, taking advantage of the transportation, swapped genuine artifacts with fake ones, embezzling public property. After individual interrogation by the investigation court of the Jiangning District Court, it was confirmed that criminal acts had occurred. From various observations, the appellants did commit criminal acts and should still be subject to the original judgment. Finally, Zhao Yaqing and Xiang Guojie, the lawyers of Xiao and Liu, stood up to defend their clients, presenting reasons and requesting the court to consult the inventory of the Palace Museum. The court, considering the reasons presented by the two lawyers as worthy of reference, ordered them to submit written defenses and agreed to consult the inventory. Afterwards, the case was declared concluded, and the sentence was scheduled to be announced at 2:00 PM on the 16th. Xiao was returned to custody, and Liu was released on his original bail. The court adjourned around 1:00 PM.

Suzhou: Public Prostitution Registration Begins Yesterday

Zhang Hanwei, the Chief of the Public Security Bureau, recognizing the prevalence of private prostitution in Suzhou, despite strict prohibitions by the authorities, where the prohibiting continues and the prostitution continues, has decided to implement public prostitution. A public prostitution plan was drafted, designating the area outside the Changmen Gate Road as the public prostitution zone, divided into three classes, with donations levied according to class. The plan was submitted to the Provincial Government for approval. A public prostitution registration office was established within the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau outside the Changmen Gate, appointing Branch Chief Xu Jingqing as the director of the registration office. Registration began on the 15th, with a deadline of one week. The registration fee for the first class is twenty yuan, ten yuan for the second class, and five yuan for the third class. After the registration is completed, it will be sent to the General Bureau for review and examination for venereal diseases, and then business licenses will be issued to start business with hanging signs. It is heard that there are many private prostitutes in Suzhou, totaling approximately five hundred or more. The 15th was the first day of registration, and only dozens of second and third-class prostitutes went to register. The first-class prostitutes (i.e., those who want to be called "changsan") are dissatisfied with the public prostitution measures set by the Public Security Bureau, so no one went to register. They are currently requesting amendments to the measures. The opening date is reportedly December 1st. It is expected that the market outside Jinlumen Gate will develop in the future.

Wuxi: Progress of Repairing Guangqin Road

Guangqin Road in Zhou Shanbang, this county, connects to Xihu Road. It is a necessary route for Xihu buses. The original stone slab surface is severely damaged, uneven, and rugged, making it quite dangerous for vehicles to travel. The Wuxi Station of Xihu Bus Company sent a letter to the County Construction Bureau requesting personnel to investigate and find a way to repair it. Director Zhang, upon receiving the letter, immediately consulted with Wang Zongshan, the director of the Engineering Department of the company, and engineer Xu Shousong. The estimated repair cost is over seven hundred yuan. The Construction Bureau proposed that during the repair period, Xihu buses should not directly reach Xihu Station and should only go as far as the intersection of Xihu Road to facilitate the progress of the project. However, Wang and Xu proposed that the vehicles continue to operate as usual and that the road surface be repaired in two parts to maintain traffic. Wang and Xu have already returned to Shanghai and will report the negotiation to General Manager Wang Xiaolai for a decision. As for the sunken parts of the road, Station Manager Hu of Xihu Station has purchased yellow sand and crushed stones and hired workers to pave and level them to avoid danger.

Hangzhou: Transferring Auxiliary Coins and Copper Coins from Various Counties under Liu's Control

To prevent unscrupulous merchants from speculating and manipulating the auxiliary coins and copper coins on the market and affecting finance, the Hangzhou Municipal Government Chamber of Commerce, the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications had previously agreed on a method of transferring funds under Liu's control and submitted it to the head office for implementation. Considering that the method only applies to Hangzhou City and that the counties still arbitrarily manipulate price fluctuations, and that Shaoxing and Ningbo have remittance relations with Hangzhou, the impact on the money industry is significant. On the 15th, the Qianye representatives of the three provinces of China, China, and Jiaotong convened a meeting again at the Central Bank and decided on the following measures: (1) Each legal tender in each county will be worth 12 jiao of auxiliary coins and 3,000 wen of copper coins. (2) Branches of the three banks may exchange legal tender for legal tender at any time, or exchange legal tender for auxiliary coins and copper coins to avoid surplus or shortage. Those who do not have branches should exchange them at neighboring county branches. (3) The Finance Department, the Chamber of Commerce, and the three banks will separately order the county governments, chambers of commerce, and branches of each county to comply with the measures.

The Southern Yudu section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway project has been rushing to lay steel rails in four sections, and the main part of the project has been completed. However, the bridge project is progressing somewhat slowly. Liangjiadu is expected to be completed on the 25th of this month. The opening ceremony may have to be held on New Year's Day next year.

Scientific Discourse

The Development and Application of the Brain - Edited by the Chinese Science Society

— Lu Yudao

1. The Location of Ingenuity - The Brain

We all know that humans are the most intelligent of all beings. Where exactly is the location of this ingenuity? Three hundred years ago, a French philosopher named Descartes said that the soul resides in a small pineal body (Pinepb Body) in the brain. Vital energy emanates from the pineal body and reaches the entire body through the nerve tubes. Now we know that this is not the case. Our soul does not reside in this small pineal body, nor is our body's movement directed by this small pineal body. Our ingenuity lies in the brain inside the skull. It now seems to be common knowledge that the brain is the master of our behavior.

Flies have little ingenuity because they have no brain. Their brain consists of only a few small ganglia, about one-tenth the size of a millet grain. Fish have a definite brain. For example, the brain of a carp is inside the skull, but it weighs only 0.93 grams. Chickens are slightly higher, with a brain weighing 3.4 grams. We generally agree that chickens are smarter than fish. Why are they smarter? Naturally, because their brain is heavier and larger. Looking at dogs, they can listen to their owners and guard the door, so they are naturally smarter than chickens. Their brain weighs about 100 grams. We humans are the most intelligent of all beings. Humans can conquer everything in the natural world, and their brain is also the heaviest, weighing about 1,400 grams. There are still animals with heavier brains than humans, such as elephants, whose brains weigh 4,660 grams. However, we can imagine that although their body area is eleven times larger than humans, their brain only weighs three times as much. Therefore, in terms of body area, the brain-to-body ratio of elephants is 2.89, while that of humans is 9.4, which is more than three times greater. Therefore, the development of the human brain is evident.

Professor T. Wingate Todd of Cleveland, Ohio, USA, has been carefully measuring the volume of human brains since 1913. He said that the brain volume of ordinary white adults is 1500 c.c. However, the brains of poor people obtained between 1913 and 1917 had a volume of 1480 c.c. By 1918, it had dropped to 1410 c.c. This is strange because in that year, most people went to serve in the army or work, and only the most useless were left behind. After the end of the European War in 1919, all industries stagnated, the army was disbanded, and society could not accommodate so many people, so unemployment increased. The average brain volume of poor people reached 1520 c.c. Social leaders all predicted that the social situation would improve next year. Sure enough, the brain volume in 1920 dropped to the pre-war level. By the following year (1921), all industries had regressed again, and the results rose again to 1550 c.c. From this, it can be seen that in a prosperous society, the brains obtained are smaller, because those with a little ability can find a job, and those left behind have smaller brain volumes. When there are many unemployed people in society, there is a phenomenon of competition for survival, and those with slightly inferior brains are impoverished. Even ordinary people are often unemployed, so the brain volume obtained is also larger. The high and low brain volumes collected by Professor Todd are nothing less than a barometer of the prosperity of society. It can also be seen the relationship between brain volume and intelligence.

2. The Various Parts of the Brain

The most important part of the brain is inside the skull. The skull is like the capital of a country, and an organism is like a country. All events in a country can reach the central government. News from all parts of the human body can also be transmitted to the brain. The transmission is done by many nerves acting as transmission lines. Therefore, every part of our body, from the slightest hair to every part of the viscera, is indirectly connected to the brain by nerves. Those that are commonly in contact with the outside world in the body and those that control the autonomous movement of the flesh are called the cerebrospinal system, while those that control the functions of the viscera are called the sympathetic or autonomic system. The latter is named because the movements of the viscera cannot be controlled autonomously. We can command our fingers and arms to move, but we cannot tell our stomach and intestines how to move or not to move. But whether it is the cerebrospinal system or the sympathetic system, its nerves first pass through the spinal cord (or spinal brain) inside the vertebrae. This is the lowest part of the central nervous system (or brain). There are a total of thirty-one pairs of nerves entering the spinal cord in the human body.

One level higher than the spinal cord is the medulla oblongata or the extended brain. It is located in the lower back of our skull. The nerves that control the sensation and movement of the head, in addition to five pairs of nerves, have seven pairs that all go to this location, and from there go to the brain above. At the same time, the nerve pathways transmitted from the spinal brain and the lines from the upper part of the brain that send commands to the periphery of the body also pass through this location.

Further up are the cerebellum and the pons, these two closely connected areas. The function of the cerebellum has independent properties, namely to control the body's balance and muscle regulation. When we see a friend, we should not shake hands too loosely, but we should not shake them too tightly. The same is true when a mother holds a child. If it is too loose, the child will slip out of her hands, and if it is too tight, the child will suffocate. These are all regulated by the cerebellum. Also, we usually alternate our left and right feet when walking forward. When each foot is raised, the other foot must support the body. This alternating support and balance is also the responsibility of the cerebellum, which ensures that the muscles of the two legs exert force appropriately.

From the cerebellum and pons, there is a small section of the midbrain, which is specifically responsible for visual reflexes such as blinking and auditory reflexes. The visual and auditory reflexes that it controls are all involuntary. Therefore, it is called the visual and auditory reflex center. Lower animals do not appear to be much different from humans in this area. On the contrary, if an eagle's eyes play an important role in its life, then the brain part of the visual reflex center is also particularly developed.

One level above that is the thalamus or interbrain, which is the area where all sensations converge, the emotion center, and the center for controlling the function of the viscera. All the joys, angers, sorrows, and joys of mankind originate from this place.

The highest center of the brain is in the two hemispheres of the cerebrum. All sensations come to this place, all voluntary movement commands originate from this place, all thoughts and creations, all the songs composed by musicians, and all the new inventions of scientists also originate from this place. This is where humans are more intelligent than animals, and where geniuses are more intelligent than ordinary people. The most wonderful thing is that the gray matter on the surface of the hemisphere is only 3mm thick, and this place is full of nerve cells. There are a total of 920 million cells in this place. The human brain is located in the place where these 920 million cells are located.

The brain manages the movements of various parts of the human body, just like the government manages various places. Under the central government, there are provincial governments, under the provincial governments, there are county governments, under the county, there are districts, under the district, there are townships, and under the township, there are villages. The human nervous system is nothing less than a complete political organization. Generally speaking, the spinal brain controls reactions, the medulla oblongata and midbrain control instincts, the cerebellum controls the balance of the body's muscles, the interbrain controls emotions, and the cerebrum controls intelligence.

3. The Development of Brain Function

The above is all about the functions of the various parts of the adult brain. All animals gradually develop from embryo to maturity, and the brain is no exception. Therefore, the brain of a child is very different from the brain of an adult, and its function gradually develops.

The human body takes shape two months after conception. But the heart beats at three weeks, and the gastrointestinal digestive tract has peristalsis at seven weeks. The chest and abdomen can move in the fourth month. These visceral movements occur first, which indicates that the function of the sympathetic autonomic nervous system is first present. In the sixth month, if the fetus is stimulated in the mouth and tongue, it will have a sucking reaction. By the seventh month, the muscles in various parts of the body can have many reactions, such as knee-jerk reflexes and plantar reflexes. However, the tendon reflexes of the upper limbs will have to wait until after birth. By the eighth and ninth months, the muscle reaction is . Usually, it can be felt in the fourth or fifth month. The fetus moves more clearly when it is about to give birth. Not only can the fetus move in the mother's body, but it can also feel. Thirty-one days before a mother was about to give birth, she was washing herself in a bathtub with warm water. A two-year-old child was playing on the ground next to the bathtub. Accidentally, the small glass bottle in his hand hit the edge of the bathtub. The mother was lying down and didn't feel anything, but the fetus in her body suddenly jumped. This shows that the fetus can already hear in the abdomen. The above shows the gradual discovery of the function of the cerebrospinal nervous system.

Not only is the infant so before birth, but its actions also gradually develop after birth. A newborn baby can only lie down and cannot turn over. By the first month, he can lift his head. By the second month, he can lift his chest. By the third month, when lying on his back, he can reach for an object. By the fourth month, he can sit with support. By the fifth month, he can sit on his lap and play with toys. By the sixth month, he can play sitting in a chair. By the seventh month, he can sit on his own without support. By the eighth month, he can stand with support. By the ninth month, he can stand by a chair. By the tenth month, he can crawl. By the eleventh month, he can walk by leading his hand. By the twelfth month, he can stand by pushing furniture on his own. By the thirteenth month, he can climb stairs. By the fourteenth month, he can stand on his own. By the fifteenth month, he can walk on his own. For normal infants with sound development, the development of their movements is generally like this. Later, they learn to speak, learn to write, and grow into adults.

However, the brain parts involved in the various actions mentioned above are too complicated. The study of the development of brain tissue and the development of behavior and movement is more complete in lower animals. Such as cats, guinea pigs, white rats, snails, etc. For example, walking, the entire action naturally includes many nerve molecules. But the most important center is the cerebellum. Goats can walk when they are born, so if you observe their cerebellar cortex at this time, it is also fully developed. Puppies can only walk three weeks after birth, so the cerebellar cortex is not fully developed at birth, and it is fully developed by the third week. People can only walk between the fifteenth and eighteenth months after birth. During these eighteen months, the gradual development of the cerebellar cortex can also be seen. It can be seen the relationship between cerebellar development and walking ability.

In the central nervous system, in addition to the nerve center, there are also nerve pathways that connect various centers, which play an important role. These pathways are composed of nerve fibers. Nerve fibers are covered with a layer of sheath, called the myelin sheath. The development of the myelin sheath in each pathway occurs at different times. Generally, the pathways for functions that develop earlier often have myelin sheaths that develop earlier, and the myelin sheaths of functions that develop later develop later. This also shows the mutual relationship between the development of nerve tissue and nerve function. (To be continued)

British Consulate - Convenes Meeting of Overseas Merchants

Discussing Contractual Obligations - Should Be Paid in Legal Tender

The day before yesterday (Thursday), the British Consul-General convened a meeting of representatives from major British firms and institutions in Shanghai to discuss how to deal with the fact that China has recently implemented currency system reforms, and how to deal with obligations and contracts stipulated in silver or standard currency from the perspective of British people. It was decided that this solution should be considered at length, but for the time being, for any obligations stipulated in Mexican dollars or Chinese standard currency, British people in China should pay in legal tender according to the stipulated amount to avoid any legal problems. Those who attended the meeting that day included representatives from more than ten companies such as HSBC, Chartered Bank, Mercantile Bank, British Bank, British and French Industrial Company, Cathay Land Company, Central Land Company, China International Investment and Trust Company, Hang Yip Land Company, Yih Kwong Land Company, Shanghai Waterworks Company, Asiatic Petroleum Company, British American Tobacco Company, Taikoo Steamship Company, Brunner Mond & Co., Jardine Matheson & Co., Sassoon & Co., and Reiss & Co..

Municipal Government - Prohibits Residents from Moving and Students from Skipping Class

Hopes Citizens Will - Use Common Sense to Judge Rumors - Observe the Situation Calmly

According to the Central News Agency, the Municipal Government, considering that rumors persist despite repeated clarifications and that migrants have been moving in droves in recent days, further unsettling citizens, has ordered the Public Security Bureau to prohibit all residents in the urban area from moving, unless approved by the branch of the Public Security Bureau in charge, otherwise they will be deemed to be disrupting public order. The Municipal Government has also ordered the Education Bureau to order all schools to continue classes as usual and not allow students to ask for leave or leave school without reason, otherwise the school principal will be held accountable. Last night, the person in charge of the Municipal Government reiterated that the shooting incident involving Japanese sailors is being investigated jointly by all parties. The Japanese side has not made any demands except for requesting assistance in the arrest. However, citizens mistakenly believed the rumors, which led to panic and mutual alarm, affecting public order. It should be known that although these rumors are unfounded, they are extremely harmful and spread quickly. Therefore, in addition to strictly investigating and prosecuting those who spread the rumors, the Municipal Government hopes that citizens will use common sense to judge new rumors and observe the situation calmly.

Municipal Bureau of Public Safety: Population Re-Registration Begins Today

Issuing Survey Forms with Deadlines for Completion; Personnel Assigned to Each District for Verification at Any Time

According to Dagongshe, the Municipal Bureau of Public Safety, in order to understand the exact number of households in the city and to prevent undesirable elements from hiding within its borders, has decided to conduct a general population re-registration throughout the city from today until the 30th. Responsible personnel will be assigned to investigate each household by district. A public notice was issued yesterday to inform the public. Public places will be notified separately by the Bureau with attached forms to be filled out. The details are as follows:

Public Notice on Population Re-Registration

The Municipal Bureau of Public Safety issued Public Notice No. 17 (Zheng Zi) regarding the commencement of the general population re-registration in the city, stating: "The Bureau is conducting a re-registration of the city's population. The revised Population Survey Regulations have been submitted to and approved by the Municipal Government and promulgated for implementation. All matters to be prepared for the population re-registration have been arranged separately. It is now set that the period from the 16th to the 30th of this month will be the period for the general population re-registration. In addition to submitting reports and issuing orders separately, this public notice is hereby issued for general information." (Signed) Cai Jingjun, Director of the Bureau. At the same time, in order to urge all householders to fill out the forms conscientiously, the Bureau issued a separate notice stating: "The Bureau has scheduled the period from November 16th to November 30th of this year to conduct a general population re-registration throughout the city. All householders must fill out the population survey form issued by the Bureau within three days of receipt, in accordance with the instructions for filling out the form, item by item, so that the police can collect it. If there are any unclear matters, inquiries can be made at the nearest branch bureau. This matter concerns important household registration policy and must not be delayed. This is a special notice."

Personnel Assigned to Each District

The Bureau considers this survey to be of great importance to future household registration and municipal administration in the city. Therefore, responsible personnel have been carefully selected for each district to form survey teams to investigate each household by district. First, the householders will report themselves, and then verification will be carried out at any time. The leaders of the teams include: Hong Qi, Captain of the General Bureau Team; Li Shenmin, Deputy Captain. The captains of the squadrons in each branch bureau include: Zhu Peizhi, Central District Branch Bureau; Wu Song Yang Haitian; Yunhanbang Luo Jiwu; Jiangwan Li Qingxin; Xinzha Branch Bureau Huang Chongren, Menggu Road Deng Ying, Hengfeng Road Zhang Zhiguang; Zhenru Shi Keshi; North Station Branch Bureau Su Xianxing; North Sichuan Road Ouyang Wei; Yongxing Road He Zhaosen; Linping Road Fu Suchen; Yinxianggang Zhang Xishu; Caojiadu Xing Zhilou; Pusong Lin Naiyou; Xu Hui Hu Qiuqiao; Caojing Wu Zhengding; West Gate Branch Bureau Huang Ti; Old North Gate Wang Jiaan; Wenmiao Wen Yingbiao; Shiliupu Branch Bureau Lin Qishan; Caojiadu Man Qiwei; Yimiao Chen Shuhan; Xundao Street Xu Fenghan; Pudong Branch Bureau Cai Zanzhou; Yangjiadu Lin; Yangjing Zhu Yunsheng; Tangqiao Wang Zhentang; Gaoqiao Branch Bureau Du Chaoqun, Donggou Lu Yongqi. The names of the deputy captains, team leaders, and team members of each squadron are omitted.

Investigation of Public Places

All Chinese and foreign public places in the urban area, such as government offices, military camps, prisons, schools, factories, hospitals, mass organizations, and other institutions, will be notified separately by the Household Registration Section of the Bureau with a Chinese and English survey form and a return envelope, to be filled out and returned within five days. The notice is recorded as follows: "To whom it may concern: In order to ensure the accuracy of household registration statistics, the Bureau is conducting a general population re-registration throughout the city from today. In addition to issuing survey forms and other documents and instructing the police stations to conduct thorough investigations, we are enclosing a survey form for your reference and completion within five days. Thank you." According to Director Li Jingyu of Dagongshe, over 7,500 of these letters have been sent out, and some are still awaiting dispatch.

Points to Note During the Investigation

In addition to investigating the population of each household, investigators will also pay attention to those with certain suspicions, such as: 1. Those suspected of being reactionary; 2. Released prisoners and parolees notified by the prison administration; 3. Those addicted to opium substitutes; 4. Households where idlers often reside or visit; 5. Those with a bad reputation, who wander aimlessly, and who are negatively commented on by neighbors; 6. Those who have suddenly become rich or poor, or whose families have unusual circumstances; 7. Those with secretive movements or occupations that do not match their identities; 8. Dispersed soldiers and vagrants who do not engage in production; 9. Those who usually make rude and extreme statements; 10. Those living in shacks, boat dwellers, mixed-race households, and others with unknown origins and suspicious behavior; 11. Others who are sufficient to endanger public safety or corrupt good morals. All of these will be placed under surveillance.

Recent Developments in International Trade: Hope for Future Balance

According to the Central News Agency, international trade has been quite bleak recently since the outbreak of the Italian-Ethiopian war. In addition, the government's implementation of currency reform has led to a significant reduction in the import of foreign goods due to higher costs. On the export side, only essential raw materials are being traded. Foreign manufacturers are all taking a wait-and-see approach. Reporters learned from the International Trade Bureau in this city that the main export from China recently has been tung oil, while exports of furs and raw silk are still decent. Tea is only being sold to Europe, and there have been recent orders from France, with black tea selling particularly well. With intense competition from various countries, the future is bleak without immediate improvements. Honey tea, made by mixing honey into tea, is currently popular in Europe and America, and all the honey from Chinese farms has been sold out. It is a pity that bee species have not yet been fully perfected. Overall, the recent trade situation suggests that there is hope for a balance in China's foreign trade in the future, and that there will not be a large trade deficit.

Second Cotton Production Estimate Report for This Year Released by the China Cotton Statistics Association

According to the Central News Agency, the China Cotton Statistics Association released its second cotton production estimate report for the country this year yesterday (the 15th) at 5:00 PM: 1. The total area of cotton fields is 35,485,818 mu, the area of abandoned fields is 12,291,300 mu, and the cotton yield is 8,391,018 dan. Compared to the first estimate of this year's yield, it is reduced by 1,205,666 dan, and compared to the actual yield of 1934, it is reduced by 2,810,981 dan. 2. The reduction in cotton field area and yield this year is due to the drought in the Yellow River basin during the sowing season and the floods in the Yangtze River basin in the autumn, which severely damaged cotton fields. During the cotton picking season, the Yangtze River basin also suffered from overcast and rainy weather and insect pests in Jiangsu, so the estimated yield was further reduced compared to the first estimate. The average yield per mu is 23.6 jin, while in 1934 it was 23.9 jin. The harvest this year is generally similar to last year. 3. Among the provinces, Jiangsu has the largest cotton field area this year, with 10 million mu, followed by Hebei with 6.31 million mu, Hubei with 4.56 million mu, Shaanxi with 3.86 million mu, Shandong and Hebei both with 1.7 million mu, Sichuan with 1.9 million mu, Zhejiang with 1.86 million mu, and Shanxi with 1 million mu. The water and drought disasters this year are the most severe in recent history. The area of cotton fields that became abandoned fields due to disasters is 3.97 million mu in Hubei, which is equal to the current area of cotton fields, 3.77 million mu in Shandong, and 3.15 million mu in Henan, both of which are more than double the current area of cotton fields. 4. Among the provinces, Hebei has the largest cotton production this year, with 2.16 million dan, followed by Jiangsu with 2.02 million dan, Hubei and Shaanxi both with 970,000 dan, Zhejiang with 460,000 dan, Henan with 420,000 dan, Shandong with 410,000 dan, Sichuan with 440,000 dan, Anhui with 280,000 dan, and Shanxi with 250,000 dan.

Ministry of Finance Approves Stamp Duty Method for Return Slips

The Ministry of Finance has approved the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's request for instructions on whether to affix stamp duty to return slips and exchange slips, stating: "The telegram and attachments have been received. As the stamp duty law does not stipulate that stamp duty should be paid on return slips, it is not necessary to affix stamps. However, the purple return slip from the China Water Bottle Factory submitted in the telegram, which serves as a receipt issued to customers by the factory after receiving returned goods, should be stamped according to the regulations for receipts for goods. As for exchange slips, if they are only used for exchanging goods, it is not necessary to affix stamps. However, upon examining the exchange slip from the China Water Bottle Factory, which contains a signature area for the recipient, it also has the nature of a receipt and should still be stamped according to the regulations for receipts for goods. The stub can be exempted from stamping according to the precedent. Please instruct accordingly." This is the approval.

Filipino Residents in Shanghai Celebrate the Establishment of the Philippine Independent Government, Telegraphing Respect to President Quezon

Yesterday was the inauguration day of President Quezon, the first president of the Philippine Independent Government. Filipino residents in Shanghai, in their joy, telegraphed the country for celebration, led by Evan Quirest, captain of the Philippine contingent of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps in the International Settlement, and congratulated Quezon on his health. The gist of the telegram is translated as follows: "To President Quezon, We, the people residing in Shanghai, China, together with the people in the Philippines, extend our respect to the President and his staff. Under the President's leadership, we wish the President longevity and health, and the establishment of security and peace at home and abroad, so that we may live among free and respected nations in the modern world. President, we wish the government of our country and the President unlimited prospects." The Philippine contingent of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps was formed in 1927, originally attached to the American contingent. It was formally established in 1932 and has been in existence ever since.
