Silk Industry Appeals for Negotiations with France: Vietnam Imposes Heavy Import Taxes on Chinese Silk. Previously Only Regular Taxes, Now Additional Taxes Added When No Treaty Existed. Currently, Besides Regular Taxes and Additional Taxes, a Balance Tax is Also Added.

The Shanghai Electrical Silk Weaving Factory Industry and the Silk Satin Industry Associations have jointly stated that they have repeatedly received urgent letters from the Annam Touan and Xiti Silk Satin Industry Associations, stating that since the announcement of the Sino-French-Vietnamese treaty, the import tax rate levied by Vietnam on Chinese silk has not only failed to enjoy preferential tax reductions as stipulated in the treaty, but is actually heavier than the tax rate when there was no treaty. Furthermore, many tax items have been cleverly created, and arbitrary valuations and heavy levies are imposed. The associations believe that the supplementary table of the commercial treaty stipulates that Chinese silk exported to Vietnam should enjoy the lowest tax rate to show reciprocity. However, the Vietnamese customs are now imposing arbitrary and heavy levies, which violates the spirit of reciprocity. The export of Chinese silk to Vietnam is likely to be completely eliminated. The chairmen of the two industry associations, Cha Shengbai and Luo Qinghua, immediately reported the situation to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting serious negotiations with the French government to help the export of Chinese silk. The original report is recorded as follows:

Request for Negotiations

The report is regarding the fact that after the announcement and implementation of the Sino-French-Vietnamese treaty, Chinese silk exported to Vietnam should enjoy the lowest tax rate as stipulated in the supplementary table. However, the Vietnamese customs are now creating tax items cleverly, arbitrarily valuing goods, and imposing heavy levies, which are even heavier than the taxes levied when there was no treaty. Overseas Chinese merchants are suffering greatly, and the sales of Chinese silk have been cut off. The report is urgently submitted, requesting a prompt and serious negotiation with the French government to abolish any supplementary taxes other than those stipulated in the commercial treaty, in order to comply with the principle of reciprocity and help the country's foreign trade. It is noted that the import of Chinese silk to Annam before 1726 amounted to more than 10 million yuan per year. Since the Qing Dynasty, when China and Annam signed a commercial treaty, Chinese silk enjoyed the most-favored-nation tax rate. Therefore, the sales of silk to Vietnam at that time were particularly prosperous. In July 1929, the Sino-Vietnamese commercial treaty expired, and the import of Chinese silk had to be treated in the same way as ordinary taxes for countries without a treaty. In the past, only one type of regular tax was levied on Chinese silk. However, in addition to the regular tax, an additional establishment tax (similar to the business tax in our country) had to be levied. From then on, the burden on overseas Chinese increased, and the sales of Chinese silk were greatly affected. In 1930, Wang Qian, the Minister of Foreign Affairs of our country, and French Minister Ma De negotiated a special treaty. However, due to the relationship between the two types of supplementary tables, A and B, the French side delayed approval, which has been suspended for several years. During this period, the export of Chinese silk to Vietnam was almost completely cut off, and the business of overseas Chinese and the export of silk merchants in the country both suffered. On May 4th of this year, the Sino-French-Vietnamese treaty was fortunately announced. With the continued export of Chinese silk to Vietnam, it was expected that the old foundation would be restored. However, urgent letters were repeatedly received from the Annam Tuan and Xiti Silk Satin Industry Associations, stating that since the announcement of the commercial treaty, the Vietnamese customs have levied import tax rates on Chinese silk that have not only failed to be reduced, but have actually increased compared to when there was no treaty. Furthermore, many names have been cleverly created, and arbitrary and heavy levies have been imposed. Taking Chinese silk as an example, only regular tax was levied in the old treaty to show preferential treatment. Later, when there was no treaty, ordinary tax rates were applied, so in addition to the regular tax, an establishment tax was also levied. Now that the new treaty has been established, the establishment tax should be abolished in order to comply with the principle of reciprocity. However, recently, the Vietnamese customs have not only failed to remove the establishment tax, but have also added a balance tax, which is 25% of the assessed value. For example, the import of 100 kilograms of crepe-faced, lightweight, dyed pure silk fabric into Annam is subject to the following comparison of new and old tax rates: A. Tax rate under the old treaty: Regular tax: 1,360 francs. B. Tax rate when there was no treaty: Regular tax: 10,000 francs; Establishment tax: 900 francs; Total: 10,900 francs. C. Tax rate after the recent announcement of the commercial treaty: Regular tax: 8,500 francs; Establishment tax: 537.5 francs; Balance tax: 2,250 francs; Total: 11,287.5 francs. According to the above example, it can be proven that after the new treaty was signed, the Vietnamese customs' import tax rate on Chinese silk was not only heavier than the tax levied under the old treaty, but also increased more than the ordinary tax rate when there was no treaty. Although the added balance tax is said to be 25% of the value, it is assessed based on the exchange rate, which is actually arbitrarily inflated and has no standard. Sometimes it is even as high as 50%. The establishment tax is calculated by combining all costs and taxes paid, and then re-evaluating the value, which is like adding a bed on top of a bed, taxing taxes within taxes. Therefore, the total amount of import tax paid for Chinese silk is generally between 100% and 150% of the value. With such heavy taxation and extortion, overseas Chinese merchants cannot bear the burden. If Chinese silk wants to be exported to Vietnam, its vitality will inevitably be cut off. The associations are greatly distressed and cannot remain silent. They dare to truthfully report the situation, hoping that the departments concerned will investigate and approve, and request that the French government be seriously negotiated with, and that all supplementary taxes not stipulated in the main treaty and supplementary table be stopped from being levied by the Vietnamese side, and that it must be guaranteed that no cleverly created tax items will be arbitrarily levied in the future. The regular tax levied should also be noted and should not be higher than the import tax for non-reciprocal countries, in order to comply with the principle of the lowest tax rate in the supplementary table, so as to realize the spirit of reciprocity in the commercial treaty. If the French side delays and ignores the negotiations, then our government may also levy additional taxes on goods such as coal and rice transported from Annam to our country to show retaliation. Whether this is appropriate or not is up to you to decide. I am waiting anxiously for orders. In addition to the attached table comparing tax rates, this is presented respectfully.

Explanation: (1) From May 1926, the tax was increased from 200 francs to 800 francs per 100 kilograms. After October of the same year, it was increased to 1,360 francs. (2) From July 1929, in addition to the regular tax mentioned above, an establishment tax of 2% of the value was added. The lowest estimated value was 18,000 francs per 100 kilograms, and the tax was 360 francs per 100 kilograms. (3) In July 1929, the Sino-French commercial treaty expired, and our country lost the most-favored-nation tax rate and was treated at the ordinary rate for countries without a treaty. (4) In January 1933, the establishment tax was again increased to 5% of the value. (5) On August 8, 1935, the new tax rules were implemented. The regular tax was slightly reduced, but the establishment tax was not canceled, and the French side established a separate item called the balance tax. Combining the various tax items, there was no reduction, and the tax was actually heavier than when there was no treaty.

Boy Scouts' Internal Fundraising a Success

The floods this year have caused severe disasters in the Zhongting, Guanhe, and Han rivers. The severity of the disaster is even worse than that of 1931. The disaster area covers dozens of provinces, and the number of victims exceeds millions. They are displaced and suffering unspeakable hardships. People from all walks of life are donating to help to the best of their ability to contribute to relief efforts. Although there are many people who do this, it is difficult to be comprehensive with such limited resources. The Water Disaster Relief Association in this city, due to the severity of the disaster and the urgency of relief efforts, has not only appealed for donations from all parties, but has also held various entertainment events to allocate all income to relief efforts. In addition, it has also held two types of fundraising: Boy Scout fundraising and general water disaster fundraising. The Boy Scouts' external fundraising has already been stopped, and their internal fundraising will also end in just two days. According to the person in charge of the Boy Scout Council, the income from this general mobilization of Boy Scout fundraising has been very satisfactory, and the amount should be in the tens of thousands of dollars. The detailed official figures will be announced as soon as the units of each regiment of soldiers have paid their dues. Within these two days, people from all walks of life are still encouraged to enthusiastically donate and make a final effort to help the disaster victims. In addition, the general water disaster fundraising organized by the Fundraising Group of the Association has been enthusiastically supported by various fundraising companies and stores, and the results have been excellent. Yesterday, the Association received 1,000 yuan from an old woman named Qiujiu, and Mr. Jiang Zhongquan collected 131.98 yuan from eight households, including Jiu Jun.

Japanese Troops Withdraw Guard Soldiers from Yesterday Onward: Remarks of the Staff Officer of the Japanese Marine Corps in Shanghai

Japan United News Agency (Shanghai, 15th) reported that after the shooting death of a Marine Corps sailor, soldiers were originally stationed to guard the scene of the incident and its vicinity. Now that the investigation of the case has come to an end, it is feared that this may help to incite the public, so it has been decided to withdraw the guard soldiers from today onward. According to the staff officer of the team, after the incident occurred, the team immediately dispatched troops to guard the scene of the incident and its vicinity, and established close contact with the police authorities to make efforts to search for the murderer and collect evidence. However, now that the investigation of the scene of the incident and its vicinity has come to an end, it will be possible to vigorously organize evidence from other aspects. Therefore, at this time, the guard soldiers should be withdrawn immediately.

Shareholders Meeting

The Nantong Dasheng No. 1 Textile Company, due to more than one-third of the directors being vacant due to resignations and the remaining also resigning, convened a temporary shareholders meeting at the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association at 2 p.m. yesterday. Jin Xing Real Estate Company Held Creditors' Meeting Yesterday - Bankruptcy Administrator Reports on Receivership - Election of Three Supervisors to Oversee Progress

According to the Hua Dong News Agency, after the Jin Xing Real Estate Business Company, operated by Sun Chunsheng, was declared bankrupt by the First Special District Court on October 17, Xie Lin (accountant) and Liu Shifang (lawyer) were appointed as bankruptcy administrators. A bankruptcy creditors' meeting was convened yesterday at 1 p.m. at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA to elect supervisors to oversee the bankruptcy administrators in managing the bankruptcy affairs. The details are as follows:

Creditors Present

Excluding special claims of 6,601,668.84 yuan which did not need to be present, the creditors present yesterday included representatives from Xin Fu Qian Zhuang, Central Trust Company, Rui Chang Sheng Qian Zhuang, Hong Feng Qian Zhuang, Zhi Zhong Bank, Heng Long Tai Ji Zhuang, Zi Kang Zhuang, Hong Sheng Fu Ji Zhuang, the Municipal Council, Wu Peng, and others, a total of ten representatives, representing 104,965.28 yuan. This accounted for more than half of the total claims from 18 creditors, amounting to 200,086.97 yuan, and met the legal quorum.

Chairman's Report

The meeting was chaired by Judge Yu Lude of the First Special District Court. Liu Shifang and Xie Lin reported. After the formalities, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that after the Jin Xing Real Estate Company was declared bankrupt by the court, excluding over 610,000 yuan of special claims not restricted by bankruptcy law, the remaining over 200,000 yuan of ordinary claims would be subject to the appointment of bankruptcy administrators for receivership in accordance with bankruptcy law, which has been completed. The creditors' meeting was now convened to report on the progress and to elect supervisors to oversee the process. Bankruptcy administrator Xie Lin then reported on: (1) the receipt of the company's books, documents, and property; (2) the claims filed by the creditors; (3) it was found that Sun Chunsheng's investment in the bank had transferred the shares to his wife Shao Zhen's name, and a request had been filed with the court for provisional attachment; (a total of two items); (4) according to reports from various households, the real estate was originally entrusted to Jin Xing Real Estate Company for leasing, but due to Jin Xing's bankruptcy, it was declared that the entrustment should be revoked and could not be included in the bankruptcy estate; (a total of nine items); (5) the bankruptcy administrator's income and expenditure; (6) the furniture received was valued by the Yi Zhong Auction House and is proposed to be auctioned immediately; (7) Jin Xing Company is an unlimited liability company organization and holds an unlimited liability company registration license from the Ministry of Industry; (8) Lawyer Murakami sent a letter regarding the Jin Xing Building used by Jin Xing Company, requesting the house and outstanding rent.

Election of Supervisors

Three supervisors were then elected by ballot. The results were the Central Trust Company, Hong Feng Qian Zhuang, and Zi Kang Qian Zhuang were elected. Finally, Xie Lin explained the matters to be carried out in the future. The creditors proposed that the supervisors hand them over to the bankruptcy administrator to proceed in accordance with the law. The meeting adjourned at 3:30 p.m.

Jin Shou Lane - Tenants Request Rent Reduction Based on Precedent

The houses in Jin Shou Lane on Shandong Road, located between Wuma Road and Wuhu Road west of Shanglin Street, are owned by the wealthy merchant Xi Hehan and managed by Taili Foreign Firm. The tenants of the lane, noting that landlords in neighboring areas have successively implemented rent reductions, with documented cases, have repeatedly gathered to request the owner to consider the merchants' difficulties and reduce the rent by 30%. However, the management office has been evasive and no agreement has been reached. Therefore, yesterday, the third lane-wide tenants' meeting was held at the South District Branch of the Municipal Association. The association has repeatedly sent letters through representatives to the management office requesting rent reduction, but there has been no response and no rent collection. The methods to be discussed should be proposed. The public resolved as follows: (1) Request a 30% rent reduction starting from September, and will not stop until the goal is achieved; (2) Engage lawyer Jiang Chiping as the association's legal advisor; (3) If the landlord does not collect the rent at 70%, all tenants will affix the association's seal and deposit the rent in the bank for safekeeping; (4) All tenants who receive lawyer's letters from the management office demanding rent or encounter legal disputes should report to the association so that the association's legal advisor can handle them; (5) Every five tenants will elect one representative to be responsible for handling disputes, which should be reported to the representative for the association to review and handle.

Nine Issuing Banks Guarantee Reserves, Central, China, and Communications Banks Separately Take Over

According to the Guowen News Agency, after the Ministry of Finance issued a bulletin on currency system reform on the 4th of this month, the cash reserves of various banks and money shops have been checked and sealed by officials dispatched by the Ministry of Finance, or sold to the three banks. As for the nine banks issuing banknotes, their issuance reserves, consisting of 60% cash and 40% assets, have also been ordered by the Ministry of Finance to be taken over by the three banks. The details are as follows:

Central, Communications Banks Take Over, Nine Banks Guarantee

After the Central, China, and Communications Banks were ordered to take over the issuance reserves of the nine banks issuing banknotes, consisting of 60% cash and 40% assets, the three banks, together with the Issuance Reserve Management Committee, decided on the takeover methods and allocated the takeover responsibilities. The Central Bank took over the China Agricultural and Industrial, China South, and Agricultural and Commercial Banks. The Bank of China took over the Siming, China Industrial, and China Farmers Banks. The Communications Bank took over the China Reclamation, China General Chamber of Commerce, and Zhejiang Xingye Banks. As for the 60% cash in the issuance reserves, due to the difficulty of transporting it and the frequent use of legal tender by the Central, China, and Communications Banks, and the scarcity of one-yuan legal tender notes, the cash will not be temporarily exchanged for legal tender. It will be temporarily sealed in the vaults of the respective banks.

40% Guarantee, Interest Paid Monthly

As for the 40% guarantee in the issuance reserves, which consists of government bonds, treasury bills, and other guaranteed assets, it has now been transferred to the Central, China, and Communications Banks for safekeeping. It is reported that interest must be paid monthly on these assets. A calculation will be made at the end of the month. However, among the 40% asset guarantees of the nine banks, there are items mortgaged to outsiders. If the debtor repays the loan and requests the return of the mortgaged item, it can be exchanged with the three banks at any time.

Branches and Sub-branches, Ministry Orders Separate Handling

As for branches and sub-branches in various regions, the Ministry of Finance has separately instructed the local authorities to handle them separately. For example, in Tianjin, Hankou, and Guangdong, branch committees of the Issuance Reserve Management Committee have been established. In nearby areas, the Management Committee will determine methods for joint management. However, the specific methods have not yet been fully determined.

Local Banks Not Yet Taken Over

In addition, such as Zhejiang Local Bank, in addition to the Ministry of Finance sending personnel to check the cash reserves on the 4th of this month, as for the issuance of banknotes, because the bank is provincial in nature, it is reported that the Ministry of Finance has issued separate orders for handling, so it is not included in the three banks' takeover list.

Clearing Methods, Slight Changes

According to past practice, banks had to send each other the banknotes of other banks they received every evening. Since the 4th of this month, the banknotes of other banks received by the Central, China, and Communications Banks have not been returned separately, but have been replaced by legal tender for circulation. The other nine banks, such as Bank A, do not need to exchange all the banknotes of Banks B and C, but can hand them over to the three banks for clearing or add them to their interbank savings accounts. (Note: The clearing of the Banking Industry Preparedness Committee's clearing house every evening involves various bills, which are not related to banknotes.)

Shangchuan Transportation Company Extends Chuannan Railway - Survey Completed, Track Laying Begins - Expected to Reach Zhujiaqiao This Winter

According to the Guowen News Agency, the Shangchuan Transportation Company was initiated and organized by Huang Yanpei, Gu Lanzhou, and others in 1924, with a capital of 400,000 yuan. It has built a light railway from Shanghai to Chuansha, a total length of 21 kilometers. It has been in operation for ten years. The railway has three large locomotives, six small locomotives, and sixteen passenger cars. The entire railway employs a total of 120 people. The annual operating income is about 200,000 yuan. After paying annual interest of 1% or 8-9% and employee salaries, food, office expenses, coal, repairs, etc., there is sometimes a surplus. Starting this year, after a resolution by the shareholders' meeting, a plan was approved to extend the original Shangchuan Line, passing through Nanhui to Daduan Town, a length of 28 kilometers, with a budget of 600,000 yuan. In addition to the board of directors and old shareholders undertaking a portion, the rest will be raised through new shares. Surveying began in March of this year and has been completed. Construction has already begun, and earthwork has been laid to Zhujiaqiao in Nanhui County. 100,000 sleepers and 100 tons of steel rails have been purchased from the United Kingdom and Germany, and are expected to arrive in Shanghai this month, and track laying will begin immediately. It is hoped that a section will be completed this winter and opened to traffic. All locomotives and passenger cars will be temporarily used from the original ones. Once the business develops in the future, carriages will be added and gradually expanded.

Jinghu Railway and Zhuan Steamboat Bureau Handle Passenger Joint Transport - Revised Contract Term of One Year

The Jinghu Railway and Zhuan Steamboat Bureau have been handling passenger joint transport for many years. The original contract has expired. A revised standard joint transport contract of fifteen articles was signed last month, with a term of one year. The designated joint transport stations, on the railway side, are Shanghai North, Nanxiang, Kunshan, Suzhou, Wuxi, and other five stations. On the steamboat bureau side, they are Baihegang, Qingpu, and Zhujiage, three ports. Joint transport tickets are valid for the day of issue. For accompanied baggage exceeding the free weight, the railway charges two cents per kilometer per 20 kilograms, while the steamboat bureau charges five cents. The loading and unloading from the station to the steamboat or from the steamboat to the station is handled by the railway bureau's stevedores, charging twelve copper coins per piece, which is shared by both parties in proportion to the total joint transport income from passenger baggage, without additional charges to passengers.

Health Bureau Implements Compulsory Vaccination Starting Yesterday - Expected to be Assisted by Public Security Bureau Police in One Month

According to the Daily News, in view of the uneven temperatures in the city after entering winter, which can easily lead to the spread of smallpox, and the only good way to prevent it is to vaccinate with cowpox, the Municipal Health Bureau sent personnel to various primary and secondary schools in the South Shanghai and Zhabei districts starting on the first of last month to administer free cowpox vaccinations. The bureau has also determined that the city's area is vast, the population is complex, and the general working class lacks health knowledge and does not know how to prevent it. Therefore, after consultation with the Public Security Bureau, it was decided that, starting yesterday (the 15th), a large number of health officers will be dispatched to form teams with the police of the Public Security Bureau to go to the city's shack areas to compulsorily administer free vaccinations. In addition, the bureau will dispatch multiple health vehicles to the main roads and administer vaccinations along the way. The date is scheduled for one month, in the hope that all citizens of the city will be able to get vaccinated for prevention in a short period of time, so that smallpox will no longer be possible to occur.

Qinmei Brothel - Who is the Procuress? - Prostitutes' Statements Contradict - Younger Sister Loses Virginity, Difficult to Marry - Yang Baosheng Charged Case Concludes

Qinmei Old Nine, a prostitute at Qinmei Brothel No. 5 Fuyu Lane, Beihai Road, whose original name was Song Xiaodi (also known as Huihua, daughter of Song Guisheng of Chuansha, 19 years old), was pawned by her father to the procuress Yang Baosheng (also known as Yang Shengji) of the brothel in 1932 for 500 yuan. Ostensibly, she was a fostered daughter, but in reality, she was a prostitute. Recently, unable to bear the procuress's abuse, she voluntarily escaped from the brothel and, together with her father Song Guisheng, filed a criminal complaint against Yang Baosheng for harming social customs, requesting legal action and demanding compensation of 3,000 yuan. The case had been gathered once by the First Special District Court, and it was reported in the newspapers. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Jiang Shuzi convened a new trial of both parties. Many prostitutes from the brothel district came to court to listen. The court first questioned the defendant Yang Xiansheng, but the procuress denied that the Qinmei Brothel was opened by her. She said that the owner of the brothel was Zhou Lao San, and Song Xiaodi was a fostered daughter. Although Song Guisheng had repeatedly asked to send Xiaodi to the brothel to work as a prostitute, because Xiaodi's voice was not wide enough and she could not learn songs, she was never allowed to engage in prostitution. Zhou Lao San once borrowed 1,000 yuan from her, and she occasionally ordered Xiaodi to go to the brothel to collect money, but never for prostitution. The court then questioned Zhou Lao San, who admitted that he was the owner of the brothel at No. 5 Fuyu Lane. When asked about the brothel's name, he was initially at a loss. After thinking for a while, he claimed that it was Qinmei, and said that there was only one prostitute in the brothel named Liu Bao, and Xiaodi was not among them. The court then summoned Liu Bao, who testified that she worked as a prostitute at No. 5, and Xiaodi only came to collect interest occasionally. According to the plaintiff Song Xiaodi's testimony, she had been forced by the defendant to work as a prostitute for more than three years, under the name Qinmei Old Nine. At that time, the plaintiff's representative lawyer presented a small newspaper, saying that the flower selection news had a photo of Xiaodi. If she was not a prostitute, she would not be listed in the flower selection. In addition to Xiaodi and Liu Bao, the No. 5 brothel also had Lao Er, Lao San, Didi, and Er Yuanyuan, who were currently sitting in the audience and could be summoned for questioning. Unexpectedly, the four prostitutes sitting in the audience, except for Lao Er, who remained motionless, the other three prostitutes unexpectedly left the courtroom. Judge Jiang immediately ordered the court clerks to summon those people back and question them one by one. Lao Er admitted that she worked as a prostitute at No. 5 and said that the brothel was indeed opened by the procuress Yang. Xiaodi's nickname was Qinmei Old Nine, and Liu Bao and others were sisters. Zhou Lao San was not the procuress, and Zhou's statement was false. However, the testimony of the three prostitutes Didi and others differed greatly from that of Xu Lao Er, saying that Yang was not the procuress and Xiaodi was not a prostitute in the brothel. The court then questioned Xiaodi again, who claimed that they were originally the same as her and had to leave the hall on business, but in order to rely on Yang for a living, they had to agree with her and say these insincere words. She was really unbearable to be abused and left the brothel on September 24. According to Song Guisheng's testimony, my daughter was to be a fostered daughter with Yang, and the 500 yuan was a loan from her. At first, he did not know that his daughter was being forced into prostitution after being fostered. Now that my daughter's chastity has been lost, it is difficult for her to marry, which will ruin her life. Therefore, I request that the defendant be punished and order her to compensate for the loss of 3,000 yuan. Finally, after mutual debate by the lawyers of both parties, the court adjourned to be pronounced next Friday afternoon.

Strange Female Corpse Case: Judge Arrives for On-Site Investigation, Witnesses Provide Detailed and Truthful Testimony; Hao Zhongyang Reenacts Details of What He Saw; Clerk Records and Creates Diagrams

On the afternoon of August 3rd of this year, when the Shengjing steamship was raising anchor to depart from the Taikoo Wharf No. 3 in the French Concession, the propeller's movement brought up the naked lower body of a strange female corpse, Zhang Jinlin, from the river. The corpse's aunt, Zhang Zhoushi, identified the body and arranged for a coffin. The case caused a sensation in society at the time. Subsequently, the Procuratorate of the District Court arrested Qiao Qishi, a female major suspect in the case. Prosecutor Xie Lian interrogated her, and she was prosecuted in the Criminal Division on the charge of joint murder. Judge Wu Xiangzu conducted two trials, details of which have been reported in previous newspapers. Judge Wu believed that the case involved significant discrepancies. The defendant, Qiao Qishi, vehemently protested her innocence and denied being present at the scene, while the testimony of the witness, Hao Zhongyang, was detailed and seemed unlikely to be fabricated. Believing that a thorough on-site investigation was necessary to clarify the truth and avoid any injustice, the judge scheduled a personal on-site inspection. Yesterday morning at 10 AM, Judge Wu Xiangzu, along with Clerk Fan Shengyang, and defense attorney Fang Junjie, accompanied witness Hao Zhongyang and traveled by car to Taikoo Wharf No. 3 for an on-site investigation. This reporter, wishing to understand the actual situation at the time, also drove to the scene. Judge Wu disembarked upon arrival and first carefully observed the area around the wharf. (Note: Wharf No. 3 has two floating bridges, north and south, connected to an outer floating pier, with a high wharf in the middle, usually used to stack bamboo exports.) Then, Hao Zhongyang led them to the northern floating bridge and pointed out that around 10 PM that night, a yellow car came from the north and stopped here (at the base of the northern floating bridge). The two men, three women, and one girl who got out of the car walked from the southern floating bridge to the floating pier and boarded the Shengjing steamship to play for a while. Then they returned to the southern end of the floating pier, spread newspaper on the springboard placed on the pier, sat down, and ate watermelon seeds while chatting. At that time, I was on the high wharf, gambling at pai gow with eight or nine companions. We saw them chatting and laughing happily, and my companions clapped their hands and joined in. Later, I suddenly saw a man take off a woman's pants. I thought they were messing around. Thinking that seeing this would bring bad luck, I went to sleep on the refrigerator on the floating bridge pier. Suddenly, I heard a child scream for help and the sound of water in the river. I immediately got up and rushed to the southern end of the floating pier to see what was happening (note: the refrigerator is about fifty steps from the southern pier side). I planned to grab some bamboo from the pile on the high wharf to try and rescue her, but a man glared at me and knocked me down." The judge asked how old the girl was and what time it was. Hao replied that the girl was about six or seven years old, and the time was one and three-quarters past one o'clock on the New Customs clock. He also pointed out that Qiao Qishi was standing on the southern end of the pier, facing the southern floating bridge (note: the Shengjing steamship happened to have arrived yesterday and was docked there). According to Hao, the deceased fell into the river near the side of the southern end of the floating pier, not the outer barrier. Hao Zhongyang recounted the events in vivid detail, and Clerk Fan Shengyang drew a diagram. The judge then dismissed Hao Zhongyang and instructed him to await further summons. They then returned to the court by car.

Despite the wind and rain, it was still very crowded with visitors. At the entrance of the venue, there was a memorial archway made of pine and cypress, inscribed with a horizontal plaque that says: "Shanghai Second Horticultural Exhibition," with a couplet on the side that reads: "Beauty and wealth gathered in the botanical garden, collecting a variety of fragrances in one record; dignified display of art and planting, happily integrate the letters of summer to inspire sprout culture." The aisle inside the gate was wide, planted with Chinese arborvitae on both sides, interspersed with various flowers. In the midst of greenery, red and purple blossoms were vibrant and dazzling, creating a refreshing atmosphere. To the west, there was a shaded canopy, with hundreds of varieties of famous chrysanthemums from the botanical garden in the center, and a greenhouse, with exotic goldfish from the Golden Fish Paradise, Angora wool rabbits from the Minsheng Chicken Farm, and Lida ducks from the Chicken Farm, all rarely seen in Shanghai. Behind the greenhouse, there was a small stream. Walking north along the stream, one reached the second gate of the venue, next to a couplet that reads, "Bamboo rhymes with maple red, vegetables and fruits compete for beauty, mountains surround water, pine and cypress are evergreen." Inside the second gate, there were rolling hills, with magnificent upright chrysanthemums arranged at the foot of the hills, which was particularly spectacular. In the center of the venue, there was a thatched cottage, titled "Abundance," with a couplet that reads, "Objects compete for novelty, scarlet, yellow, red and purple, flowers and fruits are abundant, tree art and botanical garden." The beams and pillars in the hall were all painted with vermilion lacquer, which, together with various horticultural flowers, created an interesting effect. The exhibits were arranged in a circular pattern, and the exhibits included fruit trees, vegetables, local goods, fruits, etc., which were extremely exquisite. Fragrant flowers swirled and fallen petals fluttered about, making the scene nothing short of an earthly paradise. As of yesterday morning, there were more than sixty exhibitors, including the Native Produce Trade Association, the Fruit Trade Association, Canadian Greenhouse Planting Farm, Dongda Farm, Dahua Farm, Shisen Farm, Guanshengyuan, China Chemical Industry, Huang's Livestock Planting Farm, Xiangshun Garden, Gu Lanji, and Zhiyulu. In the southeast, there were separate rooms for displaying various specimens, with more than ten exhibitors including Shanghai Municipal Agricultural Experiment Farm, Xinlu Normal School, Fisheries Guidance Institute, and Potassium Fertilizer Company. In the central office area, there was a calligraphy and painting room for celebrities and scholars to create works for guests. There were also various prizes to be awarded to the exhibitors after review. One expects that if the weather is clear, the number of visitors will be even greater.

Chinese Buddhist Society Establishes Shanghai Branch

The Chinese Buddhist Society was established in the capital in 1929 by Grand Master Taixu and lay Buddhists Mei Jieyun, Xie Zhuchen, Tao Ye, Peng Yangguang, Yao Yuping, and others. It is now reported that Shanghai Buddhist comrades Zhang Jingjiang, Shen Zhongjun, Xi Guansheng, Chen Qinsheng, Li Zifeng, Zhang Xiaoxing, Zhong Hengping, Feng Ciming, Wu Yongchang, and others, in order to study and promote Buddhist theories, have established an office inside the Xuedou Temple on Dongyouheng Road in Hongkou under the guidance of Master Taixu, chairman of the General Association. They have been preparing until now, and the organization has been established. The establishment has been approved and recorded by the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Education Bureau. It is now scheduled to hold an inaugural meeting at the auditorium of the association on November 17th at 1 PM, under the guidance of party and government agencies.

Completion of the Construction Industrial Materials Testing Laboratory of the Chinese Institute of Engineers; Ministry of Railways Approves a Subsidy of 50,000 Yuan

The Industrial Materials Testing Laboratory built by the Chinese Institute of Engineers in the city center has been completed. However, due to the lack of complete internal equipment and testing materials, it has not yet opened. According to reports, the funds for the laboratory's layout are estimated at 100,000 yuan. Various foreign manufacturers have donated funds one after another, but the amount is still far short. The institute had previously consulted with the Ministry of Railways, arguing that the Ministry's original laboratory was rarely used, and requesting a subsidy of 50,000 yuan for the institute's expenses. In the future, if there were testing materials, the institute could test them for free. Minister Gu and Vice Minister Zeng have approved the request, and the funds will be allocated in the coming days. Once the layout is complete, the laboratory can be opened.

Preparatory Office of the Fish Market Concluded Yesterday; Will Open Immediately After the Appointment of Directors and Supervisors

According to the Central News Agency, after the completion of the Shanghai Fish Market Building of the Ministry of Industry, the organizational law and other regulations of the office were also drafted separately and submitted to the Ministry for approval. The preparatory work has been completed, so the preparatory office concluded yesterday. It will be formally opened immediately after the Ministry of Industry appoints directors, supervisors, managers, and assistant managers. The organizational content is reported as follows:

Organizational Content

The organizational law of the fish market has been submitted to the Ministry for approval. The highest authority is the Board of Directors, and a Board of Supervisors will be established to supervise the operation. The General Manager, with the resolutions of the Board of Directors, will carry out the business, under which there will be a Manager and an Assistant Manager. Under them are three departments: General Affairs, Business, and Technology, as well as a Secretariat and an Accounting Department. As for the staff, it is said that they will be filled by the preparatory personnel respectively, and no new employees will be hired to save expenses. The list of directors is expected to be announced in the coming days, and the Board of Directors will be convened to discuss progress.

Department Arrangements

After the completion of the department houses in the market, the internal layout has also been completed. There are three floating piers, a total of 600 meters long, connected by five iron bridges. The length of the pier can accommodate multiple large fishing vessels at the same time. The warehouse construction, the cold storage is on the right rear of the shore, and the four walls are currently under construction, along with the installation of refrigeration machines and ice-making machines. It is expected to be completed one month later. The curved brokerage offices are on the left rear, with more than 100 offices in total, rented out for use as offices by fish merchants. In the center is the auction site and office, the entire building is shaped like a ship, and the prominent rudder tower has five floors. A wireless radio station and a weather station will be set up at the highest point, but construction has not yet begun. Tracks are currently being laid in various parts of the market to facilitate transportation, and iron hopper cars will be used to transport fresh fish, etc.

International Trade Bureau Compiles National Commercial Directory; Ready for Publication Soon

According to the Central News Agency, in order to understand the national commercial situation and statistics of Chinese and foreign commercial banks, the International Trade Bureau specially compiled a national commercial directory. The work has been underway for half a year and has been completed. According to reports, the book covers the organization, capital, types, and business conditions of domestic Chinese and foreign commercial banks. Except for a small number of organizations that are not sound, which have been cancelled, there are still more than 1,500 listed in the book. It is expected to be published in the coming days and will be an important reference book for the industrial and commercial sectors in the future.

Car Runs onto Sidewalk, Rickshaw Damaged

The silver truck of the Republic Motor Company, French Concession Registration No. 18276, Municipal Registration No. 4986, yesterday (15th) around 10 AM, was driven by the driver to the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and Route Mercier. Because there was a rickshaw in front, suddenly turned, the driver was unable to brake in time, causing the rickshaw wheel to be damaged, and the truck also ran onto the sidewalk, damaging the corner of the wall of the Defengxiang Cotton Cloth Store at No. 315. The front bumper of the car fell off, the fender was broken, and the driver's nose was also injured by the glass, with blood flowing all over his face. He was later arrested by the street patrol and taken to the police station, then transferred to Renji Hospital for treatment, and then discharged. The rickshaw puller was detained for questioning.

Silk and Satin Dyeing Industry Discusses Dyeing Prices Yesterday

The Shanghai Silk and Satin Dyeing Industry Association convened a meeting yesterday to reorganize dyeing prices. More than 80 people attended, including representatives from Lao Zhenghe, Lu Tingjian, Qian Da Hu, Wei Ren, Lao Zhenchang, Guo Fengshan, and Shun Da Chang, Zhang Xicheng. Tan Borong chaired the meeting, and Wang Shipeng took the minutes. The chairman first gave a report, stating that since the Italy-Abyssinia War, the cost of goods shipped to China from various countries has skyrocketed due to the sharp increase in exchange rates, and the prices of imported goods in China have gradually soared. Just looking at the item of dyes, prices have recently risen and there is a shortage of goods. Dyes are necessities for our industry. Since dyes are gradually rising in price, the impact on costs is enormous. The dyeing prices in our industry are still difficult to maintain even with hard work. If dyes rise sharply this time, and we do not actively reorganize and agree on uniform prices, how can we make up for the losses? Recently, the silk industries in Shanghai and Hangzhou have successively published price increases in various newspapers. The woolen, knitting, dyeing, and weaving industries have all reported price increases. The dye industry has also simultaneously advertised that it sells for cash. Recently, the government has implemented the legal tender policy, and the market economy has changed. Now, the Municipal Government has issued instructions to various industries to set appropriate prices within a limited time and submit the proposed price list to the bureau for record-keeping. There are already supervisory measures for the implementation of uniform prices. If our industry loses this opportunity to discuss prices and determine the restrictions on the amount of fabric and size, the industry will be even more unsustainable. Please work together to save the industry. Discussion of important issues: (1) Regarding the reorganization of dyeing prices, we should first formulate an increase standard for implementation. (Resolution) Appoint specialists to formulate a reorganization plan and an increase standard, and then submit it to the general assembly for discussion and approval. (2) Restrict the amount of silk fabric and size submitted for dyeing to suit the work. (Resolution) This case will be handled after careful discussion and progress. (3) Regarding whether to change the "monthly fee standard" decided at the last meeting. (Resolution) The standard for monthly fees decided last time should be changed immediately to "one cent will be collected from the industry for every piece of silk dyed in a month" as the monthly fee. At the end of each month, the association will send personnel to check the number of dyed fabrics registered in the dyed fabric book and calculate the amount to be paid. The above-mentioned fee collection standard is more universal, equal, and fair than the previous method. (4) This association should send personnel to persuade people to join the association. (Resolution) Agreed to do so. (5) Adjournment.

"忽蘇爾" (Hūsū'ěr) Felsol Asthma Medicine Sells Well

"忽蘇爾" (Hūsū'ěr) Felsol asthma medicine is the only effective medicine for treating various types of asthma, breathing difficulties, asthma caused by chronic bronchitis or heart disease, various heart diseases, new and old coughs, pertussis, influenza, and other symptoms. Its miraculous efficacy has long been praised by medical institutions worldwide. In Europe and the United States, tens of millions of boxes are sold annually. Publication of 瑯嬛文集 (Lánghuán Wénjí) - The Complete Edition of the 金瓶梅詞話 (Jīnpíngméi Cíhuà) is Released

Zhang Dai, courtesy name Zongzi, from Yuezhong (Shaoxing, Zhejiang) in the Ming dynasty, wrote 陶庵夢憶 (Tao'an Mengyi) and 西湖夢尋 (Xihu Mengxun), which are popular in the world and loved by literature researchers. Yu Pingbo once reprinted them. However, apart from these two books, the remaining collections are rarely circulated. Mr. Liu Dajie obtained a manuscript of 瑯嬛文集 (Lánghuán Wénjí) in Chengdu, totaling six volumes. Except for a few poems, all are prose, divided into prefaces, postscripts, biographies, inscriptions, etc., including Notes on Mount Tai and Notes on Putuo Mountain, full of wit. After Xu Wenchang, he can be called the first master in Yuezhong. Shanghai Magazine Company has now purchased it from Mr. Liu and included it as the tenth part of the Chinese Literature Rare Book Series. It will be published today, with the signature of Lin Yutang and the postscript by Lu Jiye. The retail price of the popular edition is 30 cents, and the special edition is 40 cents. It is said that the next book to be published is 陈眉公 (Chen Meigong)'s manuscript of 白石樵真稿 (Baishi Qiao Zhengao), with over 480 pages, divided into two volumes, upper and lower. The popular edition is priced at 60 cents, and the special edition is priced at 90 cents. In addition, the fifth volume of the 金瓶梅詞話 (Jīnpíngméi Cíhuà) will also be published simultaneously tomorrow. Combined with the previously published volumes one, two, three, and four, it is now completely published. The combined purchase price of the popular edition is 1.5 yuan, and the special edition is 2 yuan, with a 10% discount. A beautifully bound, gold-stamped hardcover edition is also printed in one large volume, selling for 2.5 yuan. It is magnificent and beautiful and will be published on the 18th. Out-of-town sales are not available, but mail orders are postage-free.

###傅元退 (Fù Yuántuì) and Ms. Luo to Marry at the New World Restaurant Today

Mr. 傅旡退 (Fù Yuántuì), a practitioner of the New Life Movement, is a graduate of the Department of Civil Engineering at Tokyo Imperial University with a degree in engineering. In his early years, he planned railway networks in the Northeast and developed Huludao. He served as the chief engineer of Wusong and Xiaguan ports, as well as a full-time member of the Design Committee of the Greater Shanghai Municipality. Later, he established the Japanese Examination Association, translating various political, economic, and diplomatic books that meet the needs of the times, which became popular. He is currently working as a counselor for the Chairman's Office of the Military Affairs Commission, the head of the Design Committee's Translation Department, and a research secretary. Mr. Fu has a noble view of life, is rigorous in his words and deeds, strict with himself, and has a forthright disposition. He is very selective in choosing a partner and would rather remain single unless he finds someone with a similar spirit of the New Life Movement. Therefore, he is only now marrying Ms. 羅梅淸 (Luó Méiqīng). Ms. Luo comes from a prominent family in Panyu. Her father, Mr. 羅維翰 (Luó Wéihàn), served as an official in the two lakes (Hunan and Hubei) during the late Qing Dynasty and was known for his political achievements. Since the Republic of China, he has founded industries such as the Hankou Jiji Hydroelectric Company and the Daxing Textile Factory, and organized literary and art societies to study ancient and modern art, under the pseudonym 四峯 (Sìfēng). Ms. Meiqing was taught by her father early on and graduated from the middle school of the Hankou Western Overseas School. She is proficient in both new and old knowledge and has mastered both Chinese and Western skills in managing household affairs. She and Mr. Fu are both practitioners of the New Life Movement. Now that they are forming a new family, they will surely be a model for society. They are scheduled to marry at 4 p.m. today (the 16th) at the New World Restaurant on Nanjing Road, with Mr. 褚慧僧 (Chǔ Huìsēng) as the officiant. It is sure to be a lively occasion.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated that the sky around Shandong is cloudy and cold but still clear with a strong north wind. The Yangtze River basin is overcast with fog or rain, gradually clouding over, with a sharp northwest to northeast breeze. The typhoon southeast of Luzon is still moving northwest-west, its center reaching within about 60 miles of 14 degrees north latitude and 126 degrees east longitude at 2 p.m. yesterday. The wind force is unknown. Also, the highest temperature in this city in the 24 hours before 3 p.m. yesterday was 62.6 degrees, and the lowest was 581.1 degrees. Letter to the Editor

Dear Editor,

Regarding a matter of correction, your newspaper on the 6th of this month, i.e., the third page, eleventh edition of issue number 22461, stated that the Soviet Russian government, in view of the large number of overseas Chinese in this city and the inconvenience in treating diseases, has specially built a large-scale hospital on a vacant lot at the corner of Pershing Road in the French Concession to provide relief to poor and sick Russian overseas Chinese, and that a religious ceremony was held for the groundbreaking on the afternoon of the day before yesterday (the 3rd).

Upon investigation, this hospital was planned and founded by the Shanghai Eastern Orthodox Association of White Russian overseas Chinese in Shanghai ten years ago (1923). Now, it is expanding and seeking a new site for reconstruction. The matter has nothing to do with the Soviet Russian government. The information published by your newspaper is inconsistent with the facts. I hereby write to request that your editor-in-chief correct the information in the short term to clarify the facts.

Yours sincerely,

Meitzer, President of the Shanghai White Russian Overseas Chinese Association

The Path of Political System Reform (Continued)

—潘公展 (Pān Gōngzhǎn) (November 1935, Shanghai)

——Respectfully dedicated to the comrades of the Fifth National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang and the gentlemen who discuss political system reform——

(1) Political system reform must be based on historical experience and national habits. Hugh Sellon, the author of Democracy and Dictatorship, once said: "Germany's past history makes it unsuitable for parliamentary politics... The Germanic nation has a kind of emotional fondness for autocratic regimes, and politically, it is the most docile and easily agitated nation in Europe; these characteristics make it unsuitable for democratic politics, and strong rulers become necessary leaders... Therefore, the failure of Western democratic rule in Germany best proves the folly of completely transplanting foreign methods to another country." He also solemnly pointed out: "The political liberation of each country occurs in its own soil, its own national character, and the experiences accumulated by its own history." Now, some "scholars" who advocate "complete Westernization" wish they could transplant the British constitutional system, which has been experienced for 1,400 years, to China overnight. One says that "one-party" dictatorship is not in line with democracy, and "party rule" must be abolished. Another says that "constitutionalism is the best training for constitutionalism" and that "political tutelage" can be concluded. However, they do not know that the flavor of party struggle under "parliamentary politics" has been tasted for more than ten years in the historical experience since the Republic of China, and the habits of the Chinese people, "those who soothe me are my lords, and those who abuse me are my enemies," and "I go out at sunrise and rest at sunset; what has the emperor's power to do with me!" have been unbreakable for thousands of years. Therefore, if we want to guide the Chinese people into the path of democratic political system, we must rely on wise leaders and the founding party to protect them. In other words, the political system can be reformed, and the constitution can be promulgated, but we must not take the old path of British and American-style multi-party strife-ridden "parliamentary politics" again, so as not to fall into a political tide of overlapping waves and exhaustion.

(2) Political system reform must be based on the legacy of the Premier and the needs of the times. The Republic of China was founded by the Premier himself, the Outline of National Construction was formulated by the Premier himself, the Three Principles of the People are the doctrine of national construction, and the Five-Power Constitution is the mechanism of national construction. All of these are the legacy of the Premier. Whether it is from military administration to political tutelage, or from political tutelage to constitutionalism, it is permissible to increase or decrease them according to the needs of the times, but it is not permissible to fundamentally disregard them to cater to popular customs. Since the members of the Kuomintang are loyal believers of the Premier, they should be of one mind and one heart and carry it through to the end. Therefore, opposing the Three Principles of the People—if you use revolutionary means to overthrow the Kuomintang, and then discard all the Premier's legacy and ignore it, then the situation is still forgivable; if the believers of the Three Principles of the People are anesthetized by the theory of political system reform, without carefully considering how to reform the political system, and take reckless actions, embarking on the path of abandoning the Premier's legacy, then the blame is unforgivable. "Since ancient times, everyone has died, but the people cannot stand without trust." In the current difficult situation, the Kuomintang, in addition to恪奉 (kèfèng) respectfully following the Premier's legacy, taking the "world as one" as its heart, and bearing the responsibility of "bearing hardship and resentment," to show the world its great trust, has no other way to seek understanding from the people of the country, nor any other path to save its country. As for the needs of the times, all those who have studied political systems know that the strengthening of administrative power is indeed a consistent trend in various countries recently, and it is especially in line with the current environment in our country. Because in extraordinary times, dealing with national affairs requires prudence and decisiveness, both of which are indispensable. If we still hold the outdated concept of preventing the dictatorship of administrative leaders in the 18th and 19th centuries, and blindly want to raise legislative power to restrain administrative power, or even make it surpass administrative power, so that even if the administrative leader has talent and the administrative organization is flexible, it is impossible to show the omnipotence of its government, then in the process of internal peace and foreign resistance, national salvation and survival, the country will inevitably suffer invisible losses. Therefore, within the scope of following the Premier's legacy, according to the trends of the times, strengthening the power of the administrative mechanism is 100% necessary. (To be continued)

Wusong Zhoujiabridge - Murder for Money Occurs, Silver Necklace Exchanged for $3.60, Murderer Ma Jinshan Arrested on the Same Day

In a straw shed in Zhoujiabridge, west of Wusong Town, there was a woman from Jiangbei Taizhou, Zhou Chou, who was over 40 years old and worked as a female worker in a yarn factory to make a living. She had a son and a daughter. Her son, Guilin, 8 years old, was playing alone in the nearby fields on the morning of the 14th. A neighbor and fellow villager, Ma Jinshan, 17 years old, caught sight of Guilin playing alone and noticed that he was wearing a silver necklace around his neck. Immediately, he became greedy and went forward to snatch it. Although Guilin was young, he refused to let go, causing Ma Jinshan to strangle the child to death with a cloth belt and abandon the body in a swamp beach. Ma then took the stolen silver necklace to the Laobaocheng Silver Shop on Songxing Road and exchanged it for $3.60 in cash for use. It was not until around 4 p.m. that the child's body was discovered by a villager cutting grass. At that time, the child's mother, Zhou Chou, was searching for her son. Upon hearing the news and going to identify the body, she confirmed that it was her son Guilin's body, which was still warm. There was a cloth belt around his neck, and a silver necklace was missing. Knowing that he had been murdered for money, she could not help but cry bitterly. The matter was learned by Bao Guanwu, a detective from the Wusong Police Station, who went to the scene of the incident to investigate the situation. He then went to various silver shops to inquire and found the original stolen goods in Laobaosheng. After questioning the appearance and clothing of the murderer, he immediately cooperated with the police to arrest the murderer Ma Jinshan. The suspect confessed without denying it. Chief Deng Zhiyi, as the matter concerned murder for money, yesterday morning ordered the local guarantor Zhou Lansheng to submit the case to the Shanghai District Court to send personnel to Wusong for inspection in order to punish the crime.

Education News

Textbook Registration Applications Must Include the Ministry's Approval License

(Nanjing, 15th dispatch) The Ministry of the Interior telegraphed to the provincial and municipal governments on the 15th, instructing all bookstores that when applying for registration of textbooks and books, they must submit the Ministry of Education's approval license together. Otherwise, the registration will not be granted.

Henan Province Promotes Compulsory Education Plan

The Henan Provincial Education Administrative Authority formulated the following thirteen original articles of the Henan Province Compulsory Education Promotion Plan this year. Article 1: In order to promote compulsory education in various counties, this outline of the plan is specifically formulated. Article 2: The principles for formulating this outline of the plan are as follows: (1) To promote and develop in a way that the government and local people work together; (2) To strive for economy and responsibility in establishment; (3) To recognize private tutoring as part of compulsory education, and to temporarily improve private schools to expand the quantity of compulsory education when compulsory education funding cannot be fully raised; (4) To provide appropriate guidance to the teachers, facilities, and educational orders of private tutoring schools to improve them and to eliminate their abuse. Article 3: The County Education Bureau shall, one month before the beginning of each year, investigate the following items clearly in order to coordinate the promotion of compulsory education in the county: (1) The status of school-age children in each school district in the county who are out of school or in school, and the reasons for being out of school; (2) The management status of private primary schools and private schools in the county, the service performance of teachers and private school teachers, and their supply and demand status; (3) The number of out-of-school children of older ages in the short-term compulsory education experimental area and the management status of short-term primary schools. Article 4: After the County Education Bureau has clearly investigated the above items, it shall immediately prepare statistics and propose a practical improvement plan to be submitted to the Education Department for inspection and implementation. Article 5: The methods for establishing schools in each county include the following: (1) Adding primary schools or primary school classes; (2) In accordance with the outline of the first phase of the implementation of compulsory education, adding half-day two-part primary schools or classes; (3) In accordance with the implementation methods of short-term compulsory education and the plans proposed by each county, adding short-term primary schools or short-term primary school classes; (4) Improving and managing private schools to achieve the practical effect of assisting compulsory education; its management regulations shall be formulated separately; (5) Rewarding private primary schools. Article 6: If each county has difficulty with education expenses and primary schools cannot be universally established, it shall, within the possible scope, find ways to promote the increase in the quantity of private primary schools, short-term primary schools, or excellent private schools to remedy the situation. Article 7: School-age children in each county who have considerable schools nearby and have the capacity to accommodate them but do not attend school may be subject to partial compulsory education by the Education Bureau with the consent of the County Government and the Public Security Bureau. Article 8: If the short-term compulsory education experimental area in each county has raised considerable funds, it shall be effectively promoted in accordance with the original plan. Article 9: The expenditure standards for various school expenses in each county, except for the expenses for rewarding private primary schools and improving private schools, which shall be determined by each county, shall be based on the following principles: (1) The annual expenses for each primary school class shall not exceed 150 yuan, except when starting a school or adding a class, when start-up fees may be raised appropriately; (2) The annual expenses for each two-part half-day primary school class shall not exceed 150 yuan; (3) The annual expenses for each short-term primary school class shall not exceed 150 yuan; (4) The expenses for short-term primary school classes attached to each school shall not exceed one-half of the short-term primary school expenses. Article 10: The sources of funds for each county include the following: (1) Sorting out education funds and collecting arrears; (2) Clearing up temple properties and increasing rental income; (3) Rewarding private donations; (4) Encouraging local people to raise funds locally; (5) Appropriately collecting tuition fees; (6) Requesting the government to provide subsidies; (7) In addition to the above-mentioned methods, funds may be raised in accordance with the provisions of Item A of Article 5 of the Regulations on the Organization of the Board of Directors of Rural Primary Schools in Henan Province promulgated by the Education Department, without conflicting with the central laws and regulations. Article 11: The performance of the head of the Education Bureau in each county in handling compulsory education shall be listed as one of the main examinations. Article 12: The county head of each county shall be responsible for planning, guiding, and supervising compulsory education in the county, and the主管 (zhǔguǎn) in charge of the Public Security Bureau and the 区保甲长 (qū bǎojiǎzhǎng) shall be responsible for assisting, and all shall be listed as one of the achievements of the police. Article 13: This outline of the plan shall be implemented from the date of approval and promulgation.

The 8th Annual Meeting of the Zhejiang Provincial Affiliated Elementary School Association, hosted by Taichung Affiliated Elementary School, held its opening ceremony at the Haimen Public Club on the 12th of this month. The Municipal Bureau of Education Orders All Schools to Participate in the Study of Aviation Science

Also Sends Letters to Various Universities and Cultural Groups to Participate in the Aviation Association's Flying Society

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education issued an instruction to all schools and social education institutions yesterday, stating, "According to the letter from the Aviation Association Recruiting Team Leader's Office, the Aviation Association of China has established the China Flying Society, which is well-recognized by people in society. In order to universally increase aviation knowledge and skills, we plan to ask your office to assist in promoting it, etc. The China Flying Society is the only institution for the public to study aviation knowledge. At a time when the national crisis is severe and the nation is dying, all Chinese people should vigorously promote this art in preparation for emergencies. Therefore, we have attached 50 copies each of the China Flying Society's constitution, membership application form, member rights, and membership application. We sincerely hope that you will check and collect them, and promptly forward them to your affiliated institutions and notify teachers and students of major secondary schools, elementary school teachers and staff, staff of various social education institutions, and various cultural groups to cooperate in encouraging and urging them to participate. We will respond accordingly. It is hereby notified that, upon approval, saving the country through aviation is an essential plan today, and the study of aviation science is indeed necessary. Apart from sending letters to various universities for assistance, we hereby urgently notify our affiliated institutions to be aware of this order."

Social Education Bureaus Convene All Schools to Discuss the Organization of School Cooperatives

Today at 2 PM in Bansong Garden

The Municipal Social Education Bureaus believe that the organizational regulations for school student unions promulgated by the central government stipulate that cooperative undertakings are one of the ways for students to be active. Organizing cooperatives in schools can enable students to understand their operating methods and gain practical experience in preparation for engaging in cooperative undertakings in society in the future. Therefore, for the sake of the development of cooperative undertakings, the organization of school cooperatives should be promoted first as a guideline. It is hereby decided to convene a joint meeting of persons in charge of major and minor schools in this city at 2 PM today in Bansong Garden in Nanshi to discuss ways to promote the organization of school cooperatives.

Huacheng Workers' Children School Held its Seventh Anniversary Yesterday

The Huacheng Cigarette Factory Workers' Children School on Huishan Road in this city has been established for seven years. Principal Chen Peiming has spared no effort in developing school affairs. Therefore, the school has made significant progress every year. The number of students suddenly increased to more than 400 this summer. The original school buildings were not enough. Therefore, the school board members Gu Shaoqing, Zhou Xuexiang, etc., raised funds to add a new school building, which has also been completed. November 15th this month was the seventh anniversary of the school's establishment. At 9:00 AM, the school specially gathered all teachers and students, as well as representatives of students from the literacy school and the worker's supplementary night school, a total of more than 500 people, to hold a celebration meeting in the school's auditorium. Chen Heqin, director of the Chinese Education Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council, Yao Zantang, representative of the director of the Municipal Bureau of Education, Pan Gongzhan, and many others, including Yu Zuoting, Yuan Deng, and school board members Gu Shaoqing and Zhou Xuexiang, all gave sincere speeches. In the afternoon, the school's students gave physical and musical performances, and the grand occasion was unprecedented.

The Municipal Bureau of Education Bans Xinhua Elementary School

The private Xinhua Elementary School at No. 2 Ruyili, Lanweiai Road, French Concession, is run by Xi Yaguang. The management is not in compliance with regulations, the buildings are very cramped, the administration is chaotic, there are no facilities, the education is not suitable, and the moral education is ineffective. The Municipal Bureau of Education has sent personnel to investigate and has sent a letter to the French Concession Public Works Bureau to ban it for rectification.

Seventh International Gongzhan Cup Handball Tournament

First Cycle Scheduled to Begin on the 25th of This Month; China is Sharpening its Swords and Guns and Practicing at the West Youth Venue

The 7th Gongzhan Cup National Land Handball Competition is scheduled to be held on the 25th of this month at the YMCA on Jing'an Temple Road. The Chinese team, which has won two consecutive championships in recent years, has agreed with the West Youth to practice at the West Youth ball room for nine days starting next Monday (18th) in order to strive for excellence and familiarize themselves with the venue. Veteran players Zhu Kuan and Sun Daosheng will once again dominate the field and maintain the honor for our Chinese team. Cup Competition History Handball is still in its infancy in our country and has not attracted as much attention as other ball games. The Shanghai YMCA has been working hard to promote it for several decades, and the atmosphere is booming. It has cultivated many outstanding talents. In the winter of the 21st year of the Republic of China, Pan Gongzhan, director of the Municipal Bureau of Education, advocated for further promotion and obtained the consent of the West Youth Association of the West Youth in this port to initiate the international handball competition, which began on December 15th of that year for the first competition. Since then, it has been held twice a year in spring and autumn, and Mr. Pan donated a large silver cup, with the name of the championship team engraved on it for each session, and kept it for one season to commemorate it. The competition was named the Gongzhan Cup International Handball Competition. This season is already the seventh session. The first four sessions were all won by the West Youth. Until the fifth and sixth sessions, the Chinese team won the championship with a neat lineup.

This Year's Date The date for this year's competition has been decided by the committee the night before last. The first cycle will be held on the 25th, 26th, and 27th of this month, and the second cycle will be held on the 3rd, 4th, and 5th of next month. The competition will be divided into ten singles groups and five doubles groups. A three-game two-win system will be adopted. The winner of each singles or doubles will score one point, and the team with the most points will win. The balls used in the competition will be Spooler 101. Both the Chinese and Western teams have made considerable preparations for this year's competition, and there will be wonderful performances.

The Municipal Fourth Middle School Joint Games Postponed

The Municipal Education Bureau Officially Announced Yesterday

The Municipal Bureau of Education issued an instruction to the middle schools in this city yesterday, stating, "The Fourth Joint Games of Secondary Schools in this city were originally scheduled to be held in the autumn of this year. Later, it was discussed that the Sixth National Games would also be held in the autumn. This city is extremely busy preparing for the National Games and organizing participation in various tasks. By the time the closing ceremony ended, it was already late autumn, and the weather was suddenly cold. It is not suitable for students to exercise due to their physical strength and health. In addition, some of the athletes representing this city who participated in the National Games were selected from private secondary schools in this city and already had the opportunity to compete. Holding sports again during the same period will cause fatigue for the students' minds and bodies. Moreover, some schools in this city have suspended classes for one or two days or two or three days to visit the National Games. If the Joint Games of Secondary Schools are held, each school must suspend classes again to visit, which will affect students' studies. This year's Joint Games of Secondary Schools will be better to give students a chance to rest than to hold them in a hurry without any benefit. It has been decided to postpone the event to the spring of next year when the weather is warmer and hold it later. In addition to reporting the reasons for the postponement to the municipal government for record, it is hereby ordered for your information.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (96)

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"No, I've kept them. I thought these must be some treasures of yours that you've carefully preserved," said Mrs. Shu, handing him an old straw hat filled with butterflies and beetles, a handkerchief wrapping a large pile of oddities picked up along the way: a few bird nests, carefully wrapped with moss; strange shells and pebbles; several pieces of fungus; and a few small crabs, in a state of great anger because they were imprisoned.

"Can I have some equipment to put these guys in? Mr. Harder and I found them, they are first-rate characters, so I want to keep them for observation; may I?" Don asked, forgetting his foot, finding it funny to see the crabs scuttling across the bed.

"Of course, you can; Bo Li's old cage is just right. I'll go get it, and be careful not to let them pinch Tandy's toes," Mrs. Shu said as she left. Meanwhile, Don was overjoyed that his treasures had not been discarded as dirty rubbish.

Soon, Ned, Little Bridge, and the cage came together. The crabs moved into this new home, and the children were ecstatic. They showed no fear when they were put into the room. Don recounted the capture of them in much more detail for these admiring listeners. Then he unfolded the package and explained each item. By this time, Mrs. Shu had retreated to a neighboring room so that they could chat freely, but she was surprised and amused by the children's naive conversations.
