Shen Bao Wireless Radio Weekly

Methods of Ultra-Shortwave Oscillation

— Chongling

Even today, ultra-shortwave radio, although still in the experimental stage, is progressing rapidly, which is quite amazing. It is expected that with the efforts of general experts in the future, ultra-shortwave radio will be able to keep pace with shortwave radio and find new uses. This article describes three methods of ultra-shortwave oscillation that have been successfully tested and introduces them here for the assistance of those who are initially studying ultra-shortwaves.

The oscillation method of ordinary oscillating tubes cannot be applied to generate ultra-short waves with extremely high frequencies due to the limitations imposed by the Goudie rate. The new method was initially successful due to the efforts of experts, including three types: (1) Barkhausen oscillation, (2) Magnetron oscillation, and (3) Diode electron oscillation. They are described separately below.

(1) Barkhausen Oscillation: The Barkhausen oscillator was invented by Mr. Barkhausen and uses a positive grid and negative plate triode (as shown in the figure). A positive pressure of 100 to 200 volts is applied to the grid of the triode, and the plate is connected to a negative pressure of several volts to cause electronic oscillation inside the triode. Therefore, Barkhausen oscillation can also be called triode electronic oscillation. The reason for the occurrence of electronic oscillation can be simply explained as follows: The filament in the tube emits electrons due to heat. Because the grid, which is quite close to the filament, has a positive pressure, there are almost no electrons in the space between the grid and the filament. Therefore, the electrons emitted by the filament have extremely high speeds and are immediately absorbed by the grid. A part of the electrons passing through the grid gap are rejected by the negative pressure of the plate and return. When they reach the vicinity of the filament, they are absorbed by the grid again, rush out of the grid gap, and are turned back by the negative plate. This cycle continues, resulting in oscillation, which is called electronic oscillation. The oscillation frequency depends on the speed of the electrons passing through the grid, so it is related to both the positive grid pressure and the negative plate pressure. If the grid pressure reaches 100 to 200 volts, ultra-short wave oscillation of 30 cm to several meters can be generated. However, the generated power is extremely small and the efficiency is also quite low. The two lines ab shown in the figure are two parallel copper tubes, which are the oscillating circuit for ultra-short wave output, and LL are two high-frequency choke coils.

(2) Magnetic Field Controlled Tube Oscillation: The magnetic field controlled tube is a type of diode. Its plate is cylindrical, and its filament is a line installed in the cylindrical shaft position inside the cylinder. The outside of the tube is surrounded by a current-carrying coil, so that the direction of its magnetic field is parallel to the filament. In order to avoid eddy current loss caused by the magnetic field on the circular screen, the screen is often divided into two parts, making it two semi-cylinders, each connected to a positive pressure, as shown in Figure 11. The role of the magnetic field is to control the movement of electrons inside the tube. When there is no magnetic field, the electrons in the tube, like ordinary diodes, are emitted from the filament and reach the plate directly along the radius, as shown in a in the figure. When there is a magnetic field, the force between the magnetic field and the electron movement occurs (the direction of the force is perpendicular to the direction of the magnetic field and the direction of electron movement), causing the electrons to reach the plate along a curved line, as shown in b. If the magnetic field is increased to a certain level, the electrons can move in a circle and fold back to the filament without reaching the plate, as shown in C. Under this C situation, electron oscillation occurs. Therefore, according to the device in Figure 3, if the filament current and plate voltage are properly matched, increasing the strength of the magnetic field (that is, increasing the current in the line diagram F) until the plate current is zero, ultra-short wave oscillation will occur, and will be output by the tuned circuit of two parallel copper tubes TT.

(3) Diode Electronic Oscillation: The third type of oscillation does not use a grid or a magnetic field. The electronic oscillation is entirely undertaken by a specially constructed diode. The structure of this diode is different from the ordinary ones. The filament is cylindrical and the plate is a line, installed in the center of the circle, which is exactly the opposite of the diode described above. The electrons emitted by the filament have speeds that do not go along the radius, causing the electrons to rotate around the plate axis and causing some electrons to escape the attraction of the plate and move back and forth, causing electronic oscillation. Englishman McPetrie recently specially made a diode to do this experiment. The equipment is shown in Figure 4: The plate in the tube is a tungsten line with a diameter of about one millimeter. The filament is also made of tungsten, consisting of four tungsten wires wound on a circle with a radius of about 12.5 millimeters with the plate as the axis and connected in parallel. A and B are two parallel long copper tubes, installed between the plate and the filament. D is a circular copper plate with a diameter of about 30 centimeters, passing through the two lines AB, for changing the wavelength and replacing the choke coil. C is a variable capacitor of about 110 MMF, which is also used to change the frequency. According to the results of his experiment, when the plate voltage is increased to about 360 volts, an ultra-short wave of one and a half meters can be generated, and the generated oscillation frequency is very stable. Sliding the circular copper plate D, or changing the capacitor C, the generated frequency can be arbitrarily changed within the range. When D is pulled closer to the vacuum tube, the frequency increases accordingly. However, D cannot be too close to the vacuum tube. If it exceeds a certain point, the oscillation will stop unless D is still pulled back and then gradually pulled closer, the oscillation cannot be restored.

Recent European and American Television

— Ming

"Television" is a successor to "Wireless Radio." Although it cannot yet be described as "developed," its future prospects are considerable. In short, it is a period when research is most needed in reality.

Television broadcasting was conducted in England and the United States several years ago, but because the results were not satisfactory, the United States stopped it last year. Although England still continues to broadcast, it has in fact become the "end of the crossbow"! According to the current television broadcasting in the UK, it is only carried out by the British Broadcasting Corporation. The images used for broadcasting are very simple, only 30 lines, which are blurry and unclear, and it is not surprising that they are difficult to satisfy.

Television is different from ordinary wireless radio. With ordinary wireless radio, even a simple receiver such as a mineral radio can achieve considerable results; but television is the opposite. Unless both the broadcasting machine and the receiving machine are very complete, it is not easy to obtain good results.

In the wireless radio industry, the research on television seems to have suffered a setback on the surface, but in fact, European and American countries are competing in research, especially the United States and Germany.

The most significant achievements in the improvement and research of television have been made by R.C.A. Victor Company in the United States, and the Ministry of Communications and Siemens in Germany. Currently, the images broadcast by R.C.A. Victor Company in the United States have been improved from 120 lines to 240 lines, so the images projected are quite clear, like watching a movie. It is heard that they plan to further improve to 360 lines in the future.

Currently, the research focus of European and American television experts is concentrated on the following points:

1. In broadcasting machines, there is what is called "film intermediate type." The method is to first photograph the object to be broadcast into a film, and then continuously send out the images on the film by the broadcasting machine. The characteristic of this method is that film is an object, not a person, so the broadcasting can be arbitrarily illuminated with strong light, and the results are more considerable. However, since multiple procedures and media are involved, the image may become blurry.

2. Receiving machines can be roughly divided into two types: those for home use and those for public use. Public receiving machines also use film as a medium. The method is that the radio waves broadcast by the broadcasting machine are received by the receiving machine, then converted into current, and the images are photographed and printed on the film, and then projected like a movie. After the projection, the film is immersed in warm water to wash off the film on the film, and then coated with a photosensitive film, which can be reused.

The above two methods are currently under continued research.

In short, recent European and American research on television has made great progress. Both technically and mechanically, it is nearing completion. So why is television not yet widespread? The reasons are as follows:

1. The machinery used for television is extremely complex, unlike the simplicity of ordinary wireless radio. For users, the receiving machines that should be prepared cost at least 300 to 400 US dollars each. This is one reason why it is not easy to popularize.

2. The radio waves used by television are different from those used by ordinary wireless radio. They are a type of ultra-short wave below eight meters. This type of radio wave is not easy to reach far. According to experimental results, the broadcasting range of each broadcasting station is only 70 miles. Therefore, in order to make it reach various places, it is necessary to invest heavily and build numerous broadcasting stations and relay stations. For example, according to the results of research by R.C.A. Victor Company, in order to make television reach all over the United States, it is necessary to set up more than 80 broadcasting stations. This is another reason why it is not easy to popularize.

3. Television broadcasting machines are very expensive, far exceeding the cost of wireless radio broadcasting machines, so it is not easy to set up broadcasting organizations in ordinary cities. This is another reason why it is not easy to popularize.

4. The cost required for television broadcasting is extremely huge, so the cost that users should bear is not a small amount. According to calculations by R.C.A. Victor Company in the United States, the fee that users should pay each year needs to be more than 100 gold (US dollars). In this time of economic panic, is it easy to collect such a huge amount of receiving fees from users? This is another reason why it is not easy to popularize.

In short, recent research on television in European and American countries has made rapid progress, and there is a trend of rapid progress. Technically and mechanically, it is about to reach completion, but it is still far from "practical." The desire to "popularize" is even less optimistic. However, with the determination of the experts to study, success can be expected!

Supply of Voltage to Each Pole of the Vacuum Tube (Continued)

— Guan Tingzhen

The resistance of the filament or heating element should also be calculated using Ohm's law when in series: Voltage required Resistance = (Supply Voltage - Vacuum Tube Rated Voltage) / Vacuum Tube Rated Current (Ohms)

If the radio uses one No. 78, one No. 77, one No. 43, and one No. 25z5 connected to a 120-volt power line, then its series resistance is equal to 120 volts (supply voltage) minus 62.6 volts (sum of 2×6.3 volts) divided by 0.3 amps (vacuum tube rated current). The answer is about 191 ohms. The electrical power is 120 volts minus 62.6 volts multiplied by 0.3 amps. The answer is about 17.2 watts. When purchasing, a resistor with a larger wattage should be selected. If the rated currents of the vacuum tubes in series are different, then a resistor must be connected to both ends of the filament of the vacuum tube with the smaller current to allow the excess current to pass through. In this way, the calculation of the series resistance must be based on the vacuum tube with the largest rated current.

Ultra-Shortwave Communication Machine in the National Games

— Mingxiang

Ultra-shortwave is a treasure buried in wireless radio, which urgently needs to be excavated. American amateurs have already achieved an amazing communication record of 720 miles. There must be not a few amateur research comrades in our country who are interested in ultra-shortwave, but it is rare to have considerable achievements through experimentation. Recently, at the opening of the 6th National Games, the Central News Agency installed multiple 5-meter ultra-shortwave communication machines in the venue to transmit venue news. It was lightweight, clear, and worked perfectly. This can be called the first practical application of ultra-shortwave in our country. The structure of the machine is extremely simple, both transmitting and receiving. The manufacturing method and experimental results are published in detail in the second issue of the Practical Wireless Radio magazine. Readers can succeed by following the instructions. The cost of the whole machine is also very economical. Including the microphone, earpiece, and battery set, it costs about 40 yuan. This machine is on display in the kitchen of the business department of Zhongyong Wireless Electrical Machinery Factory at No. 77, Laohe Road in this city for comrades to visit.

Spring and Autumn

Snippets

— (Microorganism)

Old birds fly around during the day to catch small insects to feed the newly hatched baby birds, and sleep with them in the nest at night. How loving and tender is that? But as soon as the baby birds have grown their feathers and can fly by themselves, they will disperse and each look for their own small insects to eat, and they no longer need the old birds to feed and protect them! Therefore, if a person still relies on the shade of his parents and cannot stand on his own after becoming an adult, he is simply not as good as birds!

On rainy days, water from the eaves drips onto the hard flagstones. The water clearly does not have much strength, but after a long time, a small hole will be formed on the flagstones. This shows that any difficult thing in the world can be achieved if you spare no effort to do it. As the saying goes, "If you work hard enough, an iron rod can be ground into a needle." How apt is this saying!

Record of Visiting Mr. Chen Qubing's Public Funeral

— Daoyi

Mr. Chen Qubing of Wujiang was a member of the Tongmenghui. He followed the Premier in the revolution for many years. He had profound academic knowledge and abundant works. He once organized the South Society and led the literary world. He served as a professor in various universities in Beijing, Hangzhou, Shanghai, and Guangdong successively. He had students all over the country. Unfortunately, on the afternoon of the Mid-Autumn Festival in the 22nd year of the Republic of China, he passed away. His old friend, Mayor Wu Tiecheng and others, held a memorial meeting in Shanghai last spring. Now, Liu Yimo, Liu Yazi, Chen Bulei and other celebrities have launched a public funeral at the foot of Tiger Hill in Suzhou. The ceremony was held on the 10th of this month. The reporter admired Mr. very much and went to visit on that day. I will record the grand occasion roughly.

On the morning of that day, the public funeral was held in the Bao'en Temple of the North Temple Pagoda in Suzhou. Old friends and students gathered from far and near. The presidents of the five academies of the National Government and the Central Party Headquarters sent representatives to pay tribute. The magistrate of Wu County and the authorities of various institutions all attended the grand ceremony in person. Those who came from Shanghai included Liu Yazi, Ma Gongyu, Zhu Shaoping, and many other celebrities. At the foot of Gusu Terrace, there was a constant stream of carriages and horses. The walls of Bao'en Temple were covered with elegiac couplets. The most important ones were: Chiang Kai-shek's couplet: The country is still in great difficulty, thinking of Deng Yu's magical plans, why is heaven not generous, crying for Qiao Xuan with a chicken and wine. Premier Wang Jingwei's couplet: It is difficult for the dragon to be tamed, the old man of the South Society praised Zi Jian, the peng corner is restricted by heaven, the cold rain in Wujiang adds to my sorrow. Member Wu Zhihui's couplet: Building the country bears a strange talent, but I regret not being able to hold the balance to govern the world, the literary world recommends a fierce general, who can sweep the pen and promote Hanwei. The rest are so beautiful that it is difficult to record them all. Miss Chen Mianxiang, the daughter of the gentleman, has a poem describing her sorrow: When will the sound of the osprey destroy the room? I sadly write the vow of the tomb, who made me lightly bury it for three years? I should be an orphan in the nine springs, dare to say that I will wait for the table of Longgang, I still hope that there will be a stele of Taoism in human books, looking back at the road on the bank of Xixian Bridge, the autumn wind and rain are so bleak, Zhonglang's daughter is not ashamed of her family's academic origin. After the public sacrifice was over, the public funeral ceremony was held at the tomb at the west end of the two mountain gates of Tiger Hill at 2 pm. After playing music, offering flowers, and reading the eulogy, all those who attended the funeral paid their respects. The ceremony was extremely grand and solemn. From then on, another scenic spot was added to the foot of Tiger Hill, which will be forever commemorated by future generations.

Anti-Drug Propaganda and Movies

— Madman

In the past, the entire Chinese film industry, apart from a few works that could be said to have a little significance, was filled with scarlet atmosphere, licentiousness and enjoyment, anesthetizing many young men and women. Although in a certain environment, we should not be too harsh and should forgive them, it is undeniable that the authors did not have sufficient awareness and understanding.

If it is undeniable that movies are not just pure entertainment, they should be responsible for educating the masses and improving society, then the detective film "Emerald Horse" recently produced by Mingxing Film Company is really worthy of high evaluation. Although this film cannot be said to be a perfect work, it has indeed fulfilled a bit of the responsibility of movies.

Since the opening of the sea ban and the large-scale import of opium, a poisonous mist has permeated our entire nation almost everywhere. From the high-ranking officials and nobles in the big cities to the hawkers and peddlers in the remote villages, everyone was addicted to it. The old, the young, the men, the women, the fields, the property, everything was smoked away, and the future of the entire nation's survival was shaken. Although not long ago, the authorities had made a determination to eradicate drugs, can you say that there is absolutely no existence of drugs under this strict prohibition? The responsibility to help promote anti-drug is indeed a natural duty that the film industry cannot ignore. Mr. Xu Xinfu seized the current theme needed by this era and produced this detective anti-drug "Emerald Horse" with sound. The focus of the entire play is not on how to punish drug addicts, but on the elimination of drug trafficking and drug-making organizations, because this is the factory for creating drugs.

Goldfish Musings

— Liang Yu

The Chinese Ornamental Fish Society was organized by fellow goldfish enthusiasts, with the late renowned director Mr. Zheng Zhengqiu, along with Xi Guansheng, Chen Zhushen, Zhu Dake, Xu He, Wu Ji, and myself as the initiators. Initially, we planned to gather for a monthly meal to gradually discuss the society's development. Unexpectedly, Mr. Zhengqiu passed away suddenly, and Brother Wu Ji, a key member, became discouraged. Even the monthly gatherings were suspended. However, Chen, Zhu, Xu, and myself were eager to revive the society and decided not to let the Chinese Ornamental Fish Society's reputation decline.

Pearlscale goldfish are the most prized variety, known for their delicate nature and susceptibility to disease. Among those in Shanghai who raise pearlscale goldfish, based on my observations, the order is as follows: first, Ye Xinfu; second, Shao Fengqi; third, Zhou Songling. However, Mr. Shao has recently been preoccupied with business and unable to devote time to goldfish keeping. He has transferred all his prized specimens to my care, with the condition that I provide him with goldfish eggs next spring in exchange. This is a great honor in my goldfish-raising history.

There are three goldfish farms in Shanghai that have pearlscale goldfish. I would rank them as follows: first, Goldfish Paradise; second, Shanghai Goldfish Garden; third, Lin Society. Beyond these, they are rarely seen.

There is a significant lack of specialized books on goldfish keeping in our country. Xu He, the owner of Shanghai Goldfish Garden, will be publishing a "Goldfish Miscellany," which contains a wealth of information. My own "Fish之道" manuscript is about 5,000 words long, and Brother Wu Ji also has a lengthy manuscript. Additionally, there are translations of Japanese books on goldfish keeping, as well as dozens of copperplate illustrations of various exotic goldfish varieties. When this book is published, every goldfish enthusiast should have a copy. It will undoubtedly provide immense benefit in learning goldfish keeping methods.

The owner of Goldfish Paradise, being wealthy, has acquired a unique collection of famous varieties. After the successful goldfish exhibition held at the Municipal Zoo, the garden gained further acclaim. The Social Affairs Bureau will be holding a horticultural exhibition at Pudong on the 15th, 16th, and 17th of this month and has specifically requested that Goldfish Paradise send goldfish for display. I hear that the owner of the garden has already responded with a letter of agreement.

Fragrant Incense, Vague Records

— Original text by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

And so, the old lady sat silently, without uttering a word or making a move, her eyes gazing forward but not focused on anything in particular. Although we knew she was deep in thought, we didn't know what she was thinking about. She never spoke a word, her hands rested motionless on her lap, and her face was tensely set.

But she certainly appeared older, at least ten years older than she had been yesterday or the day before. I couldn't help but feel a sense of pity for her from the bottom of my heart, but I dared not say anything to comfort her! All I saw before me was a very, very old woman sitting on a comfortable yellow satin cushion, but carrying on her two weary old shoulders the heavy burden of national security. How burdened she was! Yet she was not afraid. She knew that she at least had the means to deal with everything at present; what would happen in the future was unknowable, so she couldn't help but worry. But in any case, all the people of China were waiting for her to act, and sooner or later she would have to represent China in expressing an appropriate attitude.

The hands of the clock ticked by, but the Empress Dowager continued to sit silently.

Standing beside her, I couldn't help but ponder along with her: I wondered if the old lady was thinking about wanting to reclaim the portion of her youth that she had suddenly lost today. (457)

Global Curiosities

Japanese Newspapers

— Ji Yun

The newspaper industry in Japan can be described as highly developed. Newspapers like Asahi and Mainichi are almost like trusts in the Japanese newspaper world, with branch offices throughout the country. Larger prefectures have an additional page dedicated to local news. As a result, local newspapers lack vitality, which is different from China. Japanese newspapers are published twice a day, morning and evening editions. The morning edition has about sixteen pages, and the evening edition has about four pages. At first, seeing "Today's Total: Twenty Pages" on a Japanese newspaper was quite shocking. Later, I learned that a Japanese page is equivalent to one side of a Chinese newspaper, so twenty pages is actually only five sheets, less than our newspapers. Each newspaper costs about one yuan per month, which is not expensive, so many people subscribe. Moreover, education is widespread in Japan, and people are concerned about national affairs. Old women in their fifties and sixties can tell you who Mussolini and Hitler are. Although I haven't seen rickshaw pullers reading newspapers, it is common to see chauffeurs parked on the side of the road reading newspapers or books.

Foreign telegraph news occupies about one page, and city news and daily commentary also occupy one page. In addition, there are radio, business, family, and literary supplements. The telegrams are not like those in China, which seem to be just a series of news items. They are usually organized by the newspaper. News about China is of great interest to the Japanese and appears almost every day in several items. However, there is no news about the lives and studies of Chinese students in Japan. Local news is similar to that in China, consisting of articles about suicides and robberies, with large headlines using a sketching style to make the news look like a novel. What is more valuable is a commentary and a constant stream of foreign dispatches. Japanese newspapers have more foreign correspondents than Chinese newspapers, and the information they provide is about important facts in each country, rather than focusing on local customs.

I find the most interesting aspects of Japanese newspapers to be the photographs and cartoons. The collection of celebrity photographs collected by the various newspapers is truly mountainous. Whenever there is an important news story, a photo of the main figure is always attached to the corner. And even advertisements can have different styles every day, sometimes with caricatures, which is very interesting. This is a method that Chinese newspapers have not yet adopted. Articles related to geography include simple small maps so that readers can understand them at a glance. Maps of various places in China are often found in Japanese newspapers. There are even more photos in local news, with newspapers hiring photojournalists who go out in cars and planes to gather them. Radio, economic news, and film news are similar to those in China, but sometimes there are a few theoretical works that are also very valuable.

Literary works occupy only half a page and are mainly theoretical and lyrical. Their aim is to introduce Western culture and promote Japanese literature. The family supplement is for women and children and is more popular and interesting. Most newspapers have a "Consultation Center," which is a reader's mailbox where readers can submit questions anonymously. So most of the discussions are about marriage, love, and family issues. As the saying goes, "Even an honest official finds it hard to judge family matters," but the editors of the various newspapers actually answer every question, which is quite painstaking. On Sunday mornings, there is an illustrated magazine, or cartoons, or scenes of local scenery and life, occupying a page. Originally, there was also an evening edition on Sundays, but the various newspapers have recently agreed to abolish it.

The talks published in the newspapers are also very interesting. For example, the Chrysanthemum Talk, where the newspaper sends out invitations in advance, inviting many chrysanthemum experts to participate in a tea party. Each person speaks freely, expressing their grand theories. The next day, they are published in the newspaper, providing the readers with a paper conversation. This type of talk has a wide scope and is finely categorized. Even the makeup methods of actresses can become the subject of a talk. Newspaper companies often provide large companies with space to hold exhibitions or host readers for travel and excursions. Sometimes, the newspaper includes discount coupons for movie theaters, so readers can enjoy various unexpected benefits in addition to reading the newspaper.

After the newspaper business develops, the facilities are naturally perfect. The Asahi and Mainichi newspapers both use airplanes for transportation. Tokyo newspapers are distributed at six or seven in the morning, while newspapers in Chiba Prefecture arrive before four in the morning, when readers are still in sweet dreams. During the great flood in Kyoto, there were five or six extra editions a day, almost every two or three hours. The newsboys who issued the extra editions wore copper bells, running around and distributing the newspapers. As long as you hear the sound of the bell, the residents naturally become tense. The newsstands at street corners also shake a string of copper bells, which is different from the Chinese newsboys who shout "X Newspaper, XX Newspaper."

Art Exhibition News: Zhao Anzhi, a painter from Wujin, recently opened a solo exhibition at the First Park in the capital, with over two hundred works on display. His subjects include figures, landscapes, birds, and insects, and his imitation Song dynasty cloth paintings are particularly distinctive. Zhao's cloth paintings take inspiration from the Song dynasty. I hope that writers and collectors will promote them as much as possible, so that the value of our domestic cloth will increase tenfold from now on. Perhaps in a few years, it will be comparable to Song brocade.

Xiaoxitian

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Episode 11: Gently Leaning, the Moon-like Beauty is Pitied in the Courtyard; Ardently Scolding the Son-in-Law, the Lion's Roar is Heard from the Next Room

When Bei Hai saw Yue Ying in this state, his expression naturally changed. Since marrying Jia Duocai, Yue Ying had never been so close to Bei Hai, and with Jia Duocai standing right there, she couldn't say whether it was shame or regret, but she felt that if there were cracks in the ground, she would squat down and crawl into them. Bei Hai glanced at him and saw that his face was red and purple, his eyelids were drooping, and there seemed to be tears in the corners of his eyes. He hurriedly covered his mouth with his hand and coughed lightly twice. Turning back, he saw a woman standing in front of him, and he dared not look at her for more than a second, immediately hurrying towards the backyard. After reaching the backyard, for some reason, his feet stopped on their own accord. At this moment, a second thought commanded him to turn around, so he turned back to the corner of the wall, hiding his body behind it, and poked his head out to look into the front hall. As luck would have it, Mrs. Zhou was talking to Jia Duocai, her eyes not looking elsewhere. Yue Ying took a step back, tilted her body, and turned her head to look behind her. Clearly, she was looking at Bei Hai's shadow, and so the two of them looked at each other. Yue Ying did not have this intention when she turned her head to look at him this time. Not having this intention and still turning her head, this was something she could not understand herself. Unexpectedly, Bei Hai had not left and was still lingering there, which was beyond her expectations, adding a touch of excitement to her shame and regret. Not only did her face turn red, but her heart also pounded wildly. (361)

Routes of Transmission of Pathogenic Microorganisms

— Translated by Dr. Jia Zhizhong

Sanitary organisms fall into two categories: one is the lowest form of plant, called fungi; the other is the lowest form of animal, called protozoa. Anything harmful to the human body that causes disease is collectively called a pathogenic microorganism. There are two routes of transmission into the human body, outlined as follows.

(1) Invasion through the outer skin! Such as tetanus bacilli, rabies virus, pyogenic bacteria, bubonic plague bacteria, etc.

(2) Invasion through the inner skin! Such as (A) cholera vibrio, typhoid bacillus, dysentery bacillus, anthrax bacillus, tuberculosis bacillus, syphilis spirochetes, etc., that invade through the esophagus; (B) tuberculosis bacillus, pneumococcus, scarlet fever bacteria, bubonic plague bacteria, etc., that invade through the trachea; (C) gonococcus, syphilis spirochetes, puerperal fever bacteria, etc., that invade through the urethra.

The above is only a brief overview; more detailed discussion will follow.

Business News

Gold Market on Currency Swap Day: Price Fluctuations Based on Forward Premium

Despite Midday Rumors of Currency Swap or Lower Prices Leading to Rises, Forward Premium Gradually Increased, Resulting in a Final Drop of Two and a Half Yuan

Yesterday, the gold market experienced a currency swap day, with many major players remaining on the sidelines. However, due to prior speculation that the forward premium might reach six or seven yuan, there was a temporary rebound midday. Unexpectedly, after trading commenced, the premium gradually increased, eventually leading to a decline. In the morning, overseas silver markets showed stability in both London and New York. The forward silver price in Montreux rose by 3.7% and contracted by varying degrees. Exchange rates slightly narrowed. London spot gold fell by 1.5 pence. The Central Bank's official exchange rate announcement showed no change in British or American currencies, and the customs gold unit remained unchanged. The standard gold price was listed at 1,149.6 yuan, but market sentiment remained calm. The morning opened with lower prices, and after the opening, major players took advantage of the low prices to purchase, driving prices up. However, banks took the opportunity to sell at higher prices, making further increases difficult. Mobil was locking in near-term U.S. dollars, anticipating the HSBC exchange rate, which showed a stable British pound and a slightly contracted U.S. dollar at 0.0625. At this point, fluctuations were minimal, with supply and demand in balance. Banks' appetite remained sluggish, and forward prices slightly hardened but then declined slightly. However, due to rumors that this currency swap would at most involve the short side paying a premium of six or seven yuan, market sentiment improved, stimulating buying interest. Mobil continued to lock in U.S. dollars, gradually tightening the near-term market and driving prices up. However, major players gradually supplied at higher prices, and soon the market gradually declined. Predictions indicated no change in Indian silver. At noon, the overall trend was stable. In the afternoon, due to the rising forward premium for currency swaps, the market shifted from stable to weak. Although there was a slight rebound after the opening, the increasingly high forward premium gradually became unsustainable. When the currency swap officially opened, rising to a premium of 12.8 yuan for the short side, selling pressure intensified, breaking the 40 yuan barrier. Buyers maintained support by buying at lower prices. After the currency swap opened, prices fell back, returning to the previous levels. However, prices consistently failed to break above 42 yuan. In the end, the currency swap once again aided the short side, leading to renewed weakness. The future trend remains one of consolidation. As for this currency swap, predictions beforehand were varied. During the preliminary trading in the afternoon, the initial bids were for the long side to pay a premium of seven or eight yuan, but there were few takers. When the official trading opened, the premium surprisingly rose to 12.8 yuan, equivalent to a monthly interest rate of over 1.1%, attracting investment from major players and retreating to 11.3 yuan. However, the short side had a considerable amount of spot goods, making it difficult for buyers to avoid crowding, and the premium eventually increased to over 13 yuan. The day's market conditions are recorded below:

The morning opening was 1,141.3 yuan, down 1.3 yuan from the previous closing. It then became one yuan. Hengyu, Huixiang, Fuxing, Yongyuanmao, Yongtongchun, Changri, and Chunlaijin rose to 2.8 yuan. Dadecheng and Deli sold, falling to 2.1 yuan. Dadecheng then rose again to 2.8 yuan. Maijia Li bought January U.S. dollars at 0.0625. Huixiang and Hengyu sold to 2.1 yuan. Mobil bought November U.S. dollars at half a yuan, anticipating the HSBC exchange rate, which showed a stable British pound and a slightly contracted U.S. dollar at 0.0625. The situation was calm. Dachangxiang, Dadecheng, Huixiang, and Laijin rose to 2.8 yuan. Youli sold January U.S. dollars at 0.125. Dadecheng, Hengyu, Huixiang, Yicheng, and Fuyu divested, falling to 1.8 yuan. Dadecheng, Yuanyingfeng, Hengyicheng, Richang, Fuxing, Yongrichang, Fuyu, Qianchangxiang, and Luxu successively purchased, rising to 5.4 yuan, mainly because Liang Yiwei said the forward premium for currency swaps would at most be six or seven yuan, and a certain bank was also purchasing. Yingxiang and Fuxing Yongzhentai took the opportunity to sell, falling to 3.6 yuan. Dingkang, Huixiang, Qianchangxiang, and Laijin rose again to 5.5 yuan. New Stocks Reach Highest Price in Four Years

According to a report from Xinhua Foreign Company, yesterday (14th), New York stocks rose to their highest price in the past four years. Commerce Secretary Zabpan stated that former President Roosevelt and Howard wrote in a letter that the reform process was complete, and that the President must act in accordance with his words, in other words, that industry and commerce need no longer be afraid. The activity of trading was unprecedented since February 7, 1934. At the opening, there were frequent transactions of 10,000 shares per transaction. The teletype machine was lagging behind by as much as five minutes. Steel stocks were the strongest, with U.S. Steel, Bethlehem Steel, and National Steel all creating new highs for 1935. Railroad stocks also rose. The local securities company announced the issuance of a dividend of 0.2 yuan, which was the first time since 1931. Union Pacific Railroad announced that it would issue the usual quarterly dividend of 1.5 yuan. Both of these contributed significantly to the rise in railroad stocks. Automobile stocks and entertainment stocks were actively bought. In the end, there was a slight pullback due to the emergence of more profit-taking. Small exchange stocks and the bond market also rose. The total transaction volume for the day was 3.95 million shares.

Yarn and Cotton: Estimated Drastic Reduction in Cotton Production, Cotton Market Feels Increasingly Firm, Ultimately Diverging from the Yarn Market

The cotton market is very firm, which is inversely proportional to the yarn market. As American cotton rises, Indian cotton also steps in its footprints. The estimated price of foreign cotton continues to increase. Because of this, Japanese companies are constantly buying Chinese cotton. The market price is being drawn tighter and tighter. Banks are buying. Not only are they not selling, but they are also buying more when prices drop. The long side is gaining a lot, and they are not letting go.

Zheng Biao Opens Another High

The opening market for bid cotton shows a very tight trend. Since the rise in the American cotton market is intensifying, with the spot price already outside the 0.12 yuan level, and there are constant export transactions for appointment cotton, market sentiment is relatively boosted. The prices for all months open higher across the board, which is inversely proportional to the yarn market. The prices rebounded slightly during the second session, but they went back up at the closing. As a result, the prices for all months rose by 0.35-0.5 yuan compared to the closing prices from the previous day. Although there were large-scale sales from Jinzi Bang and Dafu, Yuanyi, and Gengfeng during the afternoon opening, Meiji and banks bought everything. The market relies on their support. Moreover, the second release from the Chinese Cotton Industry Statistics Association estimated the total cotton production for the entire country at 8,391,018 bales, which is a large decrease of 1,205,666 bales compared to the previous estimate of 9,596,684 dan. The market did not know about this news at the closing, but it is also beneficial for the long side. As a result, the price for each month fell by 0.05-0.2 yuan compared to the afternoon closing price. The selling in this month increased by 0.05 yuan.

Heavy Pressure in the Yarn Market

The yarn market, after an initial rise, has continued to fall, and the situation is unusually stagnant. This is because the pressure from the environment is increasing, and people are in a state of unease and uncertainty. At the same time, spot yarn sales are sluggish, and the various guilds are extremely unmotivated to buy. Recently, securities have declined, buying sentiment has been further dampened, and the cotton market is quite expensive, increasing the factory's cost calculations. Therefore, some parties have adopted a strategy of buying on dips, but in reality, there is a lack of demand for spot yarn, making it difficult to raise market prices.

Second Estimate of This Year's Cotton Production

The China Cotton Industry Statistics Association announced the second estimate of national cotton production for the 24th year at 5:00 PM on November 15, 1935, as follows:

Cotton Field Area 35,485,818 mu

Abandoned Field Area 12,291,200 mu

Ginned Cotton Production 8,391,018 dan

The above estimates (1) are based on reports from twelve provinces, including Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, Shaanxi, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Sichuan (Sichuan is a newly added province this year; previous years did not include Sichuan), and the two cities of Shanghai and Tianjin; (2) are based on the cotton crop situation before November 10; (3) include all losses from disasters suffered by the cotton crop in each province before November 10; (4) cotton fields are measured in mu (60 square zhang per mu), and cotton production is measured in dan (100 jin per dan).

The association's second estimate for this year is compared with historical cotton field production and estimates published annually for the past two years below:

1934

First Estimate 44,441,047 11,497,924

Second Estimate 44,807,579 11,172,554

Final Revision 44,971,264 11,201,999

1935

First Estimate 36,320,768 9,596,684

Second Estimate 35,485,818 8,391,018

The national cotton crop this year, following the progress of the 10th year, still showed a trend of increasing cotton fields in various provinces at the beginning of planting. However, during the sowing season, the Yellow River basin, such as Shandong, Henan, and Hebei provinces, experienced severe drought, resulting in many abandoned fields where sowing was not possible, germination failed, or seedlings did not grow. The Yangtze River basin, on the other hand, was relatively good. Around the time of flowering, the drought in Shandong and Henan provinces began to ease, but Hubei province suddenly reported flooding, and a large area of cotton-growing regions was submerged, resulting in abandoned fields. According to this estimate, the number of abandoned fields nationwide this year reached as high as 12,291,300 mu, the highest record in cotton production statistics. The cotton crop situation, according to the first estimate, was good in various provinces in winter, and even in disaster-stricken areas, recovery after the disaster was fast. Therefore, although there was significant damage to fields due to disasters, it was still possible to produce more than 9,596,000 dan of cotton, with an average yield of 26.6 jin per mu. After the first estimate, Shandong and Henan provinces, which were the most severely affected by the drought in the Yellow River basin, showed some improvement due to favorable weather during the boll-forming period, and production increased compared to the first estimate. Hebei remained unchanged, but Shanxi and Shaanxi saw reduced production due to continuous rain. The Yangtze River basin mostly saw a decrease, especially in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. The typhoons that have historically had the greatest impact on cotton harvests in Jiangsu and Zhejiang after autumn were fortunately avoided this year, but continuous rain and widespread pests caused the cotton production, which had shown promise of a good harvest in the first estimate, to decline sharply. The national cotton production also decreased as a result, falling to 8,391,018 dan, a decrease of 11.6 percent compared to the first estimate, and the average yield also decreased to 23.6 jin per mu.

American Cotton Spot Price Up 2 Points

Yesterday, at the opening of the American cotton market, trading was active, and prices for each month rose by two to six points. According to predictions, the 12-cent loan will be extended to after January 2nd. The government's attitude is said to be firmer than before. At the same time, stocks were strong, and news from Liverpool was good. Unfavorable forecasts for the West, along with consistent buying by fellow brokers and foreign firms, caused market prices to rise gradually. There was strong hedging at the opening, but it disappeared later, further intensifying buying sentiment. As a result, spot prices rose by 20 points, and futures prices rose by 21 to 23 points. English cotton spot prices fell by four points, and futures prices rose by 11 to 12 points. Indian cotton trading was light, with speculators buying and a few European exporters selling. Pingle remained unchanged, Omra fell by half a rupee, and Bai Luo Creek fell by 0.25 rupees, according to the original telegram (dated 14th).

Many Rumors in the Grain Market, Flour and Wheat Affected

Yesterday, at the opening of the flour market in the morning, prices for each month once saw a rebound due to the rising prices of foreign wheat by five or six jiao. As the ordering of foreign wheat has not materialized, buying sentiment remained active both inside and outside the industry. Prices for each month rose by two to three fen at the opening. Later, due to rumors about the situation, bulls adopted a wait-and-see attitude, and there was a surge of floating short positions, causing prices to fall back by one fen. At the opening in the afternoon, prices initially remained flat, but then, due to very quiet departures from the market, with a transaction volume of only over 200,000 in half a day, outsiders continued to buy in due to the uncertainty of foreign wheat. Although near-term prices were flat, far-term prices rose by more than three fen. It is observed that subsequent movements may also be related to the future of the situation.
